¶ chronicle ihon hardyng metre frō firſt begynnyng englāde vnto yt reigne edwarde ye fourth made end chronicle yt tyme added cōtinuacion ſtorie proſe tyme firſt emprinted gathered one diuerſe ſoundrie autours moſte certain knowelage ſubſtanciall credit yt either latin el mother toungue haue writen ye affaire englande ❧ londini ❧ officina richardi graftoni menſe ianuarii 1543 cum priuilegio ad imprimendum ſolum rg printer publisher device ¶ dedicacion preſent woorke vnto right honorable lorde thomas duke norffolke thenprynter richard grafton lorde thomas norffolke duke moſte gracious noble aunceſtrie blood deſcended captain right woorthie auenturous frō scotlād euen newely retended wher englandes querele ye haue reuenged behalf noble kyng henry wyſhe health honour victorie ¶ becauſe hath pleaſed almightie god right title quercle englande vſe ſtocke iron rod wherewith ſcourge falſehood scotland truthe ne holde bande ihon hardynges chronicle thought moſte mete bee dedicated grace ¶ hardyng true herted englyſheman eſquier valiaunt hardie bolde vnlearned time serched chronicle bothe late olde euer theſame hath bee told frō begynnyng scotlāde dooeth reigne vnder kynges englande ſoueram ¶ hardynges owne ſelf hath partie bee scotlande oft tymes hath brought ſeales homage fealtee vnto kyng englande ought vnto scottes ſued ſought yeldyng liue humble ſubieccion englandes gouernaunce proteccion ¶ people propre nature hath euen firſt ſo vntowarde vnſtedfaſt inconſtaunte vnſure nothyng maie poſſibly bee frowarde haue thei continued then foorthwarde neuer gladde bee quiet reſt defeccion aye readie preſt ¶ wherefore thon hardyng lorde maiſter tyme ſerued without blame edwarde firſt duke yorke kyng realme fourthe name chronicle affermeth theſame thei rebell till prouiſion kyng englād ſhall haue made theim ¶ deede englād hath oft cōſtreigned one scottes ſlackeneſſe dooyng homage pricke forewarde whē thei would haue refreined yt ſharpe ſpurre marciall forceage abate wantonneſſe courage iron rodde due correccion oft thei attempted defeccion ¶ ye scottes aye bee boſtyng crakyng euer ſekyng cauſes rebellion spoyles booty preades euer takyng euer ſowyng quereles diſſenſion burne ſteale intencion yet people god dooeth hate curſe thei alwaies begynne euer haue woorſe ¶ englande hitherto hath neuer lacked power oft nede wer scottes compell duetie dooe menne honour englande hath ſtories dooe tell whiche whenſoeuer scottes rebell wer hable tymes theim ſubdue obedience england renue ¶ emōges ye whiche noumbre noble father twelfth yere henry ſeuenths reigne aunciente recorde gather beeyng ſuche credence cannot feigne yode scotlande pryde reſtrein ſēbleable power bookes dooen auowe like commiſſion grace ¶ ſeaſon ſo valiauntely scottes vanquiſhyng puttyng flight thei ranne awaye moſte ſhamefully hable hym tabide ſight hable ſuſtein brunt might soondrie caſtelles raced grounde whiche honour englande redound ¶ kyng iamy alſo makyng greate braggue vaūte hauyng armie myle daie father captain valyaunt made moment feare runne awaye scottiſh kyng ſēding foorth heraldes tway chalenged father wt many proude woorde battayle wage trye ſworde ¶ chooſe thou ſir earle ꝙ kyng iamy whether ſhall fight armie againſt armie orelles thou trye manne manne ſparyng bloodſhed either compaignie chaunce haue victorie nought ſhall demaunde englandes loſſe thine sauig barwike toune euer bee mine ¶ heraldes ſaied noble knight shewe kyng place purpoſely battayle wage tentes haue pight come flee fyght ſharpely ſtandeth maye ſee eye fyrſt would bloodſhed ſaued bee therof leſſe deſirous ¶ secundarily likyng poore earle meane eſtate maye combattre hym beyng kyng two fightes may ceaſſe debate dooeth honour ſuche highe rate muſt nedes graūt ſelfe bound caſe humble thankes rēdre grace ¶ towne barwike knowē lorde requireth caſe bee ſlaine kyng ſouereins mine owne graunte therof dodeth remain thys maie ye bear worde lord perſon lyfe aduenture ſhall precyous round worlde ¶ kyng iamy heraldes twoo spedefullye returnyng due knowlage muche otherwyſe loked thoo earles ſtout aunſwer meſſage fled hand would battayle wage father retourned home victour coumfort laude praiſe ioye honour ¶ ſame father fyfth yere mooſt noble kyng henry eyght hys grace armie turney ſame kyng iamy scotland ſtreyght agaynſt england banner dyſpleyght vanquiſhed scottes wt helpyng hād slew king iamy brought england ¶ agayne xv yere ſame reygne ſelfe proper perſonne full courageous set forth againſt ye scottes without dyſdeygne lyke captayne valyaunt venturous wher ye brēt iedworth toune right populous wyth diuers victory grace whiche made englande reioyſe glad ¶ yere folowyng alſo bookes teſtify scottes came houge power lx thouſande men vnder duke albany beſiegyng warke caſtel thynkyng deuour heryng grace dyd approch yt houe scottes trembled ſo dyd theyr duke cowardly fled ſhame rebuke ¶ sembleably thys laſt viage nowe thys laſt october nouember made scotlande great damage dooeth ſemeth ryght well appere pleaſeth king ſend thether houſe hys ryght appoynted god bee scottes ſharpe ſcourge rod wherfore thys chronycle ihon hardyng haue thought good dedycate grace becauſe ſame euery maner thyng doothe beſt ſet nature place diſtaunce tounes euery myles ſpace beſechyng grace take good parte myne honeſt labour beneuolent harte preface chronycle iohn hardyng emonges wryters haue put vre penne ſtyle thynges endite none haue behynd theim left ſo greate treaſure ne poſteritee haue dooen ſuche delite thei whiche haue taken peines write chronycles actes eche nacion haue theſame made true relacion ¶ chronycles knowe thynges auncient ſucceſſion tymes menne ſtate policy regiment howe long eche partie hath ruled procedynges chronicle make reporte matiers dooen paſſed many thouſand yeres gooen ¶ chronycles knowe eche countree men haue proweſſe marciall perſones chiefly actiuitee betwene warres haue befall either ciuile el externall howe theſame haue conueighed wrought el appeaced quiete brought ¶ chronicle dooe recorde teſtifye euen worldes firſt beginninges dooe kepe continuall memorie courſe proceſſe maner thinges liues maners prince kynges aſwell gentile iudaicall aſwell iuſte godly tyrannicall ¶ perſones prince countree haue louing true obedient time neceſſitee haue ſerued theſame good entent conſtauntly therin haue liues ſpent chronicle regeſtred feithfully immortall honoure glorye ¶ contrarye wiſe ſouerains countrees haue wicked traitours colluſion crafty traines haue rebelled againſt gouernours ſame helpe haue ſlacke proctours ſembleably ſette name endeleſſe infamy reproche ſhame ¶ theſe thinges others thouſande mo wherby realmes haue decaied growen chaunged proceſſe altered fro fruitefull expedient bee knowen chronicle ſo plainly ſhewen thinges antique v bee apparent yf doinges preſent ¶ wherfore goddes worde holy ſcripture whiche abandoneth maner vanitee yet chronicle admitteth lecture thing greate fruite vtilitee lanterne poſteritee example ought knowe way refuſe folowe ¶ bible bookes iudges kynges althoughe moſte full high diuine miſterie farre ſurmounting ethnike dooynges yet yf bee read take literally hath fourme courſe plain hiſtorie kynges ſerued god trangreſſed whiche thereby proſpered wer oppreſſed ¶ bookes kynges euery yf thinges ſeme touched ouer briefly larger ſtorye dooeth v referre whiche chronicle eche manne truely sette length memorie albeit thoſe chronicle euident loſte dooe remain preſent ¶ bookes inſcribed paralipomena perfecte membre piece bible ſummarye kynges iuda therfore hebrue hath title appellacion chronicle machabees alſo deming plaine hiſtorye holy writing ¶ whiche bookes neuer ſet greate maime knowlage lamentable lacke outen doubte greate cauſe blindneſſe age faith ineſtimable damage ſpirite god authour thoſe example might bee glaſſe ¶ chronicle therfore true reporte whether chriſtian realmes matier pleaſaunce fruite comforte thouſande cauſes mo diligently bee attended vnto yea maner writer ſame worthie laude thanke honoure immortal fame ¶ neither one bee reiected behalfe hath dooen endeuoure though ſome bee ſuch might bee corrected yet thoſe haue therein beſtowed laboure haue minded profyte v power neither ſo full ſomwhere dooeth faile ſo bare dooeth ſomthing auaile ¶ exceding benefite trowe ye eche manne haue cognicion actes bothe owne countree alſo euery forein nacion yf liued eche thing dooen view actes antiquitee though nowe preſentlye theim ſee ¶ chronicler therfore highly cōmende emonge others authour ihon harding power point contēd vttermoſt extent learning engliſhe men might haue vnderſtanding affaire touching theirowne countree euen dayes olde antiquites ¶ though cōning ſo muche ſome others intelligence yet good minde entent zele ſuche hym lacked pointe diligence ſuche bookes thought credence feithfully deſcribe ſuche thinges rime happened englande tyme tyme ¶ thinges dooen owne dayes foloweth authours auenture without choice difference true wayes well aſſured corrupte pure whether certaine orelles vnſure whether fabulous menne veritee whether vaine good authoritee ¶ ſoeuer owne time dooen reporteth fidelitee right ſo eche thing ended begonne withoute ſpotte inſynceritee diſſimulation veritee founde meanes veray trueth know knewe certainly ſhewe ¶ beginning henry ye fourth kyng realme englande conqueſt euen edwarde fourthes reigning whiche thre ſcore yeres one leſte leaueth nothing vnwriten largeſt ſemed bee importaunce touchyng peace warre wyth scotlande fraunce ¶ vnto scottes coulde neuer bee frende becauſe ſawe theim towardes england falſe begynnyng laſt ende neuer ſtandyng anye league ne bande homage fealtee ne wryting theyr hande neuer ſo readie make rebellyon thei promiſed mooſt ſubiection ¶ ihon hardyng bee trew man behalfe inſpyred prophecie thei wyll neuer bee thei falle england ſuttle craftie entendyng myſchiefe thei ſhewe contrary spoylers robber amende wyll neuer tyll kyng ſhall haue made theim englyſhe euer ¶ neither anye euer wrote mat • er scotland could better ſkill falſhoode vntrueth note affection better wyll better knew water woodde toune vale hyll feruente scottes perſue england knew woulde neuer true ¶ neyther anye chronicler euer eyther dooth largly declare euen brutus howe came paſſe kynges englande ſoueraines ouer scotlande oughte rule beare hymſelfe wytnes ſubiection homage vnder englandes protection ¶ thinges tymes ſuche though werke haue ſome ſpice blindneſſe yet authour blamed much popyſhe errour ſeaſon doubtleſſe worlde ouer go oppreſſe therfore ſuch thinges muſt good part take pardon faulte tymes ſake ¶ yet haue thought beſt autour ſet euen ſuche fourme hymſelfe dyd endite wer vnquod thyng yf ſhould go alter chaunge olde men haue wryte secondly v maye bee greate delyte blindneſſe thoſe tymes conſider whiche hathe pleaſed god v delyuer ¶ fynally darkeneſſe thoſe dayes ſee honoure kyng dooeth redound goddes helpe geuen hath bee popyſhe trumperye confounde thyng al trew engliſh hertes hath boūd inceſſauntly praye kyng henrye ye eyghte whoſe godly wiſedome hath made ſtreyghte aſmuch hardyng boke doth ende edward fourth whoſe ſeruaūt whome alſo booke dyd commende conſideryng alſo tyme ſpace beyng lx yeres coulde let paſſe many goodly ſtatutes decree battayles ſtories good leſe wherfore annexed theim continuacion begynning wyth edwarde fourth yt name edward fyfth kyng generation richard third immortal ſhame cruelly murdered ſtory ſayeth ſame plaged hys greate greuaunce authours wrote proſe reportyng truth without fraude gloſe ¶ right gentle reader thy parte ſhalbe good wyll zele payne labour entreprete take good parte gre geuing ſame ſuche good wordes fauour may enforce myne endeuour ſettyng forth mo werkes take hande thy ſolace honour englande ¶ proheme iohn hardynge chronycle moſte ſubſtance power myght age diſtilled debilitee yt time aged wight greate faute haue habilitee labour ſhuld haue wthold fro witte would haue ſome diligence ghooſt kepe ſynne inſolence ¶ werke great lōge bryng fyne doeth euer fro tyme tyme encreaſe long hath dooen afore chriſt dyd enclyne marie mother mayden without leaſe chronicle ſo men haue theim put preaſe meetre ſome alſo proſe latyn full wyſely dyd cloſe ¶ ſome frenche made intellecte men could latyn vnderſtande ſufficiently endited protecte ferre nowe take hande ſome lynes two theyr ryme ay bande though witte ſo curious ferre make glorious ¶ yet wyll vſe ſymple witte haue pleaſaunce conſolacion cur thoſe kynges therof choſe ¶ ſente hym alſo sepulture keyes reſygnyng wholy vnto hym ryght defende lande sarizenes ſicke therto might lande deſtroyed ſight soudyan great lamentacion goddes people chriſten conſolacion ¶ theſe title chronicle recorde ſeen good deliberacion many theim theſe full well accorde haue ſeen greate delectacion clerkes wrytten informacion olde feldes cornes freſhe grene grewe olde bookes cōmeth cunnyng newe old bookes cō meth newe knowledge ¶ wyll nowe ceaſe forth procede mater wher fyrſt beganne chronicle lande worthihed remembre balade entent pleaſe god man eke pleaſe good femynitie duke wyfe named cecely lady wife dame cecely ¶ latyn hath litell intellect vnderſtande great nobilytie like lande whiche ſhe electe tyme commyng like haue ſouerayntie vnder rule ſhulde feminitee whiche maye pleaſe ladyſhippe hert reioyſe inward gladſhippe ¶ well wote great intelligence latyn hath good inſpeccion pleaſed bee hie ſapieuce lady vnder proteccion heyre alſo maye rede theyr eleccion whiche may pleaſe nobilitee laboure would reioyſed bee ¶ alſo heyres ſucceſſours tyme commyng haue clere knowledge realme noble gouernours haue kept helpe baronage victorye bretain tongue full fyne chriſte lawe made hym enclyne gaue hym ſhelde ſiluer white croſſe endlong ouer twhart full perfect ¶ theſe armes vſed brytain cōmon ſigne eche māne knowe naciō frome enemy would nowe bee conſumed ¶ kyng maryus kepte yt realme lawe peace full rich proſperyte dyed ſo sarum buryed dowteles reigned ſixty yere three tribute payed full well roome citee chriſtes faith ſumwhat wall legion briton hole aſſembled made wall well wrought lyme ſtone seuer made turues ſoddes ſembled caſtelles ſtrong towres none eche myles ende agaynſtande foonyſe ſea ſea yet well ſeen dyuers place wonte ¶ legion home returned agayn britayn ſuffred great diſeaſe scottes pightes ther theim ful great payn syxe yere next whiche haue ſome eaſe kyng aldrye ſorowes apeaſe eſſer britayn ſent theim conſtantyne head alſo medecyne ¶ conſtantyn kyng aldries brother wife crowned royall diademe conſtā tyne reigned x yere cairceſter brytons could deuyſe hoſte royall hym ſeme gwayme malga chronicle exprieme scottes peightes vēged ouercam brytayne wrought afore full mykel ſhame ¶ thre ſonnes full fayre wife conſtance eldeſt ſonne wiſe wherfore life made hym monke ſo beſtiall gette life aboue celeſtiall ſecounde ſonne hight aurelius ſurname called ambroſius ¶ youngeſt ſonne hight vterpendragon theſe two wyſe young wer age vncle ſent direction nurture learne maner language whiche maye haue knowelage diſcrecion good ordinaunce rule haue realme gouernaunce ¶ conſtantyne reigned well x yere vpon daye garden went peight houſe hym full nere hym ſlewe anone treaſon conſent vortiger euer entent conſpyred haue regaltee greate britayn kyng ſo bee lxvi chapiter ¶ conſtaunce kyng britayne reigned one yere monke firſt made kyng wyſe ideote whome vortiger crowned entent make hymſelfe kyng falſe cōtryuyng ſeyng kyng full ſymple rule lande conſtaunce ſonne ye mōke cairgwente conſtaūce kyng vortiger duke weſtſex daye haſte crowned baron hole aſſente knowyng ſhulde foole alwaye realme ſaue kepe diſraye waged peightes hundreth ſerue yt kyng alwaye vpon body abydyng ¶ made kyng full certenly beleue thei ſhuld eſpie emong enemytee frendes yt peightes ſhuld hym greue ne scottes theyr greate peruerſitee thei afore certayntee shuld let hym witte malice vnderſtande ſubtyll meane fage kyng fande ¶ vnder payed theyr wage full well chere full good pleaſaunce vnto daye ſayd theyr knowlage kyng nomore would haue theyr attendaunce wer kyng ſhuld theim well auaunce whiche thyng euer came preefe ꝑſone ſhuld cheriſhed cheefe ¶ wage alſo full well ſhuld payde whiche beheſt anone ſlewe kyng brought head hym full foule arayde made hym wroth ſemyng london ſubtyll wrytynge gaue charge peightes kyll none eſcape nether good ne yll ¶ vortiger protectour yere handes kynges caſtels ſawe might crowne full clere haue wyll ſo dred lordes temperall prelate hie ſpirituall heuyneſſe indignacion aſſented coronacion ¶ whē cōſtaūce thus yt kyng one yere could nothyng rule ne gouernaunce common ſawe ideote clere theyr voyces gaue theyr obeiſaunce vortiger theyr hole attendaunce comons would euer yet olde newe eche yere kyng chaunge renewe lxvii chapiter ¶ howe vortiger kynge britayne reigned xviii yere falſhed treaſon cōſpired peightes ſlea kyng howe engiſt horſus paiens landed kent beloued vortiger howe wedniſdaye frydaye name goddes goddiſſes honoured howe engiſt horſus lāded kēte made thoncaſtre horne caſtre coū tre lyncolne howe engiſt ſent doughter maried kyng vortiger brought greate multitude paiens accombred realme warre chriſten fayth wherfore briton crowned kynges ſonne vortiger thē crowned kyng might vortiger kynge britayn reygned xviii yeres peightes scottes kyng ſo kylled ſclaundred hym mikell good hight vnto peightes kyng haue ſlayn ſpilled ſuche treaſon ſo fulfilled preuy ordinaunce made theſame ſlayne theſame chaunce ¶ whiche arooſe hym auēged ful great hoſte deſtroyed corn towne brent lande felly reuenged whiche tyme came region engiſt horſus duke great renoune ſort ſent voyde saxonye menne warre alſo germanye ¶ ſhyppes thre arryued ſo kent vortyger caunterbury laye whiche withhelde anon farre ſent warre scottes pyeghtes aye brent lande noyed day daye peynemis trowyd mercury venus theyr goddes payanie ¶ mercurie woden language called ſo propre name whome honoured olde age fourth daye euery weke hame wednyſdaye wherof named ſo mercury geuing name wodē called wedniſdaye olde cuſtome haue vſed alwaye ¶ venus alſo theyr hygh goddeſſe whome alwaye halowed ſixte daye euery weke prayer holyneſſe theyr tonge friday called alwaye whoſe honoure named frydaye sonne moone iubiter saturne mar god armes dyd adorne ¶ yere chriſtes incarnacyon foure hundreth full fourty ſyxe alſo engyſt regyon firſte came hauen wt thre ſhippes mo ſaynte bede ſayeth geſtis anglorum ſo ſcottes pieghtes faught ful mightely droue theim oute victorye ¶ engiſt none habitacyon deſyringe ſo caſtell dwell hym men kepe frome aduerſacyon scottes peyghtes yt enemyes fell olde chronyclers canne tell aſked much ground bulleis ſkyn thonge myght cyrcuyte fully brede longe ¶ whiche king graunted anone made thonge bully ſkyn ſmall longe rounde dyd gone ſtony grounde ſet caſtell thus ſubtelte ſleyghty gyn made thongcaſtre men tolde lyndeſey nowe caſtre wolde ¶ engyſt ſent doughter rowan came anone ſhyppes eyghtene well ſtuffed men britayne agayne scottes peightes opteyne whome vortiger thought ful longe ſene proferred drynke ſayde waſſayle learned ſayde drynke hayle ¶ wordes fyrſt came vp ſo land ſet herte loue wed kyndes lawfull bonde church could beſt hym learne moue thus saxon vortiger ſet aboue whiche ſonnes baronage hym hated ſore ryght maryage ¶ paynimes bloodde ydolatrye greate people turned peruerte greate alſo pilagien hereſye accombred hole aduerte wherfore ſonne people conuerte lupus ſent felowe germayne chriſten fayth preache britayne biſhoppes ii folke conuert againe proceſſe ſo home agayne went engyſt pleaſe kyng full fayne ſonne occa germany ſent ebiſſa cherdryk conſent vortiger iii c ſhyppes brought men warre beſt might ſought whiche ſonne hight vortimer fyrſte wyfe alſo baron ſuche multytude people affrayed kyng befall compleyned without helpe generall wherfore anone together dyd conſent vortymer crowne hole aſſent lxviii chapiter ¶ howe vortymer ſonne kynge vortyger kynge brytayne withſtande power engyſte saxon twyes crowned howe engyſt vnder treaty ſlewe baronage brytons yt playne salyſburye vortimer crowned anon ryght royalte might appende vortymer kynge britayne ful wiſe ap pued lyke knight courage knighthode extende aſſayle elles defende myſcreauntes faught ſore vpon de • went elles place went ¶ abirforth fought theim alſo better ay yede catigerne brother kylled tho horne alſo ſlayne greate manhode thus vortimer victorius ſo yede tyme vpon north ſea bankes faught batayle vnthankes ¶ fled vnto yſle tenecte theim ſyeged fearfully aſſayled ſlewe theym doune hepes ay met theyr power almoſte fayled forefoughten full ſore batayled beſought kyng myght haue lycence germany make reuertence ¶ wente home lytell folke alyfe tyme came agayne cytees church amended full ry fe chriſtentee mainteyne full fayn anone ſubtell quene rowayne made hym poyſoned whiche dyed venymes thus mortifyed ¶ pyller braſſe layde hyght gate saxon landed afore bad men alſo farre myght hym ſe truſte wolde nerre come thore neuertheleſſe letted therfore buryed hym troynouaunt cite • bade ſolempnite ¶ kyng vortiger crouned engeſt ſent bade hym come anone vortimer ſoonne deade ſlain wt three hūdred ſhippis full mēne echone brytain landed kyng ganne gone whome full glad well reioyſed folke greate power noiſed ¶ brytons alſo baronage fight hym aroſe whole conſent whiche ſent theim meſſage realme none eiuill ment helpe lande entent thei hooſt diſpleaſed thei could beſt deuiſe thei ſhould eaſed ¶ bad theim ſet daye wher thei might mete auiſe power home ſende hold common quiet fro enemy realme defende defaute auiſe tamende brytons thought profer reaſonable realme alſo full profitable ¶ thei ſent hym woorde mete firſt daye maye foure hundred ſo euery ſide vpon plain sarum meeke araye craft pollicye engiſt caire cradok called ſo tyde byſide awmeſbury full fair edefied whiche daye engiſt bad menne within hoſes long knif haue ¶ ſaied nemyth ſexes eche manne ſlee bryton knife ſo ſhall kyng held hym troynouaunt marred ſore greately agaſt ſo thei aſked anone theim graunt citees caſtels ſufficiaunt lette hym paſſe awaye without troublaunce whiche engiſt graunted becauſe aliaunce lxix chapiter ¶ howe engiſt cauſed logres bee called engeſtlande whiche common putte geſt awaye common ſpeache call • england ſhortenes ſpeache engiſt hooſt thorient south north ye greate britain kepyng except thoccident englāde wherof ſo named whiche brytons held warre muche pain olde chronicle haue herd ſaine anone called engeſtes lande whiche ſhorted called england ¶ cōmons yt thought long ſay muche lighter tongue ſaie englande mouth ouer long name aye long producyng call engiſtislande thus came firſt vnderſtande conceiue thus came firſt englandes name ſhort ſpeach corrupt per ſincopene ¶ engiſt gaue lande saxon kyng ſo kent vortiger cambre ſought buylde vpon caſtell entent holde hym fro panymes violent whiche cambre caſtell genoren made full ſtrong lande hergigyen ¶ vpon ryuer ewey cloarte hill dragon water vnder merlyn ſaied caſtell ſo ſpill ne birth many menne wounder werke bothe aboue vnder father ne prophecye cannot wryte ſuche affirmably ¶ notwithſtandyng philophiers wiſe affirme well ſprites ſuche bitwene moone therth called incubice haue gotten chyldren wemen vnſeene ſtories diuerſe haue ſo ſeen howe philoſophier wiſe magancius affirmeth alſo apuleyus lxx chapiter ¶ thy ſelf dooeth ſignifye beames twoo extendyng ſeuerally ¶ beame ſouthward fraūce yt dooeth extende thy ſoonne thou ſhalt haue dooeth ſignifie ſhall conquere fraunce vnto thend almaignie alſo germanie ſo roome throughout al romanie aboue prince tyme mooſt fained chriſtente mooſt dred beſt named ¶ beame irelande extendyng thy doughters eke dooeth alſo ſignifie child alſo theim ſhalbe lordes might ſepulture worſhip ſeen thus worthy kyng buryed dene reigned tyme thirten yere dedde laied ſo beere lxxi chapiter ¶ vter pendragō kyng brytain armes bare brother vter cairgwēt croūd howe kyng amoured duke gorloys wyfe gatte kyng arthure emonges gorloys duke cornewayle wife bring igrene fayre figure whoſe beautee others made faile well hole auiſed nature womanhede exceded euery vnto iordan maner conyſaunce moſte knewe duke preuytee whiche brought igrene three ¶ thus laye kyng hir euer whē would truſtyng hir lorde euer ſiege made ſadly holde people aſſautyng caſtell one accorde gerloys men pleynly recorde theyr lorde ſlayn vter felde ſhe merueyled faſt hym behelde ¶ gatte hir ſonne full fayre fro hir went vnto hooſte agayn duke ſlayne moſte repayre whiche kyng glad layne tyntagell hoſte full fayne came anone wyll comforted hir bad holde ſtyll ¶ betwene theim two diſcure priuetee wrought ſette daye wed hir cure heuynes ſhe brought lordes death ſo muche hir thought hir ſo ſlayne hir wyfehode alſo defouled afore tyme euer kept vnfouled ¶ daye wedded hir cround ſhe ferforth childe begonne comforte ſette table rounde wyncheſter worthieſt knightes alone approued beſt knighthode foone whiche table rounde ioſeph arimathie brether made ſeynt grall onely ¶ whiche made ſeege pereleous none ſhulde ſytte without great miſchiefe one ſhuld moſte religious knightes rounde table chiefe ſaynt graal ſhuld recouer acheue aduenture fortunitee death virgyne ſhulde bee ¶ hir tyme quene borne ſoonne arthure hight ſtatur fayre large lymme wyſeſt vnder ſunne age bee father heyre lymmes right comly ſtronge fayre occa oyſa afore stale home come warred britayn ſore ¶ kyng ſent forth ſyr loth lowthian worthy prince hardy bounteous doughter wedded yt hight thē great landed britayne colgrym came brent lande hye arthure kyng howell came full fayne hooſt great ſyſters ſonne certayne leſſe britayne vncle went againſt colgrym fyght entent ¶ cador duke tyme cornewayle kynges brother mother ſyde came kyng people yt might auayle dyd britayne full wyde enemy met mikell pryde vaynqueſhed theim lyncolne ſeging whiche fled full faſte yt ſyege leauing ¶ calidon wood nere vnto ſea kynges two theim ſeged ſore famiſhment fought ſwore kynges men lande throughoute voide people land colgrym baldolffe alſo duke cheldryk chieftayns wt dughty duke cordrik ¶ leyde hym hoſtage ſpede vpon ſea agayne landed eft totneſſe ſo dede ſeged bathe arthure full faine hoſtages honged ſyght ful plaine fought colgrym baldof ſlewe cordryk gaue weſtſex man trewe ¶ duke cador folowed vpon chace ſlewe cheldryk saxonie kyng agayne came caſe kyng beſeged albanye wherfore went hoſte full manly alclud scottes peightes laye theim diſcomfyted hym delyuered oute scottes peightes droue oute yſles scotland became men lyue peace euer full wyles gwillomare kyng irelande ouer kyng arthure full harde warre beganne hoſte full greate iryſhe saxonye scotlande brent alſo albanye ¶ yt kyng hym met hym faught diſcomfyted hym put hym flygt vnto irelande batayle ſore vnſaught scotlande lowthyan ryght kyng loth lowthian hight fyrſte knyghte ſo table rounde arthure true alſo lyegeman founde ¶ ſyſter anne vnto wyfe wed whome gate curteous knyght gawen dunbar caſtell lyfe ledde aguzell kyng tyme certayne albanye vryan murref playne kyng kyng arthure full trewe lyegeman aye chaunged newe ¶ kyng arthure wedded wyfe gwaynore faiereſte creature tyme accompted paſſyng birth natyſe iuly fayre ſhe fygure aungelyk womannyſhe nature ſo ferfurth mē thought ſelues wel eaſed beholde ſo well al folke ſhe pleaſed ¶ table rounde knightes honourable tyme voyde great defycience many actes marcyable diſpended warres violence wherfore kyng ſapience worthyeſt euery realme aboute table rounde ſent without doute ¶ thre kynges foreſayde scotlande two kynges alſo walys full chyualrous howell kyng leſſe briteyne lande duke cador cornewayle corageous worthy gawen gentyll amarous fel theyr rule wronges oppreſſe bodyes lawe myght redreſſe fayth yt church maydens widowes clene chyldren alſo tender age cōmon profyte euer ſuſtene agayne enchauntmentes body wage agayne whiche crafte ſo ſore ouer ſet arthure felde mordred fled wyncheſter night full faſt hym ſped ¶ kyng folowed faſt vpon chace fought agayn hym full ſore many prince lordes caſe ſlayn bothe ſydes euermore round table longe afore many worthy knightes ſpended arthures loue might amended ¶ rounde table wyncheſter beganne ended hangeth yet ſlayn ylke battayl knightes euer ſitte britayne borne ſaue launcelot yode quyte kyng folowed chaſe mordred fled cornwayle yt caſe lxxxiiii chapiter ¶ battayll camblayn arthure preuayled ſ • ewe mordred arthure deathes wounde howe arthure died buried blacke chapel glaſtenbury wher water yt called camblayne mordred abode wt mightie hoſte ſtronge arthur fought yt day hie diſdayne full oft alone euer met amonge arthure ſlewe mordred knyfe long calibourne called ſuche vertue whomſoeuer ſmote therwith ſlewe ¶ mordred gaue arthure death woūd whiche yode woundes medifie thyſle aualon ſtound gaue britayne full ſolitarie conſtantyne duke cader ſonne hye neuewe cader brother well knowen one mother ¶ kyng arthure aualon ſo died wher buried chapell fayre whiche nowe made fully edified death kyng arthure mynſter churche daye great repayre glaſtenbury nowe hath leyre called blacke chapell lady chronycles tell ¶ wher geryn erle charter abode beſyde toumbe whole deuocion whether launcelot delake came rode vpon chace trompette clarion geryn tolde hym ther vp downe howe arthure layde ſepulture whiche hym byde hight full ſure ¶ ſo abode together contemplacion preaſtes aboute toumbe alwaye prayer greate holy meditacion heare fleſhe repreſſyng night daye three dayes eche weke breade water aye faſted lyued great ſorowe penaūce ſoules helth goddes hye pleaſaunce ¶ whē quene gwaynour perceyued howe mordred fled awaye thryſe frō yorke yode leſt ſhe deceyued fote night mayden full wiſe carlion lyue goddes ſeruice mynſter ſaynt iuly nonnes prayer whole greate deuocions ¶ kyng arthure whō none cōdigne world ſo pereleſſe life ſoule god dyd reſigne yere chriſt chronicle expreſſe fyue hudreth two ſothefaſtneſſe fourtye alſo accompted hole clere endyng without lxxxv chapiter ¶ commendacion arthure conceipte maker booke fewe woordes alſo compleynte lamentacion ſayde maker death arthure reigned ſixe twenty yere moſte redoubted erth moſte famous worthieſt wyſeſt without pere hardyeſt man moſte coragious actes marciall moſte victorious hym neuer drope cowardiſe herte poynte couetyſe ¶ neuer prince giftes liberal landes geuyng ne meate ſo plenteous agayn fooen moſte imperiall owne ſubiectes moſte bounteous lyon felde moſte douteous houſe lambe mercy euer replete iudgement euer eguall diſcrete ¶ good lorde god ſuche treaſon vnrightes ſuffred thy deuyne omnipotente theim precience forſightes myght haue lette curſed violence mordredes pryde inſolence noble kyng forpaſſyng conqueroure deſtroye treaſon erroure ¶ fortune falſe executryſe weerdes euermore ſo thy ſubtilitee debate thou ſtrongly ſo enherdes men euer would lyue charitee thou doeſt perturbe mutabilitee ſtretcheſt thou ſo thy whele vpon mordred agayne eme ſo cruel dede ¶ wherthrough high noble conqueroure without cauſe ſhuld algates peryſhed bee ſo many kynges prince honour worlde might none better bee fals falla mordredes propertee howe might yu ſo gwynoure haue ſuch might ſhe death cauſed ſo many knightes ¶ falſe beautie gwaynour predeſtinate vnhappe made falſe thy lorde good prince ſo fortunate neuer yet ſeen men recorde whiche betwene made ſo greate diſcorde prince wer ſlayne thy chaungeable hert venge ſo fayne ¶ mordred tofore ſo good knight greate manhode proudly aye approued thyne eme nobleſt prince might put truſt ſo greately loued vnhappe thy manly ghoſt hath moued vnto ſo foule cruell hardyneſſe many ſlayn thyn vnhappynes ¶ highneſſe thyne honoure fall thou began iniurie great falſhode thy proweſſe appall ſoone entred periurie conſequens treaſon traitourie thy lorde eme alſo thy kyng ſouerayn betraye thy felowes eke certayne lxxxvi chapter ¶ conſtantyne kynge britayne ſonne duke cador cornewayle reygned foure yere conſtantine brother ſōne crowned duke cador ſōne cornwaile boūteous afore one table rounde arthures tyme knight ful auenturous trone royall ſet full precyous diademe hed ſygnifyed troynouaunt wight replyed ¶ anone saxon ſore fight alſo mordred ſonnes two capitaynes put theim flyght one fled wyncheſter hyd hym ſo london mykyll woo conſtātyne theim bothe church ſlew autres hyd mewe ¶ conſtantyne ſet lande peace reygned well foure yere greate nobleſſe dyed buryed caroll leſſe beſyde vterpendragon full expreſſe arthures father greate worthyneſſe whiche called ſtone hengles certayne beſyde salyſbury vpon playne ¶ aurelius conan coſyn fayre aurelius conan kīg britayne reygned thre yere ſea royall helde ganne ſuccede hym nexte bloude heyre vncle ſonnes two dede pryſone ſlewe crowne hym ſelfe rede ſhould haue kynges britayne afore hym ſo yf ſlayne ¶ maynteyned aye ciuyle warre debate bytwene cytees caſtelles countees al realme wt myſruled mē aſſociate whiche greatly agaynſt royaltees thre yere reygned dignitees god ſo wolde hye ordynaunce wronge lawes maketh ſhorte gouernaunce ¶ vortyper ſucceded hym crowned royalte vortiper king britayne reygned vii yere agaynſte whome saxon ſtronge grym made full greate warre deſtroyed comente batayle greate humanyte ouercame ſet lande peace vnto tyme death made deceaſe ¶ seuen yere reigned people pleaſed tender comynalte aboue thyng ſawe eaſed publyke cauſe afore ſyngulerte preſerued alſo ryght ſhould cōmons fyrſt prynces ſupportacion ſet nought waſte dominacion ¶ malgo nexte hym crowne attayned feyreſt euer daye malgo kīg britayn reygned xxii yere tyranny fully reſtreyned conquered holy thryſe orkenay irelonde denmarke iſelonde eke norway gotlande alſo obeyed royalte ſo wyſe full fortunyte within realme none ſo large ne ſtrong ne none feacte warre ſo wiſe ſwerde axe fyght thronge ſpeare ſuche exercyſe aſſayle hys fooes ſuppryſe defence alſo great keenyng prynce euer kyng ¶ one defaute greate offence sodome ſynne wolde amende haunted euer withoute defence whiche greued god brought hym end two twenty yere dyd appende lande helde peace vnyte without ſuppryſe enmytee ¶ carreys crowned kyng anone loued well cytees debate carreys kīg britayne reygned thre yere betwene townes citees euery chone ſuche wyſe maynteyned early late imagened wyll preordinate muche warre cytees countrees full comen malicyouſneſſe ¶ briton made hym full mykel war saxon alſo vnto kyng gurmound ſent affrycans irelande fleete perfourme entent britayne came theyr hole aſſent saxon full accorde briton alſo ciuyle diſcorde lxxxvii chapiter ¶ howe gurmounde kynge affrycans conquered brytayne departed ſeuen kyngdomes saxon 〈◊〉 englyſhe went wynne moo landes made gurmonde cheſter g ʋrmoūde yt mighty cōquerour king affricās moſt dred euery lond helpe britōs theyr great ſocour engliſhe saxon made thē bonde dwelled tyme northumberlande place britayne vnder truage roſe hym whole agayne yt kynges outrage ¶ fought put hym yt flight circeſtre went ſtrongly helde towne kyng gurmound yt towne ſeeged right gate ſo myght greate renowne wherfore fled wale proteccyon came myne authour nought exp̄ſſed death trowe oppreſſed ¶ gurmound britaine hole deſtroied bothe churche towne eke chriſten faith paynym ſore anoyded chryſtentye gyldas wrote ſeyth logres yt whole loſt wt paynī leyeth prelate curate religyous reliques fledde awaye full dolorous ¶ hid hilles woodes caues tharchbiſhops one london tadyok yorke fled fro knauis ſainctes bone wildernes faſt ranne hid hym gurmond ſore banne croſſe bell greate candill light curſyng thei curſed hym ferre church might ¶ kyng gurmōd gaue northūberland frome trent north yt hight berun deyre northfolke southfolke cābrydge ſhire hāde whiche eſtāgle bede calleth ſtorie fro trent themis memorye mers called engliſh gaue dwelled ther euer reioyſe haue ¶ gaue theſe engliſhe menne deede whiche came lande hight angulo germany woodes rede repleniſhed wild beſtes buck doo sith tyme hether hathe yet ſo wherfore thei called engliſhemenne logres northumberlande anglande ¶ gaue suſſex saxon eſſex midelſed surry whole kent hamſhire barkeſhire toures townes shropſhire whole glouceſter thē apēt theſe called weſtſex bede ment thus dalt lande theim therin dwellyng whiche long afore paied truage kyng ¶ thē went home fraūce diſtroied many landes region brytons yt weſt party ſore anoyed droue theim logres religion liue peace dred rebelions carreis fled thei kyng tyme cadwan made choſyng ¶ ſtode thei kyngles twenty yere howe yt briton kyn gleſſe xx yere fro yere chriſt fiue hundred four ſcore therto three clerly dooeth apere ʋnto yere chriſt bore sixe hundreth three without cadwan brytons kyng elect crouned rule theim protect ¶ kyng carreis vnhappieſt creature lamen tacion yt maker booke yt lordes brytain reigned euer afore infortune made flee thy cure cauſed maintene ſo euermore eyuile diſcord within thy realme ſo ſore might haue reigned ouer many lande whiche thyne owne loſt vnderſtād ¶ thou vnderſtandeſt full litill theuangilye euery realme within ſelfe deuide shall deſolate bee made clerkes tell mat▪ xii euery hous ſhall fall ſlyde thy wycked nowe knowen wyde ſuffred ſo debate bytwyne lorde lorde bytwyne citees landes cyuyle diſcord ¶ cauſe thy diſheriteſon thy realmes deſolacion lawe peaceble conſtitucion might haue ſaued greate conſolacion churche preſerued greate proſperacion chriſten faith thy lande diſtroyed peace ſhuld haue kept vnnoyed ¶ woful carreis thyne heires thy brytons child widdowes wife commonalte citees townes churche alſo may bāne full ſore thoſe ſtriues thy ſupporte reſt ſo many liues wher lawe peace thou well conſerued ſaued thanke god deſerued ¶ defaute lawe cauſe miſchiefes wronges ſuſtened maiſtry might peace layed downe ſhould haue chief whiche debate folowed vnright wherfore vnto prince accordeth right kepe peace al tranquillite within realme ſaue royalte ¶ kyng without lawe peace within realme ſufficiently conſerued pooreſt realme maye ſo encreaſe iniury force bee preferred till kyng ſtrength haue ouerterued ſette hym ſelf royall maieſte bee ſuche ieopardie ¶ ye lordes prince high aſtate coū cel maker duke richard yorke kepe well lawe peace gouernaunce leſt ſubiectes defoule depreciate whiche able wrongfull gouernaūce reigne ye haue greate puyſaunce peace lawe voyed vnytee floures loſt ſouerentee ¶ worthy prince duke yorke meane diſcendid downe higheſt bloodde royall se ſuche ryotes none ſuſtene ſpecially alyens none inhabite power greate ne ſmall maye lande ought trouble ouer ride twies ſo wonne muche pride ¶ vortiger engiſt horſus whome receiued whiche hym diſtroyed helpe full falſe noyous worthy bloodde brytain ſore anoyed caroll murdred accloyed nowe carreis exiled kyng gurmōd saxon hym beguiled ¶ saxon peightes engliſhemenne reigned logres lande deuided ſeuen realmes fully weſtſer suſſex kente vnderſtande eſtſer mers eſtangle northumberlande droue brytons weſt countre walis cornwaile fro towne citee lxxxviii chapiter ¶ ethelbert kyng saxon hils ethelberte reignyng kyng kēt w sainct auſtin ſēt gregory r biſſhop landed tenet clerkes aſſēt many monkes teache faith hope clothed echeone vnder ablacke cope whiche proceſſion croſſe belle came latinies ſyngyng ieſus name ¶ yere chriſt incarnacion fiue hundreth foure ſcore ſixtene kyng ethelbert dominacion kent throughout greate ioy ſeen baptized holy water clene whome gregory ſent mellito iuſto clerkes doctours many mo ¶ gregory hym made archebiſhop caūterbury englande hieſt primate paule hyeſt legacye gregorye ſent hym ordinate fro london thus tyme tranſlate caunterbury ſea metropolitan london ſette ſuffrigan ¶ saynt auguſtyne wt helpe ethelbert saynt auguſtyns made chriſtes churche alſo chriſtes churche hight aduerte ſacred ſo hym halowed tho chiefe ſea metropolitan ſo englande gregory ordinate ſaynt auguſtyne englande primate ¶ auguſtyne made peter clerke deuoute ſaynt auguſtynes thabbot religious made mellito bede clerly hath note london byſhoppe full vertuous clarke beneuolus conuerted eſſex kyng sebert lande baptized holy herte ¶ kyng ethelbert ſainct poules edefied kyng sebert weſtminſter founded mellito theim halowed edefied auſtyn made clerke full wel grounded iuſt hight rocheſter full well bounded biſhop preache helpe auſtyn baptiſe folke doctrine ¶ saint auſtyn ſet ful nere walis ſeant prelate biſhops doctours wiſe brytons bloodde thither might well atteine make reſt loue humble wiſe yt churche lande good auice whiche ſean came tharchbiſhop brytain biſhops fiue doctours wiſe certain ¶ whiche auſtyn ſyttyng preſident archbiſhop alſo high primate required prayed whole entent england high prelate gregory ſacred ordinate fraterne loue due obedience helpe hym furth diligence ¶ conuerte teache saxon engliſhe alſo chriſten feith trewe baptize theim brytain ouer paſche kepe roome full dewe whiche brytons aunſwered yt knewe ſuche eſtate britayn three archebyſhops obeyn ¶ cairlyon london yorke citee byſhops rome graūted v ordinate full long afore ye ſuche dignitee wherfore obeye newe primate ſpecially none englyſhe newe prelate englyſhemen saxon haue v noyed haue lande kyn deſtroyed ¶ paſche wyll holde forth afore holy father vnto daye haue vſed wyll chaunge youre doctrine ne lore ſhall newe emong v abuſed ſaynt iohn haue refuſed chriſtes bozome ſaw great priuetees vſe none ſolempnitees ¶ auſtyne ſaied ſith ye nowe thus forſake ſeed god ſowe doctryne chriſten fayth encreaſe make ryghtfull dome god ye muſte enclyne vnder theyr handes fro fayth declyne cruel death ſuffer hie vengeaunce sith ye refuſe chriſtes wyll ordinaunce ¶ tyme eche kyng warred others lande ſeuen kynges saxones nacion englyſhe peightes vnderſtand briton alſo great aduerſacion ethelfryde englyſhe gouernacion northumberlande kyng panyme cruell fought aydan kyng scottes fell lxxxix chapiter ¶ howe kynge ethelfryde northumberlande ſeruyce aydan kyng scottes yere chriſt vi hundreth three ſaynt bede degfaſtan wher ethelfryde preuayled ſette aydan ſubiection bede dayes ye scottes nomore aſſayled homage scottes englande aye obeyed ediccion man without contradiccion held hym lande accorde many yeres then forth nomore diſcorde ¶ battayl chriſtes incarnacion syxe hundreth yere three ſayth ſaynt bede reygne bede computacion eleuenth yere rede twenty yere iiii reygned dede tyme peightes obeyed iryſhe alſo nomore hym diſobeyed ¶ ſame yere chriſtes incarnacion briton ſette theyr parliamente cairlion good informacion cairlegeoceſtre hight ſome men ment weſtcheſter become entente choſe cadwan vnto kyng theim defende fro theyr fooes warryng xc chapiter ¶ cadwan kynge britayne firſte prince northwales cadwan crowned yere chriſt ſyxe hundreth thre bede xiii yere reigned ouer briton weſt party wale cornwayll kyng cadwan wyncheſter crownd made ye kyng britayne brytōs agayn kyng ethelfrede yt ſtound warred full ſore region brytons ſo religion weſtcheſter ſieged violence wher brochewall therle made greate defence ¶ ſlewe brochewall batayll gatte towne weſtcheſter tyde xii c monkes without fayle murder mōkes ſlewe downe right lytle beſyde came praye peace without pride fro banger hole proceſſion marters wer oppreſſion ¶ whō kyng cadwan wt mighty hoſte ſtrōge met felde full ready fight theyr frendes treated ſo theim emong good accorde betwene thē made righte duryng theyr lyues well kepte hight frendſhippe great loue vnytee theyr realmes ſtoode great dignitee ¶ ethelfrides wyfe chylde farre gone violently exiled repudiate wedded another full wrongfully anone wherfore ſhe went recouer eſtate kyng cadwan full ſycke deſolate receyued noble reuerence ſory wofull offence ¶ thē wife great gone wt childe whiche kept hir houſe abyde tyme might hym haue reconſyled receyue ſet ſyde meane tyme might lēger abide queenes delyuered wer ſonnes two one edwyn hight cadwallo ¶ chylder two together noryſhed tender age tyme men whiche tyme roſe full cruell warre betwene redwald kyng eſtangle ethelfride fought folke kenne wher ethelfryde idell downe ſlayne redwald feld ther payn ¶ kyng cadwan worlde ſo died theſame yere ſo dyd auſtyne alſo laurens made fully glorifyed archebyſhop caunterbury tho ethelbert kent heauen dyd go thus chaunged theyr habitacion payne ſome ſaluacion ¶ cadwall ſonne kyng cadwan cadwall lxi yeres reigned father reigned xiii yere crowned weſtcheſter man briton clerely dyd appeare yere chriſt vi c xvi cleare reygned well full ſyxtye yere one aboue kynges ſouerayne echeone ¶ kyng edwyn northumberlande ſonne heyre vnto kyng ethelfryde crowned kyng yorke vnderſtande whiche kyng cadwall hym defyed made hym warre briton fortifyed ſente hym worde crowne elles ſhould vnder hed ſhere edwyn accompted ryght nought kepte eſtate full royall condigne crowne gold yorke ful freſhly wrought elfrydes ſonnes wronge wyfe vndigne goten borne felly dyd repugne hym dyd exyle scotlande dyd abyde mother exyled ethelfryde ¶ ethelfryde hym gate wrong wyfe exyled owne wyfe truely wed edwyns mother knowen full ryfe full great wt chylde hym bede hath red made welles dyuerſe countrees ſpred hye wayes cuppes copper clene trauelyng folke faſte chayned ſene ¶ euery daye rode withouten reſte trompettes lowde afore rode euery wyght myght ſuerly hym truſte wolde ryghtwyſhode euery man ryght without abode complayntes lawe wolde reforme lyfe rule confirme ¶ ſente vnto ethilbalde kyng kent ſyſter haue wed wyfe dame ethelburge full fayre gent ethelbalde ſent hym worde lyfe good lykely make ſtryfe chriſtē woman paynim ſhuld wed elles ſayde meſſage ſped ¶ edwyne ſent meſſage ſo agayne wolde well ſhe kepte owne creaunce bade hym ſende chapelayne clerkes wyſe without varyaunce kepe fayth ſuraunce yf fayth better myne knowen wyll therto enclyne ¶ kyng ethelbald ſent paulyne ſacred byſhop yorke tyme iuſto archbyſhop full fyne caunterbury kepe true bapteme beleue none fethers lyme hereſye foule owne creaunce thus wedded yorke ſuraunce ¶ yere lorde vi hundreth xx tho fyue therto bede hath clerely writen yere vi hundreth twenty ſo ſyxe therto kyng edwyn weten weſtſex went batayle ſore ſmyten betwene hym byſhop quychelyne king kinigils ſonne weſtſex ſo fyne ¶ ſlewe manly quichelyne cauſe compaſſyd death afore pryuey wyſe coulde ymagyne put lande vnder trybute ſore kynygell kyng weſtſex thore became man helde hym lande byddyng ryde hym ſtande xci chapiter ¶ howe cadwall fled dryuen realme kynge edwyn helde ſubieccion baptyzed ſaynt pawlyn archbyſhop yorke kyng cadwallo brytons yere chryſte vi c eyghtene wronge councell edwyns region great warres made edwyn full kene faught hym full ſore ſene flyght hym droue felde britayne lande conquered ſo helde ¶ cadwallo fled vnto lytell britayne dwelled heuyneſſe payne dyuers yeres durſte come agayne ſubie • cion scottes power none myght yet obteyne britaynes durſte hym obeyne kyng edwyn hole dominacyon theim saxon scottyſhe naciō ¶ yere chryſte vi c xx vi edwyns doughter named eufled yorke borne whome men dyd complex maydens twelue take chryſtenhede lordes doughters wer great worthihed • whiche ſaynt paulyn archbyſhop dyd baptyſe yorke mynſter full holy wyſe ¶ yere chryſte vi c xx ſeuen chryſten lawe diſputed amonge lordes founde beſte wynne blyſſe heuen wherfore edwyn good hole concordes comons alſo lordes realme baptime toke goddes mē ſaint paulin archbiſhop ¶ ſame yere byſhoppe honorius paulyn ſent palle dignyte kyng edwin ylke paulins yorke mynſter made newe greate beaute comons full well ſo baptized northumberlande swale owſe trent ryuers countrees went ¶ thyrty dayes ſixe labored thus came lyncolne edwyn conuerted blecca bede ſayth v mayre cōmons doctryne lyndſey hole vnto fayth deuyne made mynſtre lincolne coſtage kyng edwyn alſo colage ¶ yere vi hundreth thyrty moo iuſto dyed whome honoure dyd ſuccede caunterbury archbiſhop made tho whome ſaint paulin wryten hath ſent bede dyd ſacre lyncolne ſo dede mynſter edwyn founde kynges colage named ylke ſtounde ¶ yere vi hundreth thyrty two kynge edwyne holy doctryne ſaynt felyx holye preſte tho preachyng holy archbyſhop paulyn chryſtes worde verteous diſcyplyne conuerted edordwolde eſtangle kyng realme felyx dwellyng chapiter ¶ howe cadwall penda ſlewe kyng edwyn reigned ouer brytons agayne bvt yere vi hundreth thyrty thre kyng cadwall britaine king penda merces great coū tre aſſembled ſtronge hoſtes fell kene northumberlande brent ſene ſlewe wyfe chylde olde yinge preſtes clerkes ſpared thyng church brente foule deſtroied whome edwyn met power might hatfelde towne herte full ſore anoyed redy ſo batayle doth tell rocheſter tyme befell saint paulyn vnto ſea tranſlate byſhop therof denominate ¶ kyng cadwall reygned full hole agayne britayne lande prynce without pere aboue englyſhe lorde ſouerayne ouer teachyng preachyng vertuous made hym biſhop northumberlande whoſe ſea chief holy iſſe lande ¶ ſame yere oſwold weſtſex rode chriſt loue prayer ſainct biryne wher thei kyng kynygill paynymhode baptized litill waye ſight kyng oſwold wedded beblam wife bee kyng kynygilles doughter full faire ſee hir gatte ſoonne hight cidilwold deyre reigned vnder father oſwold ¶ yere ſixe hundrith thyrty ſixe kyng penda ſleugh ordewold eſtanglande bataile ſtrong mighty gan vexe waſtid ſore hym euery lande tyraunt fell wher chriſten fonde ſleugh theim downe cruelly ouer ran sparyng nother wife childe ne manne ¶ kyng oſwold ſo mighty deede ouer scottes peightes brytaines iriſh weſtſex engliſh rede ouer logres saxon none ſo mighty aboue region flores bede hath wrytten thus whoſe wrytynges full vertuous ¶ meate ſitte vpon daye bamburgh palmer came gate aſked ſome good chriſt loue alwaye whome ſent diſhe ſyluer plate cauſe el aſtate poore manne refreſh comforte sainct bede hym thus clerely dooeth reporte ¶ holy manne within hermitage deſired ſore meditacion better maner age wer lande nacion whome ſaid reuelacion kyng oſwold holy life notwithſtandyng weddid wife xciiii chapiter ¶ howe hermite proued ſainct oſwold wife deſire biddyng ſainct oſwold wherfore came vnto kyng oſwold prayed hym might knowe life reuelacion hym told wherfore toke hym ryng life bade hym ſaye quene wife dooe hym nightes twoo three ſhe wonte home dooe ¶ token ſatte hir meate meate drynke would haue beſt water brede might none gette night ſhe leide hym reſt right hir ſelf ſo well hir ſelf ſhe treſt ought ſette dooe amiſſe water caſt fleſhe keele liſſe ¶ daye came full fain quene full ſoone toke leue vnto kyng went anone prayed hym faſt might paſſe home eue life would preue whiche holy one daye night life euer might ¶ cadwall kyng brytons ſent kyng penda warre kyng oſwold whome oſwold mette greate aſſemblemēd battaile ſtrong heuenfeld god would wher people fled people manyfold kyng cadwall penda anone bee trewe ¶ quene eufled kyng oſwys wife kyng edwyn doughter full goodneſſe oſwyns ſoule minſter hir life made tynmouth oſwy cauſeles hym ſo bee ſlain killed helpeles ſhe kyn oſwy oſwyn bede chronicle baron warre ciuyle diſcorde realmes kyng cadwaladre beyng impotent euery daye helde gouernaunce nether lawe ne peace wtin regiment wherfore briton dred none ordynaunce eche one toke great vengeaunce fro time forth eche countre warred euery cytee agaynſte marred ¶ thus defauee lawe peace conſerued cōmon profyte waſted deuoured percyall profyte ſped obſerued venus alſo cōmonly honoured lechery alſo many one dyed woode ſome raynage went ſome lytargie implyed ſome batayle mortifyed murther alſo amonge themſelues diſpent full many none lament defautes amēded correct biſhoppes fled preſtees yorke certayne wrongefully haue bene holde ſeyne ¶ good lorde take hede miſchieue howe cadwaladore kepyng lawe ne peace sufferyng debate cōmon warrys acheue fully reygne put hym nought preace lawe myght make ceaſe whiche fell ſo great diuiſyon put vnto deheryteſon ¶ alone nacyon deuolued theyr ryght expelled full fayne flee greate lamentacyon greate britayne excelled aūcetour afore lōg time dwelled knew foe mortal ſhuld occupy euermore without remedye ¶ payne moſt fell aboue payne man haue bene hye felycite fall downe infortune agayne myſerye fell aduerſyte howe maye man haue thyng contraye mat xii haue well woo begone incomperable bee paynes echone ¶ wherfore good lord peace euermore mainteine ryottes chaſtyce prouiſyon lawe vpholde ryghtfully ſuſtene ouer thyng ſe bee deuiſyon reſte peace without diſcencyon realme cytee deuyded maye ſtand late verified ¶ fraunce fell full greate diuiſion whiche yt firſt henry kyng englāde ouer rode lande greate prouiſion conquered theim diuiſion emong theim fortified wher vnite loue edified might theim haue ſaued proſperite frome hurt aduerſite ¶ whexfore good lord thynke leſſō nowe teache lorde marche heire young maye bee prowe thynke whē wether waxeth faire people vnto hym dooeth repaire litill hath theim releue peaſe maye hap people caſe ¶ ſauour newe ſhell taken olde taſteth ſame kynd ympe gardein frith ymped ſtocke fro whence came ſauourith euer nothyng blame rote frome whiche dooth ſpryng muſt euer taſt ſauour eatyng ¶ young wiſedome hym endowe whiche full hard gette without labour whiche labour maye bee eaſe nowe labour came kyng emperour let hym bee idill ſhall bee ſucceſſor honour eaſe together maye wherfore writh nowe wand grene ¶ endowe hym nowe noble ſapience whiche maye wolf werre frome gate wiſedome worth defence gold rich congregate wanteth witte alwaye deſolate good rule manly gouernaunce euer enfect contrariaunce ¶ endowe hym alſo humilitee wrath deferre humble pacience whiche ſhall increace dyed cauntorbury archebiſhop ſignified ¶ whiche ingile iue call lande englande inglis thei harde afore engeſt called engeſtes lande corrupt ſpeach englande hight therfore afterwarde ſo name hath euer wyfe chriſten man became ſo lyfe ¶ charter fyrſte ſeged ſo towne superſet cyonſneſſe dāpnable ydolatrye wtin ladyes ſmocke ſhewed theyr banner theyr ſaluacyon feare whiche full ſore herte rewed ſodaynly vnto roan remoued wyfe dame gylle dede buried without chylde betwene notifyed ¶ wedded pepam ſyſter fayre duke robert normandye roone whome gate william ſonne heyre hym duke therof anone yeres many paſſed ouergone nowe ceaſſe wyll enclyne tyll afterwarde ſhall tell forth theyr lyne ¶ kyng alurede lawes troye brute lawes moluntynes marcians congregate danyſhe lawes well conſtytute grekyſhe alſo well made approbate englyſhe tongue dyd tranſlate whiche yet called lawes alurede weſtmynſter remembred dede ¶ yere viii c lxxx eyghtene alurede noble kyng ſo dyed reygned xxix yere clene dane batayls multiplyed faught often colman notifyed chronycle cathologe entytled well dyaloge ¶ fyftye batayls ſyx ſmote somtyme worſe ſomtyme better somtyme felde note sometyme fled awaye ſayth letter lyke fortune cauſe lefte vnfeter neuertheleſſe ofte ſo came contred kepte lande fro ſhame c xii chapiter ¶ edwarde fyrſte kyng englande reygned xxiiii yere dyed yere chryſte ix c xix edwarde ſōne ſo crowned anone weſtſex parlyament protectour made againe fone whiche warred ſore englande aſſent yere viii c lxxx fyftene ſpent earle athylwolde exyled fraunce nonne rauyſhed vſaunce ¶ ſame earle athylwolde danyſhe hoſte mers eſtanglande deſtroyed ſore kyng edwarde full bolde slewe ethalwode hooſt vnderſtande diſcomfet hole droue lande made kynges englande ſubiectes ſo thought dettes ¶ ſommoned london parliamēt depoſed kynges euerychone englande made aſſent duke earles thence forwarde ſo anon euery kyngdome ordayned one ſome thre made ordynaunce kyngdomes foringed gouernaunce ¶ kyng englande proclaymed hole voyde varyaunce diſcorde warre many yeres ſtande whyles ſeuen kynges gouernaunce ther might lawe ne peace haue perſeueraūce wherfore toke euery duke homage earles alſo baronage ¶ scotland wale warred ſore dede homage scottes tyll became men made homage ſouerayne lorde britayne rede kynges dyd theyr herytage theyr men vaſſelage ryde hym euer gooe warre peace agayne frende fooe ¶ duke ethelrede mers alſo wyfe elfled hyght weſtcheſter repayred waſted dane warre ſtrife whiche roomaynes firſt builded feired tyme thei lande repeired roomayne werke while thei occupied citee firſt full freſhly edified ¶ thē faught kyng wt dane wodefeld ſore mers alſo herford wt greate pain wher victorye theim euermore faught dane ſoth ſain towceſter laid theim plain yorkeſhire alſo ſlewe dane downe voided theim region c xiii chapiter ¶ kyng made vnion realmes called englande failed neuer name noble kyng thus made vnion ſeuē realmes yt ſtode three hūdred yere sixe thyrty alſo greate deuiſion warres many colman ſaieth full clere fro gurmond driuen carreis whiche yere fiue c iiii ſcore thirtene vnto yere chriſt nine hundred nientene ¶ theſe erles duke held lawe ſhryues nowe ſhires dooen maintene common ouerlaied full ſore awe ſore oppreſſed ſtates ſuſtene wherfore voided theim office clene ſhryues made region whiche haue forgete extorcion ¶ noble kyng edward thelder hight reigned full twenty foure yere buryed wincheſter full right flores full clerely dooeth apere tyme ſurely peere wyſedome manhode ſeen lawe peace could ſo well ſuſtene c xiiij chapiter ¶ athelſtane kyng england reigned fiftene yere dyed yere chriſt nine hundred thirty fiue conſtantyne kyng scottes warred athelſtane recouered homage myracle ſainct iohn beuerley ſheweth afterward sir athilſtane eldeſt ſoonne age wiſedome euer full ſadly well auiſed kyngſtō crouned toke homage lordes right deuiſed agaynſte whome wale thei ſuffiſed warred made theim obeye made homage meune bee aye ¶ wohſe tyme ſo y• yere chriſt nine hūdred thyrty fiue full accompted robert rollo ſoule corp aſondred corp earth ſoule amounted whiche knighthod dane ſurmounted reigned duke normandy thirty yere accompted full clerly ¶ ſuccedid ſoōne wyllyā lōgſpee hym duke normandy kyng scottes cruelte rebellyō scottes hight conſtantyne hym warred cruelly whiche kyng athilſtane mightily stroyed scotland till people dyed cold hunger dyed mortified ¶ ſo comforted euen miracle faught none wt kyng conſtātyne feld habitacle theim droue lād wt muche payne tyme full fain enclyne athilſtane make homage homage scottes scotland heritage ¶ anlaaf kyng denmark full pride couſyn kyng conſtantyne scotland ſhippis many arriued humberſide burneſburgh claymed england haue kyng vnderſtand truage whiche eldres afore hym brought colbrōd fight therfore ¶ athilſtane daye aſſigned made hym redy battaill haue ſmitten colbrond armed hart benyngned ſir guy warwike weten guy warwicke palmer wyſe colman hath wryten battaill toke hym englandis right colbrond armes fight ¶ wher ſleugh danyſhe champion whiche battaill truage releſed couenaunt made compoſicion betwene kynges afore warres ceſed thus kyng anlaaf home denmarke preſid without warre conturbacion ſir guy went contemplacion ¶ kyng athelſton frauncheſid beuerley worſhip god ſainct iohn wher life written euer aye miracle ſtroke ſo ſtone neuer manne might dooe athilſton grace god direccion prayer ſainct iohn affeccion ¶ noble kyng euer iuſt trewe god faith church deuocion poore menne grace ſubiectes euer rewe preeſtes age reuerence feld towne dome ſadnes trouth diſcrecion yere nene hundred thyrty fiue reigned ſixtene yere life ¶ brother edmōd kyng thē crouned kyng e • mōd reigned • yere englande whole concent eſtate whome dothowe kyng scotlāde yt ſtoūde howell walis kyng create afore vſed determinate homage ſcottes feaute hym made leege homage wale scotlande yt heritage ¶ ſette ſainct dunſtan glaſtenbury vnder thabbot monkes religion abbot hym canturbury kyng edmond ſlain felone whiche malice falſe treaſon forfet dampned dye forfet felonye ¶ cauntorbury y• kyng hym ſaw daye yre hym ranne ſore hym wounde whiche ſtroke kyng aye dyed two ther ſtounde eche theim mortall wounde whiche prince accorded wyſe put hym ſelfe drede wher lawe may chaſtice ¶ reigned vi yere died yere ix hundreth fourtye one glaſtenbury buried without doute whome people made ful great mone lawe peace kept euerychone common neuer tyme ſuppriſſed oppreſſours hym alwaye chaſtiſed ¶ brother edrede hym crowne edrede kynge englāde london tooke royall feautee eſtates within region excepte scotlande theyr vnlewtee rebelliō ye scottes crowned gilryke dane great beautee royall bloodde borne generate theyr kyng hym fully create ¶ kyng edrede went scotland power lande waſted ſore brent wherfore scottes hole conſent feer put downe gilryke regyment droaue hym denmarke ſtent edrede came baronage homage ye scottes hym made feautee homage ¶ yere ix hundreth fourty nyne died buried wyncheſter cytee ſoule made enclyne corp paſſe awaye flee god heauen would ſhould bee viii yere full reigned death hym toke ſikenes great ſore ¶ edwyn brother reſceyued crowne edwyn kynge folyſhe proude maligne wytte full lytle reaſon baron cauſe vndigne made hym crowne reſigne depoſed hym fro regiment parliament theyr commen aſſent ¶ ſaynt dunſtane aduoutre blamed amende would kyn wyſe whiche full openly defamed realme vnwiſe whiche lordes common ryſe droaue hym awaye wher man knewe thus ſynnes olde make ſhames come full newe ¶ reigned iiii yere depriued eſtate without thanke god man therfore well worſe men moſte behate reygne hauyng lenger date dyed yere ix hundreth fyfty thre foringed hole mageſtee c xv chapiter ¶ edgare kyng englande reigned xviii yere died yt yere chriſt ix hundreth three ſcore eleuen brother edgare commē aſſente edgare choſen kyng chronicle recorde diademe crowned parliamēt homage toke royall euery lorde mercyfull full miſericorde ſaynt dunſtan reconciled whome kyng edwyn wrongfully exiled ¶ archebyſhop cauntorbury made eſtate primate dignitee monkes nonnes mynſters fayre glad fourtye founded religiouſtee within realme owne royaltee endewed theim lande tenemente sufficiently eſtablyſhemente ¶ wedded elfbede yt duke doughter ozmere gate ſonne good fayre ſaynt edwarde marter eldeſt ſonne heyre lykely prince towarde comly fayre elflede died wedded elfrith wyfe doughter duke orgare life ¶ gate ethelbert ſo anone kynges wale ſubieccion scottes kynge kynowth withouten moon homage yt scottes made hym homage without obieccion thus vnder proteccion rode hym alwaye warre peace tyme withouten lea ¶ trewe dome wyſe mede fauoure wold falſe trewe leuers lawe deſpyſe ſocoured euer felon hanged hy halſe conſpiratours murtherers traytours al cōmon weale aboue thyng preferred euery prince ſhuld ſe wer wel obſerued ¶ taxed common ne ſuppryſed ne holy churche yet clergie lyued owne aſſiſed vpon rente landes morallye officer hym ruled full tably euery ſhire went priuetee ſpie knowe hurtes commontee ¶ kyng full worthy condigne let eaſe laboure ſearche ſee defautes maligne theim correcte gouernoure god ſet neuer kyng ryotoure thoffice king trippe tapettes lyue ydelneſſe rule kyndes buſyneſſe ¶ died yere ix hundreth ſixty eleuen reygned full eyghtene yere buried glaſtenbury neuen corp earth ſoule heauen clere dead foure twenty yere byſhop oſwald ſame diociſe counſell thabbot wyſe ¶ abbot edwarde place hight layde hym toumbe made newe ſhorte brake englande iiii yere ſoule blyſſe went well ſene nowe muſte euer dwell ioye eterne emonge ſayntes heauen chriſt goddes ſonne beleuen c xvi chapiter ¶ kyng ethelrede kyng englande reigned xxxviii yere withouten lea tyme ſhould reigne peace ¶ realme ſayd right murther cruell homycede brother dight whiche murther euer aſketh vengaūce euery ſyde wherfore ſaid ſerue god ſo betyde fayreſt chaſtiſement put fro ſame regyment ¶ saynt dunſtan died went heauen kyng rode forth london citee rode ſawe cloude full euen wonderfull token rede bloodde people ſee whiche englande hole ouerſpred quantitee fro whiche bloodde reyned vpon ground men trouwed haue ben peryſhed yt ſtound next yere dane southhāpton arryued brent countre aboute alſo ſpoyled ſore brente towne ſo dyd cornewayle throughout deuenſhire alſo ſomerſet doubte dorſetſhire wylſhyre barkeſhrye brent london came euer yt ſtent ſuburbes ſpoyled ſore brent two duke denmarke norwaye northfolke southfolke eſſex ſtent brent ſpoyled ſo forth helde waye london theyr felowes laye aſſembled paſſed kente countre ſpoyled ſore brent ¶ lande kent graunted truage lyue peace home agayne went northfolke hoſte paſſage made ſo lyncolne ſtent lyncolneſhyre throughout brent yorkeſhyre alſo home went againe pylage great full faine ¶ king might get helpe wt fight treated wt king anlaaf norway wt king swaan denmarke right deſtroyed lande fell araye truage hight furthwarde paye power amongeſt thē prayſe full fayne warres ceaſe yet kyng swayne wold nothīg reſt came agayne crowned kyng greate tallage lande myſſe toke alwaye ſpecyally thyng saynt edmūdes landes hurt great taſkīg tallage rayſed vnegally pondred peyſed whiche warrys quene emme normandy brother duke rycharde thyrde ſonnes alurede edwarde edmunde ironeſyde ſo betyde theſe toke ſhyppe ſhe dyd kyng ethelrede ſea led pryuely helpe haue gotte lande ¶ whiche tyme whyls normandye ſo • ournyng kyng swayn full lowde cryed ſayde vnto men faſt gan crye deed ſaint edmunde hath ſpyed ſpeare hath mortifyed wo worth yt day noied edmundes ground ſpeare hert hath ſore wounde ¶ dyed ryght ſo without confeſſyon whyther went ne wote ne whare well wote good true profeſſyon saynt edmonde king dyed made fare blyſſe eterne withoute care baron lordes englande sent worde ethylrede hym ſtande wrote yt kyng swayn deed bade hym come lande agayne ſo dyd councell theyr rede exyled dane greate diſoayne ſlewe downe batayle wt great payne whiche therle edryk ſent kyng knowte englande come hooſt great ſtout ¶ ylke kyng knowte yt ſonne kyng swain england cam wt hoſt great power whome ethylrede met faught agayne batayle ſtronge droue home full clere whome edryk fled dyd apere denmarke falſe traytoure vntrewe purpoſyng ſo come agayne newe kyng ethelred meane tyme dyed yere chryſte thouſande thyrtene reygned colman notifyed thyrtie eyght warre intene euer ne newe vexed ſene owne lande fled drede en myte without ſocoure fro fayne flee ¶ thus chaſtyſed mother gylt accordyng well holy trewe ſcrypture cauſe ſhe brother ſlain ſpylt lyke wordes ſaynt dunſtane full ſure ſayde puniſhyng full pure oute realme dryuen expelled whiche ſyn ſo hye excelled c xvii chapiter edmond ironeſide gotē generate firſt wife duke doughter englād edmonde ironeſyde reigned kīg englād thre yere ethelrede father ꝓrogate vnto crowne royall lande men called hym ſo vnderſtande euer rode armed ay oppreſſours chaſtyce waye ¶ knowt denmarke aſſayled ofte lande tyme euer armed went vſe feate armes vnderſtande knyghthode full well dyd appent thus colman ſayth flores ment ſyxe batayles agayne kyng knowt ſmote victorye flores hath note ¶ voyde greate effuſyon chryſten bloude two together accorde fyght ſelfe full concluſyon within yke seuerne concorde withouten warre diſcorde ſo myghte get victorye reioyſe realme monarchye ¶ theyr daye place ſo aſſygned armed met ſtrokes knyghly ſet ſpeare ſwerd eyther ſo repugned axe dagger eyther bette eyther tryſte ouerhande gette laſte kyng knowt hym alayde theſe wordes thus hym ſayde ¶ wolde god edmonde thou ſo couetouſe nowe myne herte wolde caſe glad deſyrous ſhulde longe batayle thus holde men great gladneſſe manifolde yf thou halfe denmarke halfe englande whiche wepons fro thē caſte eyther armes gan embrace theyr hoſtes amarueled ful faſte dyd meane ceaſſe ſo lytell ſpace knewe betwne caſe kneled chryſte laudifyed herte deuoute ye eche ſo victoryed ¶ realmes parted two hole accorde betwene ſo concorded loued euer brother ſo chronycles haue well hole recorded fro tyme forth diſcorded yſle faught hyght clyues cōmon langage dyd pleaſe ¶ edryk lyncolne euer vntrewe reconſyled home edmonde agayne ſubtyll meane good king edmond ſlewe pryde wyſe without wounde mayne fourme wryte ſayne reygned yt tyme fully iii yere buryed man durſte ſpere ¶ yere chryſte thouſande ſo dyed awaye accompte ſyxtene vnknowen people lordes tho made great dole thē ſeen neuertheleſſe myght better bene falſe edryk ſo falſely couered openly diſcouered c xviii chapiter knowt kynge englande dē marke kyng knowt reigned englād thē anon wedded quene eme england ethelrede wife gate loue anon englande eſtates londe cōmons alſo fre bonde gate ſonne harde knowt hight fyrſte wyfe swayne herold ryght ¶ ſent edmonde edwarde yt ſonnes two edmōd ironeſide swithen kīg knowt ſlee lowſe kepe pouerte ſo ſhould neuer haue power oute claime england neyther hooſt ne route whome ſent forth hungry emperoure letter worthely ¶ beſechyng hym noryſhe ſaue declaryng hym whoſe ſonnes whiche dyd full worthy gaue vnto edmonde owne doughter dere whiche edmonde dyed ſhe fere without chylde wherfore aga cooſyn doughter herry gaue edwarde fyne ¶ whiche edwarde called edwarde thexyl • came edgare called edgar athelyng knowt let hym ſelf crounyng london hold chriſtmas houſhold went greate ſolas ¶ wher erle edrik kyng knowt hym cōfeſſed ſlain kyng edmond ironeſide owne leege lorde cruell death impreſſed gette loue hym dwell bide vnlikely goo ride twoo kynges together englande ſaied accordyng land ¶ kyng woordes well herd cōceiued howe aſked reward mede made hym tell howe lorde diſceiued afore lordes dooen deed whiche boldely without dreed hauyng ſhame aſke greate reward whiche kyng lordes gaue whole award ¶ hang hym toure duryng liue dedde folke might hym ſe treſon openly ſhriue hang till dye emong common truily greate biworde many one yt woundre rōne therle edryke strettoun ¶ kyng went norway conquered droue kyng 〈…〉 f land held ſo conqueſt ſwerd full worthily gouerned euery land peace lawe kept theim faund dome rightwyſe ſtable poore alway merciable ¶ kyng malcom scotland thē homage hym furth became euer manne homage yt scottes kynges wale hye parage north weſt occian kyngdonies landes tyme moſte redoubted prince londes loaued ¶ roome rode royall goodly wyſe biſhop greately commed chriſten prince papall whole aduiſe cardynalles foure whiche biſhop ſed malburgate foure mile fro roome extende greate meyne hym mette greate honour roome themperour ¶ commyng england gaue norway vnto ſoonne ſir swayne herold ſoonne vnderſtand england gaue whiche full fain harknowt denmarke gaue certain ſo dyed chriſten whole creaunce shaftiſbury buryed ordynaunce ¶ yere chriſt thouſand ſo thirty foure alſo truly written reigned fro tyme began eightene yere whole well wrytten darte death whē ſmitten whoſe dayes land inquiet full rich welfare whole replete c xviij chapiter ¶ herold kyng england ſoonne kyng knowt reigned fiue yere dyed yere thouſand xxxix herolde ſoonne crouned deede herold loofrike yt duke leiſceſtre londoner flores reede danyſhyr alſo ſaieth letter ſtrong werre power greater lordes engliſhe nacion london made coronacion ¶ alurede ſoonne kyng ethelrede fifty ſailes landed southampton wher kynge herold hoſte hym met deede redy fight hym croune certain lordes englondes region betwene theim treated alurede went normandy duke robert full plain ¶ afterward alurede ſo rode fro mother vnto kyng herold duke goodwyn gyldiſmore hym bode people greate nombre manyfold ſlewe menne downe would led hym furth ely hym ſlewe traitour falſe euer bee vntrewe ¶ chronicle ſaieth putte bothe eyen fro whiche dyed ſone pain woo ſayin ſlette wombe full keen lengeſt gut ſtacke nayled tho led hym ſtack ther muche wo till came wombe within thus ſleugh thei hym ſobteltie gyn ¶ mother quene eme edward ſent normandy duke wyllyam anone hir couſyn kepe ſhent kyng herold cruelty alone warnyng hym treaſō yt herold dooen whiche cauſe herold hir exild england edward alſo hir child ¶ flaundres ſhe fled full ſore amoued erle badwyn hir couſyn nie bloodde declaryng hym howe herold diſtroyed hir ſoonne alurede heyre england ſtood exiled hir without ſocour good edward alſo hir ſoonne heire england brother child alſo awaye vncouth land ¶ wherfore therle kyng hardknowt wrote hir compleynt ſocour prayed ſhould help might god wote amendid ſhe affrayed came anone warre full well aryed flaundres mother pleaſe hir ſocour ſette hir hert eaſe ¶ whiche meane kyng herold dyed weſtminſter buried full feire reigned notified fiue yere reigned without heire body gotten hym repeire england gouerne wherfore lordes aſſēt kyng hardknowte flaundres ſente ¶ bee kyng ſith herold gone pleaſe hym mother comfort came england furth anone crouned whole diſport lordes conde flores dooeth report thus kyng hardknowt kyng englande worthily yt tyme reigne tho began ¶ kyng began brother death venge kyng hard knowt▪ erle gowyn erle kent peaſed ſhould reuenge riche giftes whiche hym ſpent meekeneſſe lowe ſwore ſent dooe thyng pein high treſon kyng herold charged without reaſon ¶ good giftes mighty hie rich kyn meekely hym obeyed acquaintaūce thei made expreſſe vpon holy euangelis ſworne vndelayed kyng graūted hym grace well payed make hym coūſell gouernaūce without wrath diſcordaunce ¶ maried ſiſter gunylde henry themperour falſly accuſed ſynne cryme vſed auoutry young manne whiche hir excuſed lawe land vſed battaill hand flewe accuſour approuyng hym vntrewe ¶ whiche ſhe would nomore come bed lyued ſole euer ſo hir life good ne gold aught hir beed loue ne threte betyng ne ſtrife hym deſtroyed mikell yorkſhire diſcomfited yt archebiſhop yorke clergy milton ſwale kyng edward began ſiege berwyk like wonne falſe tale let tidinges newe yt nought kyng robert bruys kyng scotlande mette medowe nere swale water laye great power walter wareyn among hay kockes buſhed vpon byſhop ſodenly scottes yſſued ¶ xv hundreth englyſhe ſlewe home went kyng edward full glad pryſoners many mo men certayne lordes exiled twoo spencer land yt spencer made great perſecucion kyng agayn lordes ſlewe erle lancaſter lordes ye parliamēt thē weſtminſter next hold erle thomas yt called ful trewe therle vmfrey herford bold therle marche full manly men knewe monbrey alſo percy clyfford drewe armed came two spencer exiled fro englande neuer reconſyled ¶ ſone spencer came yt kyng syr hugh lorde ſyr hugh ſonne put therle marche great diſdayn roger ſonne hym wonne appeched hym hye treaſon agaynſt kyng wherfore kyng hym ſent toure tabyde parliament ¶ went kyng spencer two hoſtes full great burton vpon trent lordes laye ſparled theim ſo north went wayes one aſſente rayſe mo men truſt theyr entent spencer two fully deſtroye realme full cruelly noye ¶ borinbrig ſyr andrewe hertlaw met erle vmfrey herford hym ſlewe toke erle thomas without let kyng pountfret drewe ſette vpon hym iudges newe therle edmound arondell iuſtice ſyr robert mapilthorpe enemyes ¶ headed anone vpon hyll buryed chapell fayre henry brother ſtode kynges wyll kyng graunted bee heyre wedded alyce without deſpayre doughter heyre therle henry lacy lyncolne ſo graunted kynges mercy ¶ wyllyā fitz wareyn many another knight diuers ſhyres ſome hanged ſome head hold hym compeer right syr bartholomewe badeliſmore without rede drawen hanged put foul dead roger clyfford iohn monbraye baron headed theyr rebellion ¶ therle marche ſyr roger mortymer ſonne roger foriuged treaſon kyng death pardoned put perpetuall pryſon towre ſame encheſon fro tyme forth spencer excede quene hand mayden dede ¶ tyme kyng brother hir ſent alſo ſonne edwarde dooen homage guyen ſo haue entente dwelled ſo long viage kyng theim ſuſpecte theyr meſſage councell spencer theim exiled chronicle pleynly compiled ¶ kyng made playnly create entente ¶ kyng robert paſſed home agayn prayes greate many pryſoners fro humber north people downe ſlayn whiche kyng councelers blamed therle andrewe compeer men enough hym arayed scottes might haue ſlayn frayed ¶ hight kyng haue brought hym great power yorkſhyre held nothing hight therfore kyng counſell spencer gaue charge take hym either daye night kyl hym downe wher mete wt hym might ſhryues
