sayd beſt thyng might befall chiefteyne greue fo ouerterue kepe hymſelfe harmeleſſe therwithall maye hurte fo without fall paſſe away ſocoure harmeleſſe foole abyde diſtreſſe ¶ wer gone ſo home agayn theyr frendes theim then awaye two hundreth men common came full fayne alnewike caſtell ſymple araye men bet theim agayn alwaye tyll glad yelde theim haue grace whiche without longer ſpace quenes power yt ſhe ſo brought fro fraunce ſo litle wardeyns naught dread hight kyng hir ordinaunce kepe lande helpe ſhe may ſhe ought great power beſped whē charles doughter fraūce void dower deſpoyled fraunce fayled power ¶ quene iſabel kyng rychardes wife kyng richardes wife ſent home • raunce depoſed kyng henry derby • wels knowen full ryfe home ſent without remedye auayled hir kynne progenye nought el great vexacion frenchemen made theyr owne dampnacion cc xl chapiter ¶ mocion conceypte maker booke touchynge kynge henrye ſyxte wife ſonne gotten home putte gouernaunce fled hym cōſyderyng trouth forſoke lyuelodes welfare ſake fro ſo gotten home trewe el geue ſore iudgement vpon theim gracious lord kyng edward fourth accompte conſydre howe kynge henrye admytte vnto croune englande amounte deſert yet witte might hym ſelfe otherwyſe yet onely caſtigacion kyng richardes wicked peruerſacion ¶ whiche realme yrked euerychone full glad depoſicion glad croune kyng henry ſo anone theyr hertes whole affeccion hatred kyng richardes defection loue kyng henry daye chaunged people hym aye ¶ yet kept aye therle marche full ying erles eſtate warde brought hym vp maner thyng eſtate aſked coulde awarde cheryſhed hym norture regarde owne ſonnes duryng lyfe make hym loue hym without ſtryfe ¶ thus wiſedome ſonne henry right ſo hym cheriſhed good wiſe counſayl whiche aſſigned vnto hym tho good rule would let hym faile cauſe ſhould agayn hym preuayle fraunce hole eſtate hym brother aſſociate ¶ full good policie wynne loue kept hym direccion entiſement eiuill folie pleaſaunce without ſuſpection greate witte circumſpeccion rule hym thus heighnes obaye without ſtryfe ſitte peace daye ¶ gracious lorde nowe ſapience conſydre well ſixtye yere three kyn ye intelligence haue deuorced royaltee nowe god ſpecialitee hath graūted grace rightes recouer enemyes rule ouer ¶ conſidre well benigne innocence kyng henry nowe scotlande goddes dome ſmall intelligence preuayle men vnderſtande gette hym nowe home agayn englande meanes ye maye ſapyence wyfe ſonne dilygence ¶ truſte well yf maye paſſe fraūce power get theim wyſe eche yere wyl trouble greuaūce scottes aſſent theyr exercyſe brag boſte wolde ryſe make people cōmons yrke iackes ſalades ay newe newe wirke ¶ truſte well god nowe heuen scottes wyll ay harme may ſo haue full ofte odde euen afore chriſte borne ſo maye yet theyr power euery daye wherfor good lord brīg home theſe perſons thre theyr men geue grace fre ¶ loue better theyr great lewte forſoke theyr landes herytage fled hym aduerſyte byde payne ſorowe ſeruage good herte ſhulde rewe well theyr trewe corage yt wold haue gone durſte nought conſyder howe thei ſhewed thought ¶ yf ye might get good men haue theyr herytage youre enemy agaynſt ſtode ye ſhulde make trewe men auauntage paſſe warres hoſtage trewe haue bene kyng henry mekell trewce ryght auncetry ¶ yf ye myght theim get nowe euery chone youre warres done thē might ſyt reſt without trouble lande alone youre lande throughout thē might ye treſt yf hole ye nede miſtryſt prynce chriſten myght dere lande ye myght make ¶ graunt henry grace wt owne liuelode duchye hole lancaſter ryght worthyhede fyrſte duke henry noble knight laſte daye mikyll might wyfe ſonne get home ordynaunce geue councell theyr gouernaunce ¶ suche truſte wyll rule worthely youre pleſaunce tranquillyte peace reſte good polyce better haue ſuretye lette theim bene aduerſyte scottes french yt wold ſe deſtreſſe helpe theyr buſyneſſe ¶ yf ye maye meane treate get home ordeine faſte youre flete eaſte ſea scotlande hye edenburgh ſo maye mete vitayle ordynaunce full mete ſet vpon caſtell bene eſcape maye ye ſhall wyn ¶ haue ſene theyr caſtelles ſtronge echone ſtrongeſt bene worſte get wyn amonge certayne none may bene holde longe ye begyn saue dunbretayne ſea aboute doth ryn eche daye nyght twyce withouten doubte caſte • dunbretayne whiche may wonne famyſhyng aboute ¶ ſhippes ſea ſiege vpon lande ye maye fayle haue laſte wyll bene yelde youre hande ye haue workemen well fore caſte youre ordynaunce gonne caſte abylementes warre ſuche ye nede caſtell elles maye withſtande dede ¶ therfore caſtell·that bene tyme beginne warre scotlande go ſame withoute impedyment wynter ſomer ye begyn iuyll moneth auguſte preſent forage may begot doth appent corne graſſe horſes ſuſtenaunce fayre wether mennes hye pleaſaunce ¶ righteous prince bring home ye ſcatred men theyr paſture forſaken forlore breſte ſhulde greate foyſon ren nedy men grace helpe euermore conſyder howe god hath ſet therfore ouer flocke ſeke ſcatered ſhepe laye folde ſurely ſlepe ¶ conſider nowe moſt gracious ſoueraine lorde howe longe nowe noble auncetrye welth helth hath reigned hye recorde kepte lawe peace continually thynke bene monarchye fayreſt floures higheſt enterpryce ſoneſt maye youre foreyne foe ſupprice ¶ conſider alſo ſymple tretyſe howe kynges kepte neyther lawe ne peace went ſone awaye many dyuerſe wyſe without thanke god theyr deceſe nought dred wtin ne without doutleſſe defaute peace lawe conſerued deſtroyed right deſerued ¶ conſyder alſo moſte erthly ſouerayne lorde french scottes ye get neuer pay within thre yere theyr greate rebellyon ye myght repreſſe vtterly reſtrayne kepe euer youre poſſeſſyon obey youre might make full fayne kyng edward dyd wt hunger payne conquered hole ſubieccyon byde edward nowe might thynke thynges wel ſelfe ſtrong enough agaynſt power hys enemy gotte ſuche vyctorye yet dyd wyth dylygence prouyde margarete kynge henrye vi hys wife ſhulde hande let englande feare quyetnes wherfore edwarde nowe beynge oute feare daunger hys enemyes dyd wholy ſet hym ſelfe foure yeres enſuynge reformatyon redreſſynge hys publyke weale recompenſynge hys ſouldyers paynes deuyde geue landes theim wyth kynge henrye hys owne ſo wyth geuynge large ample rewardes dyd get fauoure hys people well laye noble vſynge ſuche vrbanyte clemencye kinde men throughlye wonne harte men whyche gentylnes fryndely famyliaritee dyd euer vſe alſo lawes realme dyd alter mend ſome ſome made newe beſydes coyned monye wel golde ſyluer whyche coynynge royalles noble daye currante whyche golde royal noble ſyluer grotes ſo hys tyme thys kinde coyne came vp hys realme thys ſtate made proclamation yf anye manne beyng traytoure rebellyon hertofore hys grace wyllyng ſubmyt hym ſelfe wholy hym ſhuld haue pardon wolde ſhuld die ſuffer according lawes kyndnes natyue loue dyd cauſe hym haue good wyl herte common ſo much euydent al dayes hys lyfe conqueroure helpe ayde thē ſo much hys enemyes euer ſhamefully put wrack ſhalbe ſhewed playnly hereafter alſo contented wyth frendſhyppe hys owne countree menne dyd wynne procure loue foren ſtraunge prynces made theim bee kynred wyth hym whereby myghte yf nede ſhoulde ſo requyre ayde ſocour leaſt bee iniurious noyſome hym maried hys ſyſter lady margarete charles ſonne phylyppe duke burgoyne throughe maryage greate helpe inſurrection chaunſed thys father rycharde earle whyche cauſe blaſed abrode euerye man dyd meruayle greatelye kynges prynces dyſpleaſed grudged ſayde playnelye hys honoure ſo dooe beganne reproue foreſayde maryage ſhamefullye hertes nowe braſtynge wherby occaſiō quarel might picked edward got kyngdome openly knowne erle warwykes meane helpe begonne ſuſpect hym ſuch authoritee ſo woulde haue plucked ſomewhat frome diminiſhed powre wherby myght haue ruled thynges owne pleaſure hys owne countree nacions man may ſee ofte chaunceth yt frendes geue ſeldome condygne rewarde man deſeruinges yea eftſones greate benefite beſtowed cō ferred vpon theim thei like ingrate perſons nothyng cōſider ye earle warwycke vnknowing ye whiche although loked better thankes ample benefite hādes yet neuertheles thought beſt diſſēble cloke y• matter vntill ſuch oportunitie might wherby myght conſidering wylfulnes kynge exprobrate vnto hym pleaſures yt done verye true euidēt king edward dyd make ſerche houſe thing touched much honeſtie wher earle dede man loued woman well great fanteſie company ſoeuer ether euell wyll deſire empire theyr league ſhuld bee infringed broken earle ſure knowledge letter hys frendes king got wife priuely yt al yt done king lewis embaſſad ioyning newe affinitee fruſtrate vain ſo erneſtly moued thought beſt kynge ſhuld depoſed frō crowne one worthy ſuch kingly offyce oure purpoſe earle warwyke beyng ſore vexed moued wyth kynge leaſt yt furoure hys intēt beyng raſhely gone aboute ſhulde bee broughte good ende determined ſo lōge ſuffer beare ſuche iniuries vntyll ſuche tyme myghte brynge matter paſſe wolde haue thē whiche ſhortly came englande ſalutyng kynge dyd hys meſſage vnto hym makinge hym ſelfe bee ignoraunte maryage earle throughe licence king went ſhyre warwike partly take pleaſure partly preſeruation ſafetie helth whyche yere ſixt yere oure lorde god cccc lxvii vi yeare reygne kynge edwarde whiche yeare george neuell brother earle made archebyſhoppe yorke dyſceaſe wyllyam late archebyſhoppe beeynge lii byſhoppe poſſeſſed rome phylyppe duke burgoyne dyed ſame yeare charles hys ſoonne made duke manne bothe manhode valyantenes warre moſte exellente thys rycharde ſayde hys ſhyre warwycke callynge hym george archebyſſhope yorke iohn montacure marque hys brother bothe long communycation many thinges ſpace ii iii dayes length gettynge meete occaſion ſpeake kynge hys doinges dyd ſhewe hys mind theim deſyrynge theim wayes coulde poſſyble take kynge henry hys part helpe crowne ſaiynge wyſe maner brother anye lyghtenes mynde playne iudgemente moued ſpeake kynge edward king henrye thys henrye godlye manne loueth theim bee hys faythfull ſubiectes doth cōſyder alſo taketh paynes whyche hathe ſoonne borne nature bee greate worthynes prayſe free lyberalitee whome euerye manne maye perceaue muche god lynes whyche helpeth hys father nowe beynge thraldome captiuitee muche hym lyeth kynge edwarde man full contumelye ingratytude geuen pleaſure euell wyllynge take anye paynes promotynge rather theim come nought noble auncient men wherefore thyncke wyll come paſſe ſhortlye eyther wyll deſtroye nobilitee elles nobilitee deſtroye al ſhulde fyrſte enterpriſe reuenge oure cauſe whych haue fyrſte taken hurt hys handes ſure knowe bothe kynge dyd fyrſte pryuelye gooe aboute defyle oure dygnitee dyd openly intende confuſyon loſſe honoure thoughe broughte dygnitee v hym therfore euen late went ambaſſadour fraunce regard whereby eſtimation whiche kynges haue conceaued v partely gotten auncetours partly owne trauailes peines ſhal nowe extynguiſhed vtterly nothinge ſette theſe ꝑſuacions wonne brother ye archebiſhoppe hert brought minde could ſo ſone eaſelye perſuade lorde marque yt firſt would meanes moued worke treaſon hād againſt kyng edward laſt whē earle promyſed helpe powre many noble prynces cōtented kepe warre marque vnwilling conſent yt fyrſt ſo dyd time warre holde king edwardes ſide thē king henryes ſhal appere plain hereafter deſtruccion ii brother ye earle warwike man greate wytte perceauing george duke clarēce brother kīg edward beare great good wyl toward brother yt king ſo euer matter firſt proue hym knowe minde begāne complain lytle king doinges duke ſame tale wyth hym ſhewed alſo iniuries taken brother hand beyng ſomwhat bolder ſpeake brake mynde large deſiring folow coūcel ſhould think done raſhnes ſhewed hym warely pollicie matter wroughte deſired yt would caſt wt ſelfe bring ſuch weyghtie matter paſſe wherby al thinges may prouided hand many great promiſes offered daughter ripe age maried duke throughe councell greate deſieryng therle warwike contented dooe thynges would haue hym yt therle communicacion duke purpoſed goo caleis whiche toune chief capitain wher wife doughters wer inhabityng thend ſedicion might bee ſoner begonne englād ſore troubled greate tyme apoin • ted ſone gone caleis brother tharchebiſhop lord marque ſhould make inſurreccion yorke wherby battaill might bee begonne ſo farre frome theim theſe thynges prepared counſaill well alowed taken went ſtreight yt duke clarence caleys ther duke promiſed othe would euer bee true maried lady iſabell erles eldeſt doughter yt whiche whē dooen thei bothe conſulted together yt ſpedily yt yt inſurreccion made yorke commaunded appoincted whiche cōpaignie begōne firſt ſpoile mercie reſpect thyng ther yorke old riche hoſpitall ſainct leonard poore impotent perſones wer harboured ſicke menne comforted hous founde yt charitee coūtree whiche geue yerely certain wheate yt firſt fruites corne ſuſtenaunce mainteynyng theim whiche noumbre grayne certain houſband menne countree refuſe gyue part counſaill therle warwikes compaignie ſaiyng plainly poore ſickely people thei yt rule gouernaunce hous procters hoſpitall claimyng dewe vnto theim ſought right cauſe greate tumulte muche conſpiracie made ſo within fewe dayes gathered aboute fiftene thouſand whiche compaignie came towardes yorke yt knowne citee ſuche compaignie menne riſen citizen watchyng euer feare doubte whether thei ſhould mete theim trie open felde tary citee kepe theim frome walles lord marque chief coūtre put theim ſtreight feare doubte whiche takyng good deliberacion aduiſement metre theim cūmyng gate yt citee ſharpe cōflicte tooke robert hulderne duke chopped hedde whiche whē dooen receiued citee ye midde night ſouldiours wer people beyng nothyng abaſhed death capitain rather eger fearce conſideryng thei could ouercome yorke without ordinaunce whiche thei lacked wēt ſtreight forth london lord marque putte death yt duke capitain yt cōmons beyng alſo one cōſpiracie intent either would bee aknowen faultie cōmocion el vtterly determined holde kyng edward dooeth appere get perfect amitie kyng knewe mynd purpoſe bothe therle warwike duke clarence owne brother alſo certefied dyuerſe mēnes letter armie drawyng nigh london ſent wyllyam harberte whome made twoo yeres duke greate power walſhe menne commaundyng hym could conueniently bydde battaill enemy erle makyng haſt towardes northampton hard ſaie northrenmenne gotte alſo ſette tentes next daye folowyng fought wt theim whiche battaill putte flight momēt cleane diſcomfited yorkeſhire menne beyng glad victorie wer ſtreight couled went ferder hauyng handes full ſpoyles prayes went backe ward lookyng erle warwike would come whiche ſhortely came calais duke clarence ſoonne lawe hooſt commēdyng highly capitaines reioiſyng gladly thei ye victorie ſpedyly prepare armie yet kyng edward beeyng nothyng abaſhed yt therle pēbruch ſo eiuill ſped ſēt hym forth greater armie whiche readie tymes ſo euer ſhould chaunce hym ſelf folowe ſmall cōpaignie might bee readier thynges iourneye encreaſe armie wt many came hym ſecte ſaiyng entent deſtroie yt route miſliuers flagicious perſones therle warwike perceauyng aduerſaries came vpon hym ſent haſt ye duke clarence whiche nigh hym hooſt would bryng armie haſt hym meanyng yt bataill hand duke hard came ſtreight ther • e thei bothe commyng together went banberie thei perceaued enemyes tētes wer pitched buckelyng together tooke erle • penbruch priſoner killed diſcomfited menne emonges noble • killed rychard erle ryuers father elizabeth quene ſoonne iohn woduile towardes euenyng kyng edward drewe nigh heryng death ſoden betyng doune menne taried toune fiue myle frome place therle warwike went chief toune hooſt within twoo dayes cauſed therle pēbruch certain ſtates taken yt tyme bee behedded meane ſeaſon begonne awaie bee foūd peace whiche letter wer wrytten fro herauldes ſent kyng therle frome erle kyng wherby kyng truſtyng verely pacified leſſe ware hym ſelf feared leſſe aduerſaries whiche thyng knowen ſhewed erle certain ſpies went furth night priuely could ſtrong power kyng tentes ther killyng theim yt kepte watche tooke kyng vnware brought hym warwike entent kyng frendes might knowe wher conueighed hym priuely then night toune yorkeſhire called middelame bee kepte faſt hold yet kyng could bee place priſone ſhortely knowen whiche cauſed many menne bee ſorie lament chaunce hym ſelf priſone ſpake faire kepers caſtell muche intreatyng greate promiſes made ſo tempte corrupt theim dimiſſed althoughe rumour erle willyng whiche might bee likelyhood therle gyuen ouer fightyng ſuche yt eiuill fortune kyng henry wherby manne maye perceiue could neuer haue purpoſe ſeyng mannes ſtrength policie able ouercome therle frēdes ventre bodyes ſpent ſubſtaūce haue brought henry royall dignitee becauſe knewe ſuerly long edward reigned neither could yet kyng hēry beare rule yet neuertheleſſe thei lette hym goo holde kyng edward deliuered went ſtreight yorke beyng honorably receiued citezens taried ſpace twoo dayes gette hym hooſt menne could haue worthy compaignie conſideryng yt ſhould goo london emong middeſt hooſt went frome yorke lancaſtre found wyllyam haſtynges lord chamberlain whō hauyng greate helpe came ſafe lōdon therle warwike duke thei perceiued kyng edward bee deliuered throughe meanes falſe trai tour thynges thei appoincted none effecte greately moued anger ſorowe callyng together chief frendes conſulted howe thei might begynne battaill whiche whē kyng taken hold ended dooen thus dooyng certain veray angre loue thei warre offred theim ſelfes fight freſhe nothyng yt whiche moued ye chief capitaines ye earneſt alſo kyng edward wyllyng fight thei wherby might either bryng theim force armes quietnes peace el deſtroy kylle theim euery mother ſoonne realme might bee 〈…〉 tter ſtate thorowe ſedicious rebellyng people wer greately impoueriſhed ſeyng churche • houſes menne ſpoiled • obbed menne ſ • euery place ye corne graſſe alſo deſtroyed grounde many miſchiefes dooen whiche dooe chaunce eftſons battaill conſideracion wherof piti • many menne ſee cōmen weale caſe whiche wēt dayly hourely aſwell therle kyng atonemēt deſieryng counſelyng theim bothe thei would rather kepe peace haue loue menne quiet lyuyng liue angre enuie fightyng one yt vndooyng realme wher wer wicked deede kylle father yet greate dele wicked deſtroye whole bodie commen weale whiche father menne whiche euery manne maynteyned kept greate entreatyng noble menne therle kyng gyuyng feyth one peace tyme wherein erle duke went bothe london ſmall compaignie menne compariſon daunger thei wer weſtminſter kyng reformacion ſtabliſhyng thynges peace bee wher kyng thei beeyng greate woordes nothyng determyned ended therfore kyng vowe made departed ſaid lytle erle duke alſo went warwike lyncolne ſhire gotte vp newe hooſt made ſir robert welles ſoonne rychard welles graūde capitain noble manne warre theſe tydynges commyng london moued kyng veray ſore whome thought would rather haue kepte peace thē warre yt ſhewed hym vnlokyng yt battaill hande wt ſo muche yt ſooner ſpede gathered armie ſame tyme ſēt dyuerſe meſſē gers haroldes rychard welles theſame rychard • eeyng often ſo ſent made excuſe ſicke diſeaſed afterward whē excuſe admitted thynkyng purge hymſelf ſufficiētly kyng came london bringyng wt hym ſir thomas democke brother lawe whē certain frendes certified hym ye kyng ſore moued hym whiche feare kyng take ſentuarie weſtminſter brother alſo mindyng tary vnto ſuche tyme yt kyng anger wer couled apeaced kyng edward truſtyng pacifie tumulte without bloddeſhede promiſyng thoſe mēne feith yt would harme thē cauſed theim bothe come ſentuarie kyng callyng rychard hym warned hym byd brother robert ſhould leaue warre goo frome erle meane ſeaſon kyng went foreward wt hooſt againſt enemy bryngyng hym foreſaid rychard thomas beeyng frome stamforde wher enemy lie ſpace twoo dayes iourney informed yt robert kepte yt armie ſtill nothyng moued yt letter father wrytyng whiche kyng beyng ſore greued cauſed bothe rychard thomas euen cōtrarie promiſe mooſt ſhamefully haue heddes chopped robert whē ſawe kyng drawe nigh hard father ſir thomas democke put death ſtoode firſt doubte whether ſhould fight becauſe ieoperdeous ventre vpon ſuche greate power yt erle came yet laſt ſtoute courage manly boldenes hym thei went together fought ſore long many menne killed bothe ſydes laſt whē fore named robert encouraged menne wer ready geue ouer coumpaſſed enemy taken alſo ſir thomas delalāt many 〈…〉 whiche capitaines beyng taken ye hooſt putte flight driuen awaye kyng beyng glad victorie cōmaunded robert ſir thomas delalant many bee put death yt ſame tyme place battaill ther kylled mēne reported tenne thouſand menne erle tyme beeyng owne toune warwike commyng ſhortely armye stamforde power enformed battayle foughte quickelyer looked men worſe parte although might diſcouraged yet made thoughe paſſed would beleue entente myghte enbouldē certaine compaigny deſpayryng geuyng theimſelfe flight beganne make newe hoſte many faire promyſes wowe brother lawe thomas stanley take parte yt ſaid thomas would meanes fight rebell agaynſte kyng edwarde ſeeyng tyme gooe one waye miſtruſtyng able reſiſte power hys enemyes fled wyth duke clarence ſoonne lawe excetre whē taried two three dayes ſeyng lacked al thynges neceſſarye warre purpoſed gooe lewes kyng fraunce ambaſſate fraunce veraye well acquaynted beloued truſtyng ether haue ſome helpe kyng el incenſe hym wholy fight againſt hym ſo toke ſhippe dartmouth duke greate nombre theyr familie ſayled ye wynde normandie chiefe lord towne entreteyned hym moſt royally al ye haſt certified yt kyng lewes cōmyng thither yt kyng meruailyng greatlye yt noble actes yt erle doen mynded thorowly helpe hym yt could knewe yt lāded fraūce glad ſent hym certayn noble ſhewe hym wiſhe haue occaſion wherby might helpe hym time would gladly dooe deſieryng hym come ambaſſy kyng laye ambaſſy manour place yt kynges ſet vpō ryuer ſyde loire duke alſo ſonne law ſhould bee loſſe harme yt ix yere kyng edwardes reigne ix yere erle fled fraunce lorde cccc lxxx greued kyng edward thei wer fled becauſe many ye people cōmunaltee deſyrous ſee hym thought ſonne goone theim worlde abſent ſuche eſtimaciō honour people yt thei worſhipped honoured none hym leaſt none hym ſo muche yt name euery mannes ſong voyce eſpecially cōmē people made triumphe abrode yt ſtretes wherby moſte parte helde earle ſyde bare hym fauoure theyr harte kyng edward wherby ye kyng feare daunger owne countremen yt wer realme theim abrode fraunce prouide yt erle cōmyng firſt ſente charles duke burgom brother law deſiryng yt would manaſhe lewes kyng wt made league peace aide erle warkwike yt duke ſonne lawe neither wt mony mē charles wrote yt kyng fraūce thretened hym many thynges ſo mainteyned helped theim kyng fraūce red letter aūſwered ſaied yt might lawfully would ſauyng league truce helpe frēds yt wer valiaūt noble men earle ſettyng nothyng thretenyng braggyng wordes ſayd ſhoulde bee neither greate peyne coſte hym whē theſe tydynges came england yt kyng veraye ſorie cauſe ſearched priuely realme wer frēdes enemy feare yt reaſon examinaciō theim yt wer priſoners hand ſome take ſentuarie ſome came ye kynges ſide emonges theim lord marque montacute offered hymſelf kyng helpe hym warres kyng gladly receaued becauſe mo would leane ſide meane ſeaſon ye erle warwike duke went ambaſſy wher kyng fraūce way people came veraye thicke ſee hym becauſe harde ſo muche ſpeakyng nobleneſſe came kyng receaued hym moſte gently whō ſhortly erle breake mynd ſhewed cauſe commyng whome kyng promyſed coulde dooe hym vttermoſte extente power sone quene margarete wife henrye yt vi came theim ſōne prince edward earle penbruck alſo oxēforde whiche lytle ſayled ouer cōmuned together concernyng yt ſafegard body league made thorowe kyng fraunce counſel firſt lady anne doughter earle maried deſpouſed prynce edwarde quenes ſoonne alſo erle duke promyſed faithfullye yt woulde geue ouer vnto ſuche tyme kyng henrye vi edwarde ſoonne proclaymed kyng englande kyng henry erle duke ſhould ouerſee gouerne realme wyll apoyntmente quene margarete ſonne prince edwarde vnto ſuche tyme forenamed prince wer lawfull age habilitee whiche promyſed faythfully obſerue dooe wer apoynted beſydes theſe many condicions made aſwel reaſon ſo require buſynes yt tyme league truth faithfulnes thus made kyng lewes holpe erle mēne harnes nauie might ſurer go englāde rhenate alſo father y• quene margarete gaue hym mēne harnyſe power hauyng ſmall nombre men take ſhippe sayne mouth ther tariyng hard word englād letter ſhould come ouer haſte ſo many yt would take parte yt ſhoulde haue nede bryng hym wer redy harneyſe water ſide willyng helpe hym al yt could onely many noble men prince would helpe hym wt mony men harneyſe yt could dooe receaued theſe letter purpoſed go forth take oportunitee tyme becauſe ye quene redy ſet forth duke oxēford ye duke penbruch went wt parte yt hoſte nauye trie chaūce thei ſhuld haue thinges ſhould chaunce well quene prynce ſhould folowe come vnto englande therfore earle duke thanking king highly coulde doone ſo much theim dyd take leaue ſayled vnto englande armie duke burgoyne contented earle ſhoulde bee holpen king fraūce agaynſt king edward prepared great nauye ſhippes aboute coſtes normandye might take hym cōming towardes englande yet neuertheleſſe earle eſcaped daungers landed ſafe menne dartmouth frome whiche place ſayled fraunce halfe yere earle came lande made proclamacion king henry vi name lawfull age ſhoulde make battayle agaynſt edwarde duke yorke whiche agaynſte ryghte lawe tyme crowne whiche doon cannot ſpoken howe ſoone went aboute ye realme come made proclamacy whiche alſo expreſſed howe many thouſandes menne came hym earle hauing power greate armie went ſtreyght london whome edwarde perceyued drawe nighe fledde tyme truſtyng haue hym ſome vauntage laſte dryuen ende mynde get hoſte reſyſt enemy beyng greate daunger owne lyfe fled wt duke glouceſtre brother vnto towne night ſea called lye taking ſhippe ſayled flaunders charles newe going awaye kyng edward made haſte london hearing tumulte buſyneſſe kente village ſuburbes ſpoyled piteouſly lytel going awaye yt kyng pacified theim ſette thinges good ordre agayne whiche benefyte louingly accepted theim doon came towre deliuered kyng henry vi priſone geuing hym robe maieſ • ye broughte hym poules people reioyſing euery ſyde thanked god chaunſed wolde deſired yere lorde iiii c foure ſcore one kyng henry beganne reigne king henry ſo often vanquyſhed began reigne nowe likely ſhortely faule againe fortune chaunſed hym many mennes opinion becauſe ſimple innocent man yt rather godlineſſe vertue excell honoure rule ſo yt loue yt religion loked dignitee honoure whiche chaunſeth fewe wil ſeke regard kepe haue enemy ſaide coward herte manlyneſſe bee kyng meete offyce ſoeuer deſpiſeth cōmune people alloweth maruaileth accompted mad man contrariwyſe yt doeth agree theim tale wiſe man dede ſuche wiſdom comēly ſaide fooliſhneſſe god alſo ſome ſaide god yt ſhould ſo bee graundfather henry fourth gotte violencye force armes ſo yt coulde bee longe enioyed hym faute graundeſire redounde nephewes nowe yt matter king henry held parlyament weſtmynſter xxvi daye nouembre whiche edwarde declared openly tray toure coūtree bycauſe taken yt crowne goodes geuen away like maner al yt take parte ſo iudgement geuen theim dye furthermore yt decree ſtatutes actes yt forenamed edward broken none effecte yt earle warwike man yt deſerued much coūtre made gouernoure ouer yt realme whō take ye duke clarence felowe hym yt meanes yt realme brought new ſtate cleane tranſformed altered parliament came lorde marque mountacute excuſing treaſon yt take kyng edward parte ſaing feare death pardone▪ truely yf man taken kyng edwardes part ſtand ſide manly ſo ſore enemie hurted ſo much frendes falſe fained coloured frende thoſe thinges ware knewe bee pernicious dooe leſſe hurte v nowe quene margarete fraunce prayed euery daye time earle went england victorie whiche ſhe knewe obteined king letter came ſhortely take ſhyppe towardes england thorowe yt ſharpneſſe wether greate tempeſtes ſhe conſtrayned lande differre iourney tyme ſame tyme gaſpar earle penbruch went wale earledome founde lorde henry earle richemonde brother ſonne chylde ten yere olde kepte pryſoner lyke noble man ye erle willyam harberte wyfe whome ſpake edwarde made hym erle taken batayl behedded cōmaundement earle warwike henry whiche richard king 〈◊〉 • 〈◊〉 vii thirde brother edward ouercome vanquiſhed gouernaunce realme whome bee beleued came kingdō ſent one god quench put awaye greate ſedicion ſtryfe betwixte henry edwarde ſeyng minded nothyng ſo muche whome lady margarete onely doughter iohn fyrſte duke somerſet dyd bryng beyng fourtene yeres age whiche althoughe ſhe maryed henry duke bucking ham ſonne earle derby yet ſhe neuer broughte chylde thought ſhe doone parte ſhe hadde borne manne chylde ſame kynge realme gaſper earle penbruch tooke thys chylde henrye earle harberte hys wife brought hym ſoone london king henry ſyxte whome kynge beeholded longe holding hys peace maruailing goodlye wytte chylde ſayde thys wyſe noble tyme preſent loo thys thys ſaye whome wee oure aduerſaries ſhall geue place prophecye henrye vi kyng henry vii poſſeſſion thys prophecied ſelf ſame henry ſhuld tyme come chaunſed dede haue kyngedome rule realme nowe edwarde althoughe oute countree yet dyd dyſpayre ſhulde haue mattre redy occaſion recouer kingdome duke burgoyne partlye promiſed hym greate ayde ſocoure partly priuy frendes englande dyd councell hym letter ſente tyme time yt would haſten iournay homward incontin • tly many fled hym oute englande eyther feare lawes offended elles ſorowe worlde ſo turned could haue theyr wyll accomplyſhynge theyr couetouſe myndes deſyres cauſed hym make haſte homewarde kynge edwarde beynge rauiſhed golden promiſes thoughte nothyng payneful wretched tary one daye lenger nothyng pleaſaunt thē go iourney ſo takynge moo wyth two thou ſande harneſed menne ſprynge yeare ſayled englande landynge coaſtes yorkeſhyre hauen towne called rauinſport ſettynge hys menne dyd reaſon wyth hys captaynes conſulte place ſhoulde fyrſte goo ieoperdious conſydering ſmall companie take anye waye longe delyberation agryed ſome certayne knightes horſemen ſmal compaignie ſhuld bee ſent one euerie quarter townes wer nyghe intente myghte drawe harte myndes people king edwardes ſyde lykelye kynge edwarde beyng wyſe manne durſt bolde would wyſe come england ſuch ſmall power excepte knowen ſurely ſhould haue great helpe hys commyng whych plain token duke clarence lorde marque procured hys fauoure promyſinge helpe coulde make tryall whych ther manifeſt token dyſcloſed bewrayed falſhed priuilie wēt know mennes mindes parte would declyne nexte day came kinge edwarde ſhewed common people dyd ſtande ſtiflye kynge henrye ſyde woulde defende hys quarell ryghte iuſte al time nomore nede nowe make anye tumulte ſo much manne would althoughe eftſons deſired prayed go king edward yea noman woulde feare earle warwike heare anye thinge ſpoken matter whoſe myndes kinge edwarde throughlye ſerched knowen chaunged mynd purpoſe wher claymed crowne publyrſhed abrode woulde haue hys ryghte landes heritage yorke ſhyre • worde cannot well ſpoken howe redily mē wer willinge helpe conſideringe claymed nothinge hys ryghte ſomuch y• pytie dyd moue manye althoughe woulde helpe hym yet hande reſyſte kynge edwarde reconſilyng ſelfe common people theſe meanes toke hys iournye towarde yorke wente beuer lay earle beinge warwik knew yt king edward landed york ſtreyght ſent poſt brother lord mōtacute liyng winter pomfreit wt great army ſhewe daunger mighte enſue yf king edward got yt towne york bed theim yf enemy drewe nigh ether mete thē plain felde elles bete theim towne vnto ſuch tyme came wyth greater hoſt prepared haſt coulde becauſe knew ſurely way enemy wolde come fyrſt ſent euery towne york ſhyre yorke ſelfe certayne poſtes bid euery man harneſſe ready yt citezins ſhould ſhut gate ſurelye kynge edward myght haue acceſſe meane tyme king edward came peaceably wythoute reſiſtaunce anye man towardes towne yorke whoſe commyng citezens certified made ſure gate ſtandynge harneſſe defence dyd ſende twoo alderman warne kyng comming nyghe dooe enterpryſe farre put hym ſelfe ieopardie mynded dryue hys awaye wyth power myghte edwarde heard theyr myndes ſo greate feare agonie could tell dooe yf ſhuld haue goone back feared common people men gredye praye woulde perſue yf ſhould goo forth daunger yorke ſhyre men leaſte ſhoulde ſodenlye faull vpon hym take hym therefore ſeeyng able match battayle thought mollyfie theim fayre wordes ſo beganne entreat moſt lowlye gentle maner meſſaungers woulde hys name ſhewe cytezyns came clayme crowne hys herytage ryghte yorke ſhyre therfore woulde helpe theyr lorde duke yorke yf myghte receaued theyr meanes wolde requyte theyr kindenes remember theyr benifyte longe lyued ſuche fayre ſpeaking flatterie dimiſſed thē folowed ſtraighte gate companie citezins beynge ſomwhat moued wyth thys anſwer entended harme agaynſt kyng henrie ſpake wyth hym wall badde hym go frome thence would go quickely ſhould take harme ſpeakyng veraye gentely euerye one theim callyng ſome name mooſt gentely deſire theim yt might come owne toune ſo paſſyng daye cōmunicacion yt length citezens partely ouer come wt mooſt gētle ſpeakyng large promiſes made fell poincte yt edward would ſwere handle citezens gentle ſorte hereafter bee obedient kyng henry cōmaundement thei would receiue hym yt citee helpe hym wt yt power thei might edward beyng glad next daye early maſſe ſaid ye gate wher receiuyng ſacrament promiſed feithfully vpon othe yt would obſerue bothe thyngēs afore named ſo receiued citee neuertheleſſe ſo ferre vnlike would obſerue one theim minded none thyng yt might depriue kyng croune ſhall appere euidēt yt oftē tymes ſe noble men aſwell laye people thorowe ambicion filthy couetouſnes thei forgettyng god godlynes dooe ſwere greate othes promiſyng thynges ye whiche entendyng thei make othe breake ſhortely yet ſuche perſons oftymes haue rewardes god one tyme edward ſo ſome tyme puniſhment falleth nephewes offence vncle cōmitted thyng ſpeake rychard third place wher manne maye ſee ye progenie edward wer puniſhed offence edward thus framed matter forgettyng ye othe yt made ſe yt citee ſtrōgly kepte gettyng hym army together thought wold lynger buſines bycauſe harde enemy made greate preparaūce haſte tooke iourney towarde london goyng purpoſely goo waye yt led hym pomfret wher ye lord marque toke yt right hand within leſſe thē iiii mile enemy whē perceiued yt thei made ſkyrmiſhe mocion came right waie paſt theim wēt notynghame greued yorke ſhire mēne ſhould deceiue theim ſo vnhoneſtly otherwiſe become kyng noble manne knowen kyng edward came wt daunger enemy notyngham came hym many noble mēne vpon conſideracion yt lord moū tacute either would entre vpō enemy though agreed theim el durſt come tentes able matche wt theim therfore menne thought better take edwardes part conſideryng yt power ſo greate hold kyng henry hee daunger liues loſſe goodes landes edward reioyſyng went leceſtre hearyng therle toune warwicke therle oxenford hym hauyng greate armie thei bothe entended bryng hym theim preuentyng purpoſe wet awaye wt hooſt either wyllyng fight el ioyne frendeſhip loue brother duke clarence whome commyng frō london wt hooſt mēne thought ſpeake yt came therle cōpaignie fearyng leſte yt would ſtand yt promiſe yt made yt variable incōſtāt ye meane tyme therle warwike heuie ſore moued wt ye lord marque becauſe would neither kepe kyng yorke bed yet thei came noſe would proffer theim one fight therfore cōſideryng yt enemy multiplied gooyng towardes hym made hooſt ſent yt duke clarence come hym hauyng hooſt london whō whē perceiued linger man doubtyng whether ſhould kepe battaill peace haue mind ſettyng forth mē miſtruſting alſo yt ſome traine allured folowe brother take partes tooke waye couētrie thende might meete enemy edward came warwike frome then erle pitched tentes hym next daie bad battaill therle whiche erle durſt come oute feare duke clarence whome thought deceaued hym duke deede came ſhewed greate power menne whiche edward perceaued made towardes hym ſhould bee thought bee made guyle ſette hooſt araye though would fight ſo duke thei came ſight richard duke glouceſtre one ſhould take vp matter firſte ſpake duke priuely eare came edward ſame hym laſte peace proclaimed wherby euery manne puttyng doune weapon edward brethrē enbraced louyngly one edward made bee proclaimed yt duke theim came hym ſhould bee perpetuall frendes thei three ſhould loue like thre brother thei wer brotherly loue euer neuer theleſſe god dooeth ſeme haue forgiuē edward offēce periury although euē nowe fortune fauored hym yer long vexed wt werre beſide yt plage diſtruciō child death thei wer thus come together thei minded proue yt erle wold come theim alſo hold wt theim whō ye duke clarēce ſēt certain frendes yt whiche firſt ſhuld excuſe yt done thē deſire hym yt would bee one kyng edward whoſe mynde whē therle heard vtterly deteſted hym muche curſyng cryed oute hym yt contrary feith othe made fled kyng edward cōmaūdemēt biddyng yt ſēt made none aunſwer rather bee like hym ſelf thē like falſe periured duke yt appoincted vtterly neuer leaue battaill either wer killed ded enemy ouercomed edward hauyng ſuche ſtrong power mēne went boldely london wher knowen duke clarence taken parte brother come one knot citezens ſuche feare thei could tell dooe lengthe dryuen feare take kyng edward parte theſame tyme came letter earle kyng henry yt duke somerſet yt archbyſhop yorke kyng counſel yt ſhould kepe citee enemy handes ſpace ij iij dayes would come ſtreyght great armye mēne defended citee ſtrongely coulde purpoſe citezens cōſyderyng ye kyng henry greate warryer yt ſmall policie feates theſame contrary wiſe kyng edwarde man hym ſelfe coulde rule realme maruelous well ſuche man woulde onelye preſerue hym ſelfe alſo defende theim maner iniuryes harmes ſhoulde chaunce thought beſt leane ſyde commyng london people coulde thretenyng ſtrayt cōmaundement otherwyſe kepte backe would mete hym comyng ſalute hym altogether kyng ruler realme whoſe commynge duke somerſet certayn fled away made beſte ſhifte euery manne hym ſelfe could eſcape hādes ſauyng kyng hē ry taryed poſte alone biſhoppes paleyce beſyde powles ſtandynge lyke deſperate manne knowynge dooe taken kyng edward caſt pryſon agayn towre edward came london xi day apryll halfe yere hadde ſayled flaunders callyng councel together highly commende citezens yt faythfulneſſe bare hym eſpeciall alderman yt cauſed people obeyſaūce hym alſo ſharpelye rebuked cytie knewe haue lent monye kyng henry yt cauſe woulde haue made theim paye mony preparyng hoſte hym laſt bad theim bee without feare promyſyng theim pardon ſafetie life thorowe whiche gentleneſſe gatte fauoure cōmen people wonderfully erle conſideryng battayll ſhould ſhortelye folowed enemyes great haſte entente yf enemy ſtoppe lette yt waye myght fight buckel theim came lō dō purſued theim long came good waye iourney worde brought yt edwarde gottē london impriſoned kyng earle perceauyng victorie ende fightyng ſhould tryed one batayle reſted ſaynt albones partely refreſhe men partely take ſome counſayl hoſte duke exceſter earle oxenforde duke somerſet lorde mountacute marque brother earle earle perceaued bee vnwyllyng fight agaynſt kyng edward therfore truſt hym yet loue yt betwixte brother brother diminiſhed ſuſpicion whatſoeuer thought eyther hym hymſelfe euer feare daunger ſo came ſaynt albones toune halfe waye betwyxte london aboute tenne myle frome london called barnet toune ſtandeth hyll goodlye playne earle entended pitche battayle edward hearyng prepared armye adioyned greate power young menne theim ſo bowes bylles ſpeares arowes maner inſtrumentes apperteynyng warre ſo furnyſſhed menne thought make riddaūce theim tyme fyniſhe battayle ſo longe holden ſo came armye mete enemy might bee redier fight theim whereſoeuer mette theim foure wynges could eſcape hym hand brought hym battayle alſo henry priſoner entente aduerſaries might bee diſcouraged ſight hym el fortune fauoured hym might neuertheleſſe bee ſaued noone pytched tentes fore named barnet nighe hys enemyes myghte fyghte daye defended hys tentes veraye ſtrongelye longer taryed better reaſon daylye concourſe noble men commen people hym woorſe earle farre frendes lodged night breake day ye earle warwike begā araye armye ſorte fyrſte lorde marque earle oxenforde ſet lefte ſyde wyth certayn horſſemen hymſelfe duke exceter ryght ſyde myddeſte betwixte theim bothe ſetteth duke somerſet archer thus araiyng theim battayl beganne exhorte theim thei would fight luſtely lyke hardye meune reuengyng quarell countree moſte falſely poſſeſſed yt croune like maner kyng edward whiche ſet theim ordre encouraged theim fight lykewyſe remembre thei inuaded rebelles traytours ſedicious perſons whiche entended nothynge vtter deſtruccion loſſe theyr countree daye came trompettes beganne blowe bothe ſydes token ligne battayle firſte bowe men ſhot drawynge nere tryed ſweorde edwarde truſtyng thorowe multitude mē haue better hād ſtāde ſtiffely theim enbouldenyng ſouldiours coulde whoſe power erle moſte manfully reſiſted ſo long cōtinuaunce battail many men wer ſlayne whoſe place ſucceded euer freſher freſher length erle perceauyng mē bee ouerthrowen kyng great power drewe nigh foreward conſtreyned kyng geue backe litle edward ſeeyng brought freſhe men aide ye ſo thother mē wer beten downe ſore ye groūde edwarde beeyng werye longe fyghtynge fought mornyng none cauſed theim wer without battayl ſtandyng defēce edward yf ſuch nede ſhould fall vpō enemy beare theim downe wt great power erle ſeyng freſhe mē come vpō theim nothing afeard truſting loking ſurely victorye dyd comforte encourage menne almoſte diſcomfited mooſt manfully deſiring theim beare oute laſte brunt luſtely victorie ſhould redounde theim weryed longe continuaunce nothing moued wordes ſelf moſte valiauntly came among myddeſt enemyes kylled ſlewe many theim hym ſelfe laſte ſtriken downe brother lorde marque folowing hym whoſe deathe fled ſo taken moſte parte theim ende earle whoſe ſtouteneſſe ſtomack made hym bee lyke peryll leopardye many time dyuerſe ſundrye ſuche conflictes warres killed partes ten thouſande menne ſo many taken priſoners could noumbred duke somerſet earle oxforde entendyng take waye scotlande dyd chaunge mindes bicauſe ſo farre frō theim fledde ſtreight wale earle penbrucke ſo euery man ſaue liues fledde ſome one way ſome erle exeter ſkaping hardely tooke ſentuarye weſtminſter remayned edward gotte victorye went london mooſt triumphyng faſſion hauyng henry hym priſoner deed corp alſo earle lorde marque brought poules laye ſpace ii dayes euery manne might ſee theim bee deed man fainyng yt aliue myght ſowe ſedicion againe reuenging quarel yet kyng ſo glad ye death therle ſory loſſe deſtruccion yt lord marque whome dyd eſteme take great frende quene margaret hearing yt edward come englande done much hurte yt realme purpoſed come england ſoonne alſo prince edward wt great armye choſen picked frenchman ſo land waimouth yt greate tempeſt yt ſee ſhe could come ſo ſoone ſhe woulde ſhe landed heard kyng edward conquered huſband takē priſoner deſtitute frendes ye erle brother lord marque ſlaine felde army diſcomfyted ſlayne putte f • ight ſhe began like piteful deſperate ladye mourne lament fate calamitee huſband ye whiche ſhe nowe ſee haue chaūſed ſowith great feare agonie ſhe caſe ſhe rather dye lyue quene mighte haue thought yt euell chaunſed putting death ye duke glouceſtre whoſe deathe althoughe peraduēture ſhe giltie yet ſhe offended ſhe dyd ſaue ſuche good man yf liued dominion publike weale king henry neuer ſuche trouble nowe leaue yt quene deſpering bothe owne life ſōnes alſo went therby monaſtery charterhouſe monkes place called bewe lieu engliſhe called faire place ther taking ſentuarie remained ſoonne knowen ſhe ſentuarie came duke somerſet brother erle deuonſhire whiche man euen frome beginnyng taken parte whoſe returning redounded euell deſtruccion alſo erle penbroke ihon wen locke ihon longſtrother capytaines ruler rhodes quene ſorowe miſerye ſomwhat comforted ſighte frendes wt whome ſhe talked ſhewed cauſe yt ſhe came rather deſiryng theim prouyde ſafegard ſoonne helpe nowe ye ſhe would wether ſerued goo fraunce againe bryng wt god willing better mature time greater power mē duke began putte good comforte would wiſe ye ſhe ſhould ſet mind whole vpon batail nowe fight againſt edward whē bothe vnprepared alſo furnyſhed men yt hable fight conſidering ye great batell wt therle warwike yt men ſore hurted weryed together yt myght chaūce haue yt better hym although diſcōfyted therle hoſte becauſe yt victorie turneth oftentymes one momēt ſhort ſpace furthermore ſhewed ye moſt part yt nobilyte bare theyr good mindes hertes kyng henry ſo bee yt ſhe would bee capitaine ſhe bene tyme paſſed promiſed great army owne coſtes charge woulde make noble menne take parte defende time quene miſtruſting fearing yet muche owne ſoonne aunſwered ſaied ſhe allowed counſell well yf ſo ſhe might bee daunger ſonne therfore fearing fought moſt earneſtly countree ſoonne might bee deſtroied caſte awaye ſhe thought beſt either putte differre battayl time elles ſende ſoonne fraunce bee kepte vnto ſuche tyme ye ſome better ſucceſſe warres truely mother withoute cauſe ſo louing chylde owne huſbande priſoner captiue perſone therfore one caſte awaye ſo nexte hym ſhe loued mooſte tenderly ſoonne alſo might goo yt wiſely aboute entente quene counſayled theim laye heedes together caſte way howe conuey buſineſſe yf would fight ſhe promiſed theim helpe good councell erle ſaied nede waſte wordes woulde fight ſtoutely agaynſte enemy therfore woulde doo might power determined apointed vpon gathered armye euery manne parte oute owne countree ſhire quene brought good hope warre ſaied wel ſtreight went yt councell yt duke bathe looking tarieng armye place ſo euer ſhe went ſhe would aknowen none thentent yt aduerſaries might knowe vnto ſuch time ſhe came wher ſhe woulde bee edward hearyng quene come duke somerſet prepared hooſt ayde ſente certayne ſpies viewe number armye ſhewed hym nomber yet knowyng whether wold goo kyng apoynted mete came london gathering armie went oxforde ſhyre pytched hys tentes abyngton encreaſinge hys nomber army much could perceauyng wer bathe taryed purpoſely multyply enlarge company came malebrydge xv myles frome bathe ſo haſted come thē go wale ſuſpected whether dede thei entended erle penbruck hauyng theyr great bonde men toune bathe quene fled frome thence bryſtowe wyllinge goo glouceter ſent ſpyes knowe yf ſhe myght haue paſſage whome aunſwere broughte ſhe coulde thei towne would anye meanes geue place ſhe hearynge went briſtowe teukiſbury ther duke pytched hys battayle agaynſt wyll aduiſe many captaynes whych counſayled hym tarye erle penbruches comyng edwarde dyd take quene kylled leaſt impryſoned euery one almooſt came nobilitee killed earle deuonſhyre iohn wenlock captayn rhodes brother duke somerſet wyth manye moo taken priſoners quene margaret ſōnne prince edward yt duke somerſet yt lord ſ ihons xx knyghtes beſyde thē theſe wer behedded ii dayes yt ſelfe ſame towne ſauyng quene margaret ſoonne edwarde shortelye prynce edwarde brought kyng aſked wherfor inuade hys realme anſwered boldly ſayde recouer kyngedome heritage forefather progenie dew wordes edwarde ſayde nothyng thruſtyng hym hys ſyght wyth hys hande whō duke clarence glouceter yt lorde haſtynges dyd kyll mooſte cruelly hys departyng hys mother quene caryed london pryſoner frō thence raunſomed fraunce ſhe lyued perpetuall ſorowe care ſo much ſelfe huſband onely ſonne edwarde whome ſhe henry huſband truſted ſhould lyue poſſeſſe ye croune kinge edward thus ouercome theim went london ther iii dayes cauſed proceſſion bee euerye place mooſt ſolempne deuoute faſſy laſt ciuile battaile king kept yere lord iiii c lxxx xi kynge edwarde returned backe ſubduynge hys rebelles one fauconbrydge earle kente hys baſterde ſtoute harted manne beynge admyrall ſea none ſhoulde paſſe betwixte calyſſe douer ayde ſocoure kynge edwarde appoyntemente earle warwyke dryuen nede pouertee beganne bee pyrate rouer ſeea ſo much throughe robberye ſhamefull ſpoylynge gotte vnto hym greate nauye ſhyppes laſte landed kente getting hym greate multitude kentyſhemenne wyth aſſiſtence theim hys ryotouſe compaignye ſhyppemenne came london ſayde wyth lowde voyce woulde defende kynge henrye reſtore hym hys crowne people cytezyns london perceauyng quene margarete ouercome battayle woulde geue theim paſſage wyth greate myghte vyolence enforſed fawconbrydge geue backe take ſhyppe kylled toke pryſoners better parte menne shortely ſame fauconbridge landing vnware southampton taken behedded wīdeſore caſtell laied ye newe chapell ſ george ſolēpne toumbe henry reigned xxviii yere repoſſeſſed kyngdome halfe yeare lyued vnto lii yeres age wife quene margaret one ſoōne called edward nowe ſcottes peace amitee bee obſerued kepte yt 〈…〉 xx yeares yet feare y• 〈…〉 e pēbruck richemond wer ye duke britain wher thei mooſt honorable intretainmēt cōſideryng alſo yt young erle richemōd would clayme ye croune ī tyme come ye feare ye whiche matter ſent priuie ambaſſadours ye duke promiſyng hym yt would reſtore deliuer vnto hāde bothe therles ſhould haue ample large porciō monye ſo dooyng yt duke make ſhort tale would meanes deliuer theim handes ſo kepte theim thei neuer might bee daūger enemy hym edward therfore thirtene yere reigne whiche yere lord thouſand foure hundred three ſcore thirteen helde parlyament weſtminſter wher firſt cauſed ſtatutes actes whiche wer abrogated henry ſixt ſtand bee good effecte goodes theſe traitours beſtowed gyuen abrode alſo baniſhed menne yt fled rebelles falſe countree bee brought grudge eiuill wer betwixt one nobilite ther ſhould bee forgottē turned loue laſtly certain mony ſhould bee payed kyng towardes yt greate charge werre thus ſtudied determined liue quietly ſet realme good ordre charles ye duke burgoin ſēt aide hym againſt lewes ye frēche kyng ſo yt could neuer bee reſt one thyng ſhuld diſquiet hym could deny hym helpe conſideryng ye benefites yt receiued hym diuerſe ſūdry tymes yt yt nowe fought againſt dedly enemie whiche aided erle warwike bothe wt menne mony come againſt hym wherfore aſſēblyng coūſaill together ſhewyng theim matter ſent woord duke yt would kepe one piece parte battail agaīſt ye kyng deede yt ſame tyme mortall battaill betwixt duke lewes yt kyng becauſe ſame lewes harde manne churliſhe alſo hurtefull aſwell frēdes foe many frēchmen abhorryng cōdicions conſent hold yt duke emong many one lewes lucēburge apoinct wt duke dooe miſchief hym one waye ſo yt kyng bothe daūger owne coūtree menne alſo duke beyng ſtraūger duke ſhewed kyng edward yt might ſoner allu • e entiſe hym battaill vpō kyng edward toke voiage fraūce takyng beſides tribute yt certain mony ye lordes common realme thei owne gētlenes gaue vn hym ye ſuſtenaūce maintenyng armie yt kyng called tribute leuiyng mony beneuolēce whiche neuertheleſſe giuen wt eiuill many one vſyng ſuche gētle faſſions towardes theim praiyng theim ſo hartely aſſiſtaunce yt thei could none wiſe dooe geue hym whiche whē gathered armie whiche xx went caleys ye iiii daye july whō charles yt duke mett reioyſyng gretely victory inſtantly deſire hym would ſticke ſtoutely battaill yt might haue yt frenche kyng yt loſt hym lewes yt kyng hard edward came wt armie encreaſed nombre people muche could nigher daunger ſooner haſtely came vpon theim armie ſent foorthe robert stoteuill noble capitain cooſtes atrebatium reſyſt power engliſhe menne kyng hym ſelf taried siluanect caſtyng wt hymſelf waye might make league peace betwixt yt duke yt kyng england hym heryng therfore yt king gone atrebates ſēt ambaſſodours hym peace whoſe myndes yt kyng knowē although foūd litle frēdſhip hādes tymes paſt yet conſideryng yt ſubſtaūce treaſure waſted ciuile battail hable maintein newe hooſt nede ſhuld yet vnneth ſuſtein theim vnder bāner thought beſt euē pure neceſſite leaue peace growe atonemēt wt lewes yt kyng whiche thyng might dooe alſo ſauing honour cōſideryng yt bothe ye duke robert lucēburge aforenamed dooē accordyng promiſe yt deſire ye ambaſſadours went ſpeake kyng pinquinake toune ambiā ſhire wher noble mēne dooe aſſēble together found y• kyng thē bothe yt kynges due ſalutaciō either long communicaciō laſt peace cōfirmed ſtabliſhed many yeres ye •• emēt wherof ye frēche kyng gaue vnto edward toward charge coſt lxcv crounes thēs forth yerely l crounes yt truce made mony paid kyng edward wēt caleis thēs englād battaill none ſlain ſauyng onely yt duke exceter ye whiche māne ſētuary cōmaunded folowe y• kyng put death cōtrary yt promiſe made yere lord cccc lxxv frome tyme foorth lewes yt kyng payed duely raunſome edward vnto laſte yere dyed tyme denyed paymente though knewe laſte dayes duke burgoyne roberte lucenburgh knowen edwarde made league wyth lewes kynge freted ſore hym wrote ſharpe letter thretenyng tauntyng hym ſaiyng cauſe reuenged theimſelfes kyng whoſe fyrye thundryng wordes kyng paſſed vpon turnyng hāde lucenburgh taken pryſoner proude malicious writyng behedded lutece thus kyng edward beyng quietnes countre abrode alſo although mighte wel thynke hymſelf lyue ſo perpetually yt ſo great conquerour yet conſideryng yt erle richemōde nigh affinitee hē ry vi feare daunger therfore thought one attempte duke britayn agayn giftes promyſes faire wordes might haue y• erle whō thought rule would aunceſtrie geuen ambaſſadours came duke great ſubſtaunce mony requeſt might bee honeſtier ſhewed duke came deſire erle hym mighte marye kynges doughter ſo affinite al euil wyll grudge might forgotten ſedicion vtterlye reiected although entended ſo cauſe al ſuche thynges bee forgotten death kyllyng hym duke longe muche deniyng theim laſte thorowe muche entreatyng alſo great rewardes brought gaue earle theim ſendynge letter kynge prayſe commendation hym thynkynge commytted lambe woulfe ſoonne father ambaſſadours verye glad got hym edward two yeres folowing kyng died ye whiche yeres beganne bee harde couetouſe getting monye alſo diligent marking attaching lordes offend time kyng scottes willed ſoōne iamy maried kynges doughter lady cicile yonger ſhould haue maried charles kyng ſoonne fraunce chaunced thorow lewes kyng brake promiſe bothe geuing ſeruice payeng raunſome laſte yere reigne likewiſe kyng scottes ſeing lewes kyng fraūce ther counſailed ye kyng fight againſt hym king willing reuēge olde iniuries vpon many conſideraciōs gathered entēded leſſe ye helpe ſaied duke albany kepe open warre yt ſend duke glouceſtre ye erle northumberlād ſyr thomas stanley duke albany wt great power men againſt ye scottes king knowing cōming went barwyke army kepe theim border perceiuing hable ſo reſiſt great power fled backe ye night edinbrough ther taryed enemy ye duke glouceſtre folowing burned ſpoyled way ſomewhat nighe enemy perceiuing alſo none scottiſhe lordes came duke albanye miſtruſted ſome deceyte crafte wrought ſo laboured haue peace whiche gotten went backe caſtell barwike ſir thomas stanley wonne lytell duke albany ye authoure warre yt lytle thankes england ſo dooing fled fraunce kylled running tylte parys buſineſſe edward aſſembled counſell together willed theim prepare batayle againſte frenche kyng neyther payde woulde paye raunſome yet geue ſoonne mariage doughter promiſed ſetting forth ye batayl yere oure lorde cccc lxxxiij xxij yere lewes xi frenche kyng whiche younge prince reigned ſmal ſpace lytle ſeaſon ouer realme pleaſure libertee vncle richard duke gloceter within iij monethes depriued hym croune regalytie alſo vnnaturally bereft hym naturall life declaracion craftie engine firſt attempted vngracious purpoſe falſe colourable vntrue allegaciōs ſet forth openly pretenſed enterpriſe fynally ſhamefull cruell deteſtable acte perfourmed ſame ye muſte fyrſt conſyder brother deſcended nature condicions inclynacions thē ſhall eaſely perceaue could crueller tyraunt appoynted acheue abomynable enterpryſe father richard plantagenet duke yorke whiche began warre lawe chalenge croune englande puttyng clayme parliamēt holden yt xxx yere kyng henry vi ether right fauoure cauſe ſo ſet forthe auaunced bloodde ſayd kyng henry although goodly ſonne clerely abiected yt croune realme autorytee parliamente entayled duke yorke heyres diſceaſe ſayd kyng henrye vi duke entendyng ſo long tary myndyng vnder preterte diſcencion growen aryſen within realme couenauntes made parliament kepte broken preuēte tyme take vpon hym gouernaunce kyng henryes life muche hardynes ſlayne battayle wakefylde leuynge behynde hym three ſonnes edwarde george richard al theſe three wer greate eſtates byrth ſo greate ſtatelye ſtomake gredy autoritee impaciēt parteners rule autoritee edward reuēged father death depoſed kyng henry vi atteyned croune ſceptre realme george duke clarence goodlye well feautured prince thynges fortunate yf ether owne ambiciō ſet againſt brother thenuie enemy ſet brother agaynſt hym quene ye noble bloode highly maligned kynges kynred woman cōmenlye malyce nature hate ſuche theyr huſbandes loue wer aproude appetite duke hym ſelfe entendyng bee kyng leaſte wiſe heynous treaſon layde charge finally faute fauteleſſe attaynted parliament iudged deathe thereupon haſtely drouned butte malmeſey within ye towre londō whoſe death kyng edward although commaunded wyſte done pyteouſlye bewayled ſorowfullye repented richard duke glouceſtre iij ſonne whiche muſte mooſte entreate deſcripciō richarde thyrde witte courage eguall beautee lyniamentes nature farre vnderneth lytle ſtature euill feautered lymmes croke backed lift ſhulder much higher right harde fauoured vyſage ſuche eſtates called warlike vyſage amonge commen perſons crabbed face malycious wrothfull enuyous reported mother duches much dooe trauayle yt ſhe could delyuered hym vncutte came worlde fete forwarde men borne outwarde fame ranne vntothed whether men hatred reported aboue truthe yt nature chaunged courſe begynnyng life many thynges vnnaturally cōmytted leue goddes iudgemēt none euell capitayn warre whiche diſpoſicion enclyned peace sōdry victory ſome ouerthrowes neuer defaute owne perſon either lacke hardynes polytike order fre diſpences ſomwhat aboue power lyberall wt large giftes gatte hym vnſtedfaſt frēdſhip whiche cauſe fayn borowe pil extorte place gat hym ſtedfaſt hatred cloſe ſecrete depe dyſſymuler lowly coūtenaūce arrogāte herte outwardly famylyer inwardly hated lettyng kyſſe whome thought kyll diſpiteous cruell alwaye eiuyll wyll ambycion ſerue purpoſe frende fooe wer indifferent auaū tage grewe ſpared mānes death whoſe lyfe withſtode purpoſe ſlewe towre kyng henry vi ſaiyng nowe heyre male kyng edward thyrde houſe yorke whiche murder done without kynge edwardes aſſent whiche would haue appoynted bocherlye office ſome rather owne brother wiſe mē alſo wene yt hys drift lacked helpyng forth owne brother clarence death whiche thyng apparaunce reſiſted although inwardly mynded cauſe thereof men notynge doynges procedynges marke becauſe longe kyng edwardes tyme thought opteyne croune caſe kyng brother whoſe life loked euyl dyet would ſone ſhorten ſhould happē diſeaſe dede chyldrē beyng yoūg yt duke clarence lyued pretenſed purpoſe farre hyndered yf duke clarence kept hym ſelf true nephewe yong kyng would haue takē vpō kyng euery one theſe caſtes troumpe duke glouceſters waye ſure hys brother clarence dead knewe might woorke without ieopardye theſe poyntes certentie whoſoeuer deuyneth cōiectureth maye well ſhote ferre ſhorte cōiecture afterward toke place fewe dooe ſhall ꝑceaue afore declare howe rychard duke glouceſtre began miſcheuous imagened pretenced enterpriſe apꝑantly ſhalbe opened muſt litle putte remēbraūce louyng charitable acte leſſe profitable thē amiable yt whole cōmynaltie ſo inwardely thought outwardly diſſimuled whiche kyng edward liyng deathe bedde long dyed life althoughe deuiſion emongeſt frendes ſomewhat greued yrked hym yet helth leſſe regarded tooke hede reaſon yt thought yt hable thynges rule bothe ꝑties thei neuer ſo obſtinate laſt ſickeneſſe whiche cōtinued longer falſe fantaſticall tale haue vntruly falſely ſurmiſed ſelf wrote pamphlet truly knew whē perceiued natural ſtrēgth gone hoped litle recouery artes al phicyſyans whiche perceaued onely prolong life thē meanes pleaſed hym beſt ſhall fal fartheſt fauour ſo yt ye lēgth euell driftes driue naught good plain wayes ꝓſper floriſhe great variaūce hath euer beē betwene alwais great cauſes tyme thyng right wel entēdid miſcōſtrued hath turned yt woorſe ſmal diſpleaſure dooē ether owne affeciō ether inſtigaciō eiuill toōges hath ſore agrauate wot well neuer ſo great cauſe hatred haue loue becauſe affinite whiche yt ſpirituall affinitie kynred chriſt ꝑtakers yt ſacamentes chriſtes churche weight whiche cōſanguynite beare would god ſhould moued ſpirituall charite fleſhly cōſanguinyte lord ambiciō deſire vanyne glory ſouere ingtie whiche emōgeſt eſtates entered crepith foorth ſo ferre till wt deuiſion varyaunce turneth miſchief firſt longyng bee next yt beſt afterward egall wt beeſt laſt chief aboue yt beeſt whiche immoderate appetite woorſhip debate diſcencion yt grewe loſſe ſorowe trouble hath win theſe fewe yeres growen realme praye god well forget well remēbre whiche thyng could aſwell haue forſene haue wt pane thē pleaſure proued god de bleſſed lady yt commō othe would neuer haue wonne curteſyes mennes knee loſſe ſo many heddes ſith thynges paſſed called agayn muche ought bee ware occaſion haue taken ſo great hurte eftſones fall yt occaſion nowe bee theſe greues paſſed quiet thanked bee god likely well proſper welthfull peace vnder couſins child god ſend theim life loue cō cord whiche ii thynges yt leſſe loſſe wer thei whō though god pleaſure yet ſhould realme alwayes fynd kynges ꝑaduētur good kynges thei emōgeſt ſelfes childes reigne fall debate many good manne ſhall innocently periſhe happely alſo long fynd peace quiet wherfore theſe laſt woordes yt euer looke ſpeake exhort require loue haue borne yt loue haue borne loue yt lord bereth v frō fiue doughters elizabeth goddes grace maryed kyng henry vii mother kyng hēry ye eyght cycile ſo fortunate fayre fyrſt wedded ye vycoūt welles one kyne lyued great wealth brydget profeſſed ſelfe tyme warre eche muſt others enemye yt ther neuer kyng realme attaynyng croune warre battayle ſo hartely beloued ſubſtaunce people hym ſelfe ſo ſpecially fauoured parte life yt tyme death whiche fauoure affeccion yet death crueltie myſchiefe trouble tempeſteous world folowed highlye towardes hym encreaſed ſuche time died diſpleaſure thoſe bare hym grudge kyng henry yt vi ſake whō depoſed wel aſſuaged effect quenched within yt ſpace xxii yeres great part man life ſome wer reconſiled growen fauour y• neuer ſtraūge true harte demaunded goodly perſonage princely beholde hert couragious politike councell aduerſitee nothyng abaſhed proſperitee rather ioyful proude peace iuſte mercyfull warre ſharpe fearce felde bold hardie yet neuer theleſſe farther reaſon policie woulde aduenture whoſe warres whoſoeuer circumſpectly 〈◊〉 aduiſedly conſidereth ſhal leſſe cōmend wiſdome policie auoyded theim manhode vanquiſhed theim viſage full faced louelie bodie mightie ſtronge cleane made ouer lyberall wātō dyet waxed ſomewhat corpulēt bourly neuertheleſſe vncomely youth greatly geuen fleſhely wantōnes yt health bodie great proſperitee fortune eſpeciall grace hardlye refrayneth dayes left al wild daliaūce fel grauitee ſo yt brought realme wealthie ꝓſperous eſtate al feare outwarde enemy clerely extinguiſhed warre hande none toward ſuche mā looked people wer toward prince cōſtrayned feare true louyng wylfull obedience emongeſt theimſelfe ye common wer good peace lordes whome knewe variaunce death bed thought brought good concord loue amytee lytle death left gatheryng mony ſubiectes whiche thyng draweth yt heartes englyſhmē frō kynges prynces nothyng ether entrepryſed ndr toke hād yt ſhuld dryuē thereunto tribute fraūce litle recouered obteyned yt yere dyed recouered toune berwike againſt yt kyng scottes albeit yt yt tyme reigne ſo benigne courteous famylyer parte vertues eſtemed thē thoſe high humilitees yet condycion thende laſt dayes decayed whiche many prince longe cōtinued ſouereingtie declyne proude porte behaueoure theyr condicions accuſtomed begynnyng yet lowlynes gentlenes ſo farre forth hym encreaſed ſōmer died beyng haueryng bowre ſente mayre aldermenne london thyther hunte make paſtyme made theim ſo hartie ſo famylyer frendlye chere ſent alſo theyr wyues ſuche plentie venyſon one thyng many dayes gatte hym eyther mo heartes hartie fauoure emongeſt commen people whiche often tymes eſteme take greate kyndnes lytle courteſye greate profyte benefyte ſo noble prynce deceaſſed haue hearde tyme lyfe mooſte deſyred whē people king edward died one called miſtelbrooke long ere daye ſprange came houſe one potier dwelling redcroſſe ſtrete withoute creple gate london haſtie rapping quickely let y• ſaied miſtelbrooke ſhewed vnto potier kyng edward yt nighte deceaſed trueth ꝙ potier wil maſter duke gloucetre kyng warrāt cauſe ſo thinke harde ſay whether ſeruaūt knewe ſuch thing prepenſed otherwiſe inklingther likelihode ſpake naughte nowe retourne trewe hiſtory wer duke gloucetre olde ſore practiſed concluſyon tyme moued therunto put hope tender age young prince nephewes oportunitee likely ſpede putteth manne courage neuer entended certen northe partyes good gouernaunce countrey aduertiſed brother deathe contriued deſtruccion nephewes yt vſurpacion roiall dignitee croune aſmuche well wyſte holpe maynteine long continued grudge harte burnynge betwene quenes kynred kynges bloodde either parte enuiyng others authorytee nowe thought dede fertherly beginning purſute entent ſure grounde ſituacion vnnaturall building might vnder pretence remēbring olde dyſpleaſures abuſe ignoraunce angre one partie deſtruccion yt wynne purpoſe many coulde ſuche coulde bee wonne might bee loſte looked therfore one thing certaine intent wer perceaued ſhould haue made peace betwene party owne bloodde intente kept ſecrete tyll knewe frendes ye whiche henry duke buckingham fyrſte yt ſent hym brother deathe truſty ſeruaunt called perſall cytee yorke duke gloucetre kepte kyng brother funeralles perſall came iohn ward ſecrete chaumberer duke gloucetre deſiryng cloſe couerte manier might ſpeake duke maiſter wherupō deed nyght duke ſente perſall beyng aduoyded whiche ſhewed duke gloucetre duke buckingham maiſter newe worlde would take ſuche parte woulde woulde farther wayte vpon hym good fellowes yf nede duke ſent backe yt meſſanger great thankes diuerſe preuey inſtruccions mouthe perſall ſomuche trauaile came duke buckyngham maiſter march wale eftſones newe inſtruccions met duke gloucetre notingham whiche come oute northcoūtrey many knightes gentylmenne noumbre vi c horſe iourney towarde london ſecrete meting cōmunicacion betwene hym duke gloucetre retourned ſuche ſpede yt brought duke buckingham maſter mete wt duke gloucetre farre northampton iii c horſſes ſo twoo came together northampton fyrſt beganne vnhappy enterprice ſo duke buckingham contynued ſtil wt duke gloucetre till crouned kyng ye ſhall plainly perceaue hereafter younge kyng deathe father kepte houſholde ludlowe father ſente hym thyther iuſtice bee doone march wale ende authoritee preſence wylde welſhemenne
