mother kinrede ſequeſtred maner frome company attendaunce euery one ought hym faithfull ſeruice many theim farre honorable parte kynne mother ſyde whoſe bloodde ꝙ duke gloucetre ſauyng kynges pleaſure farre vnmete bee matched whiche nowe bee remoued frome kyng leaſt noble bee lefte aboute hym ꝙ neyther honourable maieſtie v alſo hym leſſe ſuretye haue nobleſt mightieſt frendes frome hym v lytle ieopardye ſuffer ſpecially oure well proued euel willers growe greate authorytee wt king youth namely whiche light belefe ſoone perſwaded ye remembre kyng edward hym ſelf albeit age diſcrecion yet ruled many thinges yt bende ſtoode either wt honoure oure profyte wyth commoditee anye manne elles excepte onely immoderate aduaū cemente theim ſelues whiche whether thriſted ſore theyr owne wele harde thynke geſſe yf ſome folkes frendſhype holden better place wyth kynge anye reſpecte kynred myghte paraduenture eaſely haue trapped brought confuſyon ſome v thys eaſly haue done ſome thys nere blood royall oure lorde hathe wroughte hys wyll thanked hys grace perell paſt beit greate growing ſuffer young kynge enemyes handes whyche wythoute wyttinge myghte abuſe name hys commaundemente af vndoing thynges god good prouyſion forbyd whych good prouyſion none v hathe thynge leſſe nede late attonemente made kynges pleaſure place party heartes willes none v ſo vnwiſe ouerſone truſte newe frende made olde fooe thynke anye onely kyndenes ſo ſodenly contracted houre contynued ſcantlye yet fortnyght ſhoulde deper ſet ſtomackes longe accuſtomed malice many yeres rooted theſe perſwaſions wrytinges yt duke glouceter ſet fyre theim whiche wer eaſye kindle eſpecyall twayne henry duke buckyngham wyllyam lorde haſtynges lorde chamberlayn menne honour great power one lōg ſuceceſſiō aunceters hys offyces kynges fauoure theſe two bearynge eache ſo muche loue hatred quenes bloodde accorded together duke glouceter would remoue frome kyng mother frēdes vnder name theyr enemyes wherupon duke glouceter beynge aduertyſed lordes kyng entended brynge london hys coronation accō panyed wyth ſuch nomber theyr frendes ſhoulde harde hym bryng hys purpoſe paſſe wythoute aſſemblinge gathering people maner open warre wherof ende wyſt doubtefull whyche kynge beynge ſyde ſhoulde haue name face rebellion ſecretelye therefore dyuers meanes cauſed quene perſwaded nether nede ſhoulde alſo bee ieopardeous kinge come vp ſo ſtronge nowe euery lorde loued none thynge ſtudyed tryumphe coronation honoure yt kyng lordes aboute kyng ſhould aſſēble kinges name much people ſhuld geue lordes betwyxte whome theim bene ſome tyme debate feare ſuſpecte leaſte ſhoulde gather thys people kynges ſauegarde man impugned theyr deſtruccyon hauynge regarde theyr olde varyaunce theyr newe attonemente whyche cauſe part myght aſſemble men alſo theyr defence whoſe powres ſhe wyſte well farre ſtretched thus ſhould al realme fall roare miſchiefe thereof ſhoulde enſue whiche lykly lytle moſt harme lyke fal ſhe leaſte woulde worlde woulde put kynred blame ſaiynge vnwſelye vntruely broken amytie peace whyche kynge huſbande ſo prudently made betwene kinred hys whyche amytee hys kinne alwaies obſerued quene beyng thus perſwaded ſente worde kynge brother cauſe ner nede aſſemble anye people alſo duke glouceter lordes bēd wrot vnto kinge ſo reuerently quenes frendes ſo louyngely nothing earthlye myſtruſtyng broughte young kyng toward london wt ſober compaignie greate haſt good ſpede til came northāpton frō thēce remoued stony ſtratford whyche daye two duke theyr bende came northampton faynynge stonye ſtratforde coulde lodge theim founde earle ryuers entendynge nexte moruynge haue folowed kynge bee wyth hym earely mornyng nyght duke made earle riuers frendly chere aſſone departed verye famylier wyth greate curteſie opē ſyghte erle riuers lodged ii duke theyr pryuye frendes fell councell wherein ſpente greate part nyght dawning daye ſente pryuely ther ſeruauntes theyr lodgynges haſte horſebacke theyr lordes maner redy ryde wheruppon theyr ſeruauntes ready lorde ryuers ſeruauntes wer awake nowe duke taken keyes ynne theyr poſſeſſion ſo none ſhoulde yſſue oute wythout concente ouer thys hygh way toward stony ſtratforde ſet certaine theyr folkes ſhoulde cauſe compell retourne perſons paſſinge frome nōrthampton stony ſtratforde ſayinge duke theim ſelfes woulde fyrſt ſhould come kynge northampton thus bare folkes hande earle ryuers vnderſtode gate cloſed wayes euery ſyde beſet nether hys ſeruauntes nether hym ſelf ſuffered goo oute perceauinge ſo great thing wythoute knowledge begon noughte comparyng thys preaſent dooynge wyth laſte nyghtes cherein ſo fewe houres ſo great chaūce marueleouſly myſlyked howbeit ſyth could get awaye determined kepe ſelf cloſe leaſte ſhoulde ſeme hyde hym ſelfe ſome ſecret fear hys owne faute wherof ſaw ſuch cauſe ſelfe wherfore ſuretie hys owne conſience determyned go thē inquire thys matter myghte meane whome aſſone ſaw beganne quarell wyth hym affyrmyng pretended ſet dyſtaunce betwene kyng theim bryng theim confucyon whyche ſhould lye powre began el oequēt manne godly wiſe excuſe hym ſelf thei would aunſwer tooke hym force putte hym ward mounted horſback came stony ſtratford wher kyng goyng horſbacke becauſe would leaue y• lodgyng theim ſtrayte bothe compaignies thei came preſence thei alighted compaignie aboute theim knee ſaluted hym theim gētely receaued nothyng erthely knowyng ner miſtruſtyng yet duke buckyngham ſaied aloude afore gentlemenne yomenne kepe roumes therwith yt kyng preſence thei picked quarell lord rychard grey quenes ſoonne brother lord marque halfe brother kyng ſaiyng marque brother lorde ryuers vncle cōpaſſed rule kyng realme ſette varyaūce betwene theſtates ſubdewe deſtroye noble bloodde realme toward thaccompliſhment theſame thei ſaied y• lord marque entred toure london thence takē oute treaſure ſent mēne ſea whiche thynges theſe duke knewe well dooen good purpoſe neceſſary appoincted yt whole counſail londō ſomewhat thei muſt haue ſaied vnto whiche woordes kyng aunſwered brother marque hath dooen cannot ſaie good faith dare well aunſwer myne vncle ryuers brother thei bee innocent ſuche mattiers yee leege ꝙ duke buckyngham thei haue kepte ye dealyng theſe matter farre knowledge good grace foorthwith thei arreſted lord rychard ſir thomas vaugham ſir rychard hawte kyng preſence brought kyng northāpton thei tooke ferther counſaill affaire thei ſent kyng pleaſed theim ſet aboute hym ſuche ſeruauntes better pleaſed theim hym whiche dealyng wept booted dynner duke glouceſter ſent dyſhe owne table lorde ryuers praiyng hym bee good chere ſhould bee well thanked hym prayed meſſenger beare nephiewe lord rychard like woordes knewe haue neede conforte one ſuche aduerſite ſtraunge hym ſelf dayes ennured therwith therfore could beare meſſage duke glouceſter ſent lord ryuers ye lord rychard ſir thomas vaughm̄ ſir rychard hawte northparties dyuers priſones laſt came poumfrette thei foure behedded without iudge • et maner haue heard duke glouceſter tooke hym gouernaunce younge kyng muche reuerence conueighed towardes london theſe tidynges came haſtely quene mydnight ſore reporte kyng hir ſoonne taken brother ſoonne hir frendes areſted ſent manne wyſt whither heuye tydynges quene bewayled childes ruyn hir frendes miſchaunce awne infortune curſſyng tyme euer ſhe perſwaded leaue gatheryng people bryng vp kyng greate powre paſſed therfore nowe ſhe tooke hir younger ſoonne duke yorke hir doughters went oute palais weſtminſter ſanctuary lodged abbotes place ſhe child compaignie regyſtred ſanctuary perſones ſame night came docter rotheram archebyſſhop yorke lorde chauceloure meſſenger lorde chambrelayne yorke place beſyde weſtminſter meſſenger brought byſſhoppes bed ſyde declared hym yt duke gone backe younge kyng northamptō declared ferther lorde haſtynges maſter ſent hym woord ſhould feare nothyng ſhould bee well well ꝙ biſſhop bee well neuer bee ſo well haue ſeen meſſenger depar • ted whereupon byſſhop called vp ſeruauntes daye light tooke hym greate ſeale came daye quene founde muche heuyneſſe rumble haſte buſyneſſe conuerghaunce caryage hir ſtuffe ſanctuary euery manne buſye carye beare conueigh ſtuffe cheſtes ferdelles manne vnoccupied ſome caryed thei commaunded another place quene ſat alone belowe ruſſhes deſolate dyſmaied archebiſſhop conforted beſt maner coulde ſhewynge matter nothynge ſo ſore ſhe tooke put good hope oute feare meſſage ſente hym frō lorde haſtinges wo worth ꝙ quene goeth aboute deſtroye bloodde madame ꝙ good comforte aſſure yf crowne anye king ſoonne whome nowe haue ſhal morowe croune brother whō haue greate ſeale lykewiſe noble huſbande delyuered ſo deliuer vſe ſōne therewyth delyuered greate ſeale departed home dawnynge daye opened windowes looked themys myghte ſee riuer ful boates duke glouceter hys ſeruauntes watchyng perſon ſhoulde goo ſanctuary ner none ſhoulde paſſe vnſerched great rumoure commocion citee place people diuerſly deuined vpō thys dealyng dyuerſe lordes knyghtes gentylmen ether fauour quene feare ſelues aſſembled compaignies together went flockyng together harneyes many alſo recompted thys demeanour attempted ſo eſpecyallye agaynſt lordes agaynſt kyng ſelf dyſturbaunce hys coronat ion therefore aſſembled together common thys matter london archebyſhoppe yorke fearynge woulde aſcrybed dede ouermuche lightnes ſo ſodeynly yelded vp great ſeale quene whome cuſtodie therof nothyng apperteigned without eſpeciall commaundement yt kyng ſecretly ſent ſeale agayn brought wyth hym accuſtomed maner mete lordes metyng lord haſtynges whoſe truthe towarde kyng manne doubted neded doubte perſwaded lordes beleue duke glouceter faythfull ſure towardes prince yt lord ryuers lorde richard knyghtes apprehended wer matter attempted theim agaynſte duke gloucetre buckyngham put vnder areſt ſuretie kynges icopardye alſo ſauegarde remayne tyll matter duke alſo lordes kynges councell indifferentlye examyned diſcrecions ordred eyther iudged appeſed one thyng aduyſed theim beware iudged matter farreforth knewe truthe turnyng theyr pryuate grudge commen hurte irrityng prouokyng men vnto angre diſturbyng kynges coronacion toward whiche duke wer cō myng might paraduenture bryng yt matter ſo farre ioynte ſhoulde neuer bee brought frame agayne whiche yf ſhould happe lykely come felde though party thynges eguall yet ſhoulde autoryte bee ſyde kynge hym ſelfe theſe perſuaſyons lorde haſtynges whereof parte hym ſelfe belcued parte wyſte well contrarye theſe commocyons ſomewhat appeaſed eſpeciall becauſe duke buckyngham glouceter wer ſo nere came ſo ſhortly kynge none maner none voyce ſembleaunce coronacion cauſyng fame blowen ſuche perſones apprehended contryued diſtruccion duke gloucetre buekyngham noble bloodde thys realme thentent thei alone would rule gouerne kyng coloure therof ſuch duke ſeruauntes rode carte ſtuffe wer taken amonge ſtuffe maruayle thoughe ſome harneyes whiche brekynge vp ſuche houſholde muſte brought awaye caſte awaye ſhewed people went ſayde lo barrelles harneyes theſe traytoures hadde preuely conueighed caryages deſtroye noble lordes withall dyuerſe although made matter wiſe menne vnlykely well perceauyng thentendoures ſuche purpoſe woulde rather haue theyr harneſſe theyr backes haue bounde theim vp barrelles yet muche parte commen people therewith ryght well ſatiſfyed kyng approched nere cytie edmonde shawe goldeſmythe mayre cytie aldremenne ſhreues ſkarlet fyue hundreth commoner murraye receaued grace reuerently harneſaye parke ſo conueighed hym cytee entred fourthe daye maye fyrſte laſte yeare reigne lodged biſſhoppes palayce duke goucetre bare hym open ſight ſo reuerently ſaiyng men rode beholde youre prynce ſouereygne lorde made ſuche ſembleaunce lowlynes prince frome greate obloquy ſo late ſodeynly fallen ſo greate truſte councell next aſſembled made onlye chiefe ruler thoughte mooſte mete bee protectoure kynge realme ſo deſteny folye lambe betaken wolfe kepe whiche councell archebyſhoppe yorke ſore blamed delyueryng greate ſeale quene ſeale taken hym delyueto docter iohn ruſſell byſhoppe lyncolne wyſe manne good muche experyence dyuerſe lordes knightes appoynted dyuerſe roumes lorde chamberlayn ſome kepte roumes yt many nowe ſo protectour whiche alwayes muſte take duke gloucetre ſore thriſted acheuyng pretenſed entrepryſe thought euerye daye yere tyll perfourmed yet durſte ferther attempte aſlong hadde halfe praye hys hande well wyttynge yf depoſed one brother realme would fall yf remayned ſanctuary ſhould happely ſhortelie cōueyghed farther libertee wherfore continēt next metyng lordes councell purpoſed theim heynous thyng quene procedyng great lyce toward kynges councelers yt ſhe ſhoulde kepe kynges brother ſanctuarye hym whoſe ſpecial pleaſure conforte wer haue brother wt hym done none intēt bryng ye lordes obloquy murmoure people though wer truſted wt kynges brother lordes wer yt whole aſſ • noble yt realme appoynted yt kynges nere frendes ye tuycion royall perſon proſperitee wherof ꝙ ſtandeth alonely frō kepyng enemyes euill dyate partely alſo recreacion moderate pleaſure whiche cannot take tendre youth cōpany old auncient perſons famylyer conuerſacion thoſe farre vnder farre aboue age neuertheleſſe eſtate cōueniēt accompany maieſtie wherfore wt rather owne brothere man thinke cōſyderaciō light thynke man ſo thinketh loueth ye kyng let hym cōſyder yt ſometyme wt ſmal thynges greater cannot ſtande verelye redoundeth greatly ye dyſhonoure kynges highnes v bee grace haue come mannes mouthe realme onely alſo landes euell woordes walke farre yt kynges brother ſhould fayne kepe ſāctuary euery mā wyl iudge man wil ſo nought ſuch opiniōs faſtened mennes hertes harde wreſted oute many growe grefe manne diuine wherfore thinketh worſte ſende quene ſome honourable truſtye perſonage ſuche tendereth kynges weale honoure counſell alſo credite fauoure whiche conſideracions none ſemeth meately reuerende father lorde cardinall archbiſhop cauntourbury maye matter doo mooſte good menne yf pleaſe hym take paine whiche doubte goodneſſe wil refuſe kynges ſake oures wealth younge duke hym ſelfe kyn ge mooſt honorable brother comforte ſouereigne lord hym ſelfe mooſt dereſt nephiewe conſidering therby ſhalbe ceaſſed ſclaunderous rumour obloquy nowe goyng abroade hurtes auoyded yt therof myght enſue muſt reſte quietneſſe growe realme ſhe percaſe bee obſtinate ſo preciſely ſette owne wyll opynion neither wyſe feithfull aduertyſement moue mannes reaſon ſatiſfye thē ſhal myne aduice kynges authoritee fetche hym oute pryſone bring hym noble preſence whoſe continuall companye ſhalbe ſo well cheryſhed ſo honorablye intreated worlde ſhall oure bonoure reproche perceaue onely malyce frowardneſſe foly cauſeth kepe hym minde tyme excepte lordes anye thinge per ceaue contrarye neuer ſhall goddes grace ſo wedde ſelfe vnto myne owne wyll ſhalbe redye chaunge vpon youre better aduice protectoure ſaied coun cell affirmed mocion good reaſonable kyng duke brother honorable thing ſhoulde ceaſſe great murmoure realme yf mother myght good meanes bee induced deliuer hym whiche thing archbiſhop cauntourburye whome agreed alſo bee mooſt conuenient thervnto tooke vpon hym moue therto dooe vttermoſte endeuoure yf ſhe coulde wiſe bee intreated good wil delyuer hym thought ſuche ſpirytualtye preſente anye wyſe bee attempted take hym oute agaynſte wyll woulde bee thyng ſhould turne grudge menne high diſpleaſure god pryuiledge place ſhould bee broken ſo many yeres kepte whiche bothe kynges biſhoppes graunted confyrmed whiche grounde ſanctifyed ſainct peter hym ſelfe v hundreth yeres agone ſyth tyme neuer ſo vndeuoute kynge euer enterpryſed ſacred priuyledge vyolate ſo holy biſhoppe durſte preſume churche ſame conſecrate therfore ꝙ archbyſſhoppe god forbyd manne ſhoulde erthely enterpryſe breake immunyte libertee ſacred sanctuary hath bene ſauegard ſo many good mannes lyfe truſte ꝙ ſhall nede maner nede would ſhould doo truſt ſhe reaſon ſhalbe contented thyng good maner obteigned yf hap bring paſſe yet ſhal beſt power ſo ſhall perceaue good wyl diligence indeuoure mother dreade womanniſhe feare ſhalbe let yf bee naye womanniſh frowardneſſe ꝙ duke buckingham dare take ſoule yt ſhe wel knoweth yt ſhe nedeth ſuche thyng feare either ſonne ſelfe manne wyll warre womenne would god ſome menne kynne wer womenne ſhould bee ſone reſt none kynne leſſe loued bee kynne owne euell deſeruing put caſe nether loued kinne yet cauſe ſhould hate kinges noble brother whoſe grace oure ſelues kynne whoſe honoure yf ſhe deſyred oure dyſhonoure aſmuche regarde tooke wealthe owne wyll ſhe coulde bee lothe ſuffer hym abſente kyng v yf ſhe wytte woulde god ſhe good wyll ſhe hath frowarde wytte ſhe thynketh ſelfe wiſer ſome yt whoſe feithful myndes ſhe nothing doubteth verely beleueth know legeth woulde bee ſorye harme owne ſelfe yet woulde haue hym frome yf ſhe abyde thinke bee content bothe child bee ſhe came frome thence bee ſuche place maye bee theyr honoure nowe yf ſhe refuſe deliueraunce hym folowe wiſdome theim whoſe wiſdome ſhe knoweth whoſe approbate fidelitee ſhe truſteth eaſye perceaue frowardneſſe letteth feare goo ſuppoſe ſhe feareth maye let feare owne ſhadowe ſhe feareth deliuer hym oughte feare leaue hym handes yf ſhe caſte ſuche fonde doubtes ſhe feare hurte wyll ſhe feare ſhall fette thence ſhe wyll ſoone thynke yf menne ſette whiche god forbydde ſo greate miſchief sanctuarye wyll lytel lette theim whiche ſanctuary good menne thinketh myghte withoute ſynne ſomewhat leſſe regarde dooe nowe yf ſhe doubte leaſte might bee fetched licklye ſhe ſende hym ſome oute realme verely looke none doubte ſhe nowe ſore mindeth mind let therof ſhe might hap bring purpoſe paſſe great maſtery doo letting alone yt world would ſay ſorte wyſe councelers aboute king let brother bee caſt away vnder noſes therfore enſure feithfully minde wyll rather maugre ſtomacke fetche hym awaye leaue hym tyll feare fonde frowarde feare conuey hym awaye yet wyll breake ſanctuarye verely ſithe priueledge place yt ſorte haue ſo long contynued woulde go breake yt yf nowe begynne would ſhoulde make theim yet wyl ſaye nay deede pitie ſuch men chaūce y• ſea theyr euil debters haue brought pouertee ſhoulde haue ſome place refuge kepe theyr body daūger theyr cruel credytoures yf fortune croune come queſtion hath done thys time whyle eatch parte taketh traytoures thyncke neceſſarye haue place refuge theues murtherers whereof theſe place full whyche neuer falle theyr crafte fall therunto yt pytee euer ſanctuarye ſhoulde ſaue theim eſpecyall wylfull murtherers god commaundeth taken aulter putte death wyſe theſe caſes nede ſayntuaryes apointed god olde law yf neceſſite owne defence myſfortune dryued hym yt deed pardon ſerueth hym whyche ether graū ted courſe kynge pytee compaſſyon geueth nowe looke howe fewe ſanctuary mē neceſſyte myſfortune compelled together ſee ſyde ſorte bee commonlye therin ſuche wylfull vnthryftines hathe broughte naughte rable theues murtherers malycyous heynous traytours bee two place ſpecyallye one elbowe cytee bowel dare wel vowe yf waye good wyth hurte commeth theim ye ſhall fynde much better leſe haue thys ſay although abuſed nowe bee ſo longe haue bene feare euer wylbe men feard ſet theyr handes mēdement though god ſaynt peter patron vngratious lyuing vnthryftes riot ronne debte vpon boldnes theſe place yea rytch men ronne thyther poore men goodes buylde ſpende byd theyr creditours go whyſtel men wyues ronne thether theyr huſbādes plate ſay dare abide theyr huſbandes beting theues bring thether ſtollē goodes lyue thereon deuiſe newe robbery nightly ſtele robbe reue kyl men come agayne thoſe place though thoſe place gaue thē ſauegard harme yt thei haue done licēce alſo myſchiefe howbeit much great abuſion yf wyſe mē woulde ſet theyr handes thereunto myghte bee mended great thankes god breche priuiledge concluſion ſythe ſo long go wote pope prynce piteous polityke hath graunted men ſence relygious feare haue broken yt let v take payne let ſtande goddes name hys force ferforth reaſon wyl whyche ſo ferfourth maye ſerue let v fetchynge forth thys noble manne hys honoure welth place whyche nether nether ſanctuary priueledged mā ſanctuarye euer ſerueth defend bodye man ſtandeth daungers abrode great hurt lawful hurt agaynſt vnlawful hurtes harmes pope ner kynge entended priueledge anye one place wherin lawful one man another mā wrong man vnlaufully take hurte lybertye kynge lawe verye nature biddeth euery place maketh regard euery man euery place ſanctuarye wher man lawful meanes parel nedeth tuycion ſome ſpecyall priueledge ground al ſanctuaries neceſſitee thys noble prince farre whoſe loue kyng nature kynred proueth whoſe innocentie al world hys tender youth affyrmeth ſo ſāctuary neceſſary ner none cā haue men com ſāctuary com baptim require godfather muſt aſke ſelf yt muſt haue reaſon ſith mā hath cauſe haue whoſe conſyence hys faut maketh hauened require wyl thé hath yōder babe diſcretiō require yf nede wer dare ſay wold right angry wt theim yt kepe ther wold thīk wtout ſcruple conſciēce wtout brech priueledge ſōwhat homly wt yt ther ſāctuary mē ded yt yf one go ſāctuary wt another mās goodes ſhold ye king leuīg body liberty ſatiſfye y• party goodes euē win ye ſāctuary nether kyng pope geue anye place ſuch priueledge ſhal diſcharge man debtes beynge hable pay dyuerſe clergie p̄ſēt whether thei ſaied pleaſure thei thought agreed plainly yt lawe god ye churche yt goodes ſanctuary manne ſhould bee delyuered paymēt debtes ſtollen goodes owner onely lybertie reſerued hym gette lyuyng labour handes verely ꝙ duke thynke ye ſaie truth mannes wife take ſanctuary becauſe ſhe liſt ronne hir huſband would thinke ſhe cā alledge none cauſe maye laufully without dyſpleaſure dooen ſainct peter take hir oute ſainct peter churche arme bodye maye bee taken oute ſanctuary becauſe ſaieth abyde chylde take ſanctuary becauſe feareth goo ſchoole maſter muſt lette hym alone ſymple example yet leſſe reaſon oure caſe though bee chyldyſhe feare yet leaſt ſome feare herein feare verely haue heard ſanctuary menne neuer harde ſanctuary chyldren ther fore concluſiō mynde whoſo euer maye deſerue haue nede thei thinke ſuretye let theim kepe bee ſāctuary manne hath nother diſcreſion deſire ner malice deſerue whoſe life ner lybertie laufull proceſſe ſtande ieoperdie taketh one oute ſanctuarye dooe hym good ſaye plainlye breaketh ſanctuarye duke dooen temporall mēne wholy mooſte parte ſpirituall mēne alſo thynke hurte earthely mente towarde baby condiſcended effecte delyuered ſhould bee fetched howbeit thei thought beſt aduoydyng maner rumoure cardynall ſhould firſt aſſaye gette hym good therupon counſaill came ſtarre chamber weſtmynſter cardinall leauyng protectour lordes ſterre chaumber departed ſanctuarie quene accompaignied wt certain lordes yt reſpecte honour ſhe ſhould perſonnes ſo many perceaue arrande onely one mānes mynde protectoure entended matter truſt one manne alone el ſhe finally determined kepe hym ſome compaignie paraduenture ſome ſecrete inſtrucciō incontinēt maugre take hym leaue reſpyte conueigh hym quene lordes come together preſence cardynall ſhewed vnto thought lord protectour whole caunſaill yt hir kepyng yt kynges brother place highly ſoūded onely yt grudge people obloquy alſo unportable greefe diſpleaſure yt kyng royall maieſtie whoſe grace ſynguler cō forte haue naturall brother compaignie bothes diſhonoures hirs alſo ſuffre hym ſanctuarye though one brother ſtoode daungier perell ſhewed ferther whole counſaill ſent hym requyre delyuerye hym might bee brought yt kyng preſence libertie oute yt place whiche meune reconed priſone ſhould bee demeaned accordyng eſtate degree ſhe doyng ſhould bothe dooe greate good realme pleaſure coūſaill profite ſelf ſuccoure frendes deſtreſſe ouer yt whiche wiſt well ſhe ſpeciallye tendered onelye greate conforte honoure kyng alſo younge duke hym ſelf whoſe bothe greate wealthe bee together aſwell many greater cauſes alſo bothe dyſporte recreacyon whiche thynges lordes eſtemed ſleight though ſemed light well pōde ryng yt youthe without recreacion playe cānot endure ner eſtraunger conueniē cie bothe eſtates ſo metely yt poinct theim either theim theother lorde ꝙ quene ſaie naye conueniente yt gentlemanne requyre compaignie kyng brother good faith thynketh greate commodite theim bothe yet bee cuſtodie mother tendre age conſydered elder theim bothe eſpeciall younger whiche beſydes infancye alſo nedeth good lookyng hath awhyle ſo ſore deſeaſed ſyckeneſſe ſo newlye rather lytle amended well recouered dare putte perſone earthely truſt wt kepyng ſelf onely conſyderyng phiſicians ſaie alſo fynde double yt perell reſylynacion yt firſt ſyckeneſſe whiche deſeaſe nature beyng ſore laboured forweried weaked waxeth leſſe hable bear oute newe ſurfett 〈…〉 albeit might bee foūden would happely dooe beſt vnto hym yet none yt ether knoweth better howe ordre hym yt ſo lōg haue kepte hym tendrely like cheriſhe hym owne mother yt bare hym māne denieth good madame ꝙ y• cardinall yt grace folke mooſt neceſſarie aboute chyldrē ſo would yt coūſaill bee content alſo glad y• might ſtand wt pleaſure ſuche place might ſtāde wt honour apoinct ſelf tarie thē thynke thei cōueniēt duke yorke yt kyng honorably lybertie cōforte theim bothe ſanctuary māne bothe diſhonoure obloquy ſith alwaie ſo greate neceſſite haue yt childe mother occaciō ſometyme maye bee ſuche ſhould bee expediēt kepe hym el whiche well apereth yt ſuche tyme yt mooſt dereſt ſoonne thē prince nowe kyng ſhould honour good ordre countre kepe houſhold wale farre kepyng grace well cōtent therwt ſelf well content ꝙ quene pet caſe like theone helth theother nowe ſicke whiche caſe meruell greatly lord protectour ſo deſierous haue hym kepyng childe ſickeneſſe miſcaried nature yet might rōne ſlaunder ſuſpicion fraude thei call thyng ſo ſore againſt childes honoure alſo abideth place honoures ſuffre hym abide wher manne doubteth ſhalbe beſt kepte whiche yet entend come foorth ieopard ſelfe frēdes whiche would god rather ſuertie ieoperdie wt theim madame ꝙ ye lord hawarde knowe thyng thei ſhould bee ieopardie naye verely ꝙ ſhe thei ſhould bee priſone neither thei nowe bee trowe greate maruell though feare leaſte thoſe yt haue letted put theim duraunce wt coloure let litle procure diſtrucion without cauſe cardinall made countenaunce lord haward ſhould harpe vpon yt ſtryng thē ſaied quene yt nothyng doubted thoſe lordes kynne whiche remeyned vnder reſt ſhould vpon matter • ramined dooe well ynough toward noble perſone neither could bee maner ieopardie wherby ſhould truſte ꝙ yt quene yt guyltleſſe though thei guyltie yt enemy better beloued thei whē thei hate theim ſake ſo nere kyng howe ferre bee thei would helpe god ſēde grace thei hurt therfore yet purpoſe departe hence gentlemanne ſoonne minde ſhall wher till ſe ſe ſome mēne ſo gredy whthout ſubſtanciall cauſe haue hym whiche maketh muche afrayd ſcrupulous delyuer hym truly madame ꝙ cardynall afrayde ye bee delyuer hym menne feareth ſuffre kepe hym leaſte youre cauſeleſſe feare mighte cauſe farther conueye hym many thynke haue pryuiledge whiche haue neyther wyll aſke yet malyce offence nede therfore recon priuiledge broken although fetche hym ſanctuarye whiche yf fynallye refuſe delyuer hym thynke verely ye councel wil enfrauncheſe hym ſo muche drede hathe lorde vncle tēdre loue beareth hym leaſt grace ſhould ſende hym awaye ah ꝙ quene hath ſo tendre zele hym feareth nothyng leaſt ſhould eſcape hym thynketh would ſende hym hence whiche neyther plight ſende oute place coulde recone hym ſure bee ſure ſanctuarye whereof neuer tyraunte yet ſo deuelyſhe durſte attempte breake priuiledge truſte god nowe ſtronge wythſtande aduerſaries euer ſoonne deſerue ſanctuarye ſaye therfore cannot haue forſothe lorde protectoure hath ſente goodly gloſe whiche place may defend theſe may ſaue innocent ieopardye hath nede thereof woulde god troweth protectoure praye god maye proue protectour rather deſtroyer whereunto peynted proceſſe draweth honourable duke byde confortable theim bothe brother becauſe kyng lacketh playe feloe yea bee ſure praye god ſende hym better playefelowes hym maketh ſo hyghe matter vpon ſuche tryfleynge pretexte though coulde none bee founde playe kynge yf brother whiche hathe lu 〈…〉 playe ſyckeneſſe muſte come oute sanctuarye oute ſauegarde playe hym though prynces ſo young • coulde playe without peres chyldrē coulde playe without theyr kynred whome parte agree muche woorſſe ſtraungiers chyld ſaye cannot require priuiledge tolde protectoure ſo aſke hym ſhall hym aſke ſo ſhall ye wyll howebeit ſtraunge matter ſuppoſe coulde aſke thynke woulde aſke ymagene woulde aſke go oute yf ſaye ſhall note aſke priuiledge ſelfe ſaye agaynſt wyll taketh hym breaketh sanctuarye serueth thys lyberty perſonne onlye goodes maye frome hence take horſſe frome yf ſtale hym owe nothynge foloweth maye take chylde alſo ward farre learned councell ſheweth hath nothyng dyſſente holden knyghtes ſeruage ſocage lawe maketh garden maye manne lawfully ſuppoſe take warde frome oute thys place wythoute breche sanctuarye yf pryuyledge coulde ſerue hym aſke hym ſelfe yet ſythe lawe commytteth cuſtodye hym maye requyre hym excepte lawe geue infaunte garden onelye hys gooddes dyſchargynge hym cure ſauekepynge bodye whiche onely bothe goodes landes ſerue wherfore entende kepe hym ſithe mannes lawe ſerueth garden kepe infaunte lawe nature wylleth mother kepe yt chyld goddes lawe priuiledgeth sanctuarye sanctuarye pryuyledgeth ſoonne ſythe feare putte hym protectoures handes hathe brother already whiche yf bothe fayled inheritoure croune heyre male ſayth cauſe feare man hath dooe examen yet feare law feareth whiche learned menne tell forbyddeth euery manne cuſtody theim whoſe death maye enheryte leſſe lande kyngdome ſaye whoſoeuer bee breaketh holy ſanctuary praye god ſende hym ſhortelye nede sanctuary maye come woulde mortall enemie ſhould taken sanctuary cardynal perceaued quene euer yt lenger farther alſo ſhe beganne kyndle chafe ſpake ſore bytynge woordes agaynſt protectoure ſuche neyther beleued alſo lothe ſayd finall concluſion would diſpute matter ſhe contente delyuer duke hym lordes preſent durſte laye owne bodye ſoule bothe pledge onlye ſuretie alſo hys eſtate ſurely knewe ſuſpected cauſe might ſo dooe knewe ſaide ſhe would geue hym reſolute aunſwere contrarye would therewith departe incontinent ſhifte ſo woulde wyth buſyneſſe afterwarde neuer entended moue matter whiche thought alſo ſaue ſelfe lacked eyther wytte truthe wytte ſo dull nothyng coulde perceaue protectoure entended yf ſhould procure ſoonne bee delyuered handes whome ſhoulde perceaue towardes chyld euell wyll entended ſhe myghte thynke councell bothe euel aduyſed lytle fydelyte theyr prince quene theſe wordes ſtoode great ſtudye foraſmuche ſhe ſawe lord cardynall redyer departe remanaūt protectoure hym ſelfe redye hande ſo ſhe verelye thought ſhe coulde kepe hym ſhoulde bee incontynente taken thence conueye hym elles neyther ſhe tyme ſerue place determyned perſonnes appoynted conueygh hym ſo thyng vnreadye meſſage came ſo ſodenly nothyng leſſe lookyng haue hym ſanctuarye whiche ſhe knewe nowe menne bee ſet place coulde bee conueyghed oute vntaken partely ſhe thought myghte fortune feare bee falſe ſo well ſhe wiſt ether nede leſſe boteleſſe wherfore yf ſhe ſhould nedes go hym ſhe demed beſt deliuer hym ſpecially yt cardinalles faith ſhe nothing doubted ſome lordes whome ſhe ſawe ſhe feared leaſt might deceaued ſo well ſhe aſſured yt woulde bee corrupted thoughte ſhe woulde make theim warely looke hym circum ſpectly ſee ſurety yf ſhe owne handes betooke hym theim truſte laſte ſhe tooke young duke hande ſaied vnto lordes lorde ꝙ ſhe lordes nether ſo vnwiſe miſtruſte youre wittes ſo ſuſpicyous miſtruſte truthes thing purpoſe make ſuch proofe yf either bothe lacked might turne greate ſorowe realme muche harme greate reproche lo ꝙ ſhe gentilman whome doubte could kepe ſalfe would whatſoeuer manne ſaye doubte alſo bee ſome abrode ſo deedly enemy vnto bloodde yf wiſte laye theyr owne body woulde lette oute haue alſo experience deſyre kingdome knoweth kynred brother hath bene brother bane may nephewes bee ſure vncle eache theſe child others defence whyle bee ſunder eache liues lyeth others body kepe one ſalfe bothe bee ſure nothing bothe perylous bothe bee one place wiſe marchaunt neuer auentureth good de one ſhyp notwithſtanding deliuer hym brother hym kepe handes whome ſhall aſke theim bothe god worlde feithfull bee wot well knowe wyſe power ſtrength liſt kepe hym lacke helpe ſelues nede lacke helpe caſe yf cannot elles may leaue hym onely one thing beſech truſt father putte euer truſte put nowe farre thincke feare muche ye bee well ware feare lytle therwith ſhe ſaied yt childe fare well myne owne ſwete ſoonne god ſende good kepyng let kyſſe gooe god knoweth whē ſhall kiſſe together againe therwith ſhe kyſſed hym bleſſed hym tourned backe wepte gooing waye leauyng poore innocent chylde wepyng faſte mother cardinall lordes receaued younge duke brought hym ſtarre chaumbre yt protectoure tooke hym armes kyſſed hym theſe wordes nowe welcome lorde hert ſaied yt likelihode euen inwardly thought therupon forthwith brought king brother biſhoppes palaice powles thence thorowe citee honourably towre oute whiche daye neuer came abrode whenne protectoure bothe chyldren poſſeſſyon yee ſure place beganne thryſte ſee ende enterpriſe auoyde ſuſpicion cauſed lordes whiche knewe bee feythfull kyng aſſemble baynardes caſtell cōmen ordre coronacyon whyle complyces affinitee eroſbyes place contriued contrary make protectours kyng whiche counſel adhibite fewe ſecrete beganne ſome maner muttering amongeſt people though thing ſhould longe bee well though wyſte feared wherfore ſuche great thinges mennes hertes ſecrete inſtyncte nature miſgeueth theim yt ſouthwinde ſomtime ſwelleth hym ſelfe tempeſte ſome one manne happely perceauing fylled many men ſuſpicyon thoughe ſhewed fewe menne knewe howbeit dealing ſelfe made muche matter thoughe counſayle cloſe lytle lytle folke drewe towre kyng drewe croſ bye place ſo protectoure reſorte kyng maner deſolate ſome made ſuyte vnto theim doyng ſome theim theyr frendes ſecetely warned myghte happely tourne theim good bee muche attendaunte kyng withoute protectoures apoyntmente whiche remoued dyuerſe kynges olde ſeruauntes frō hym ſet newe theyr rome aboute hym thus many thinges comming together partly chaunce partely purpoſe cauſed length cōmon people onely whiche wauer wt winde wiſe menne alſo ſome lordes marke matter muſe therupon ſo much lorde stanley whiche afterward erle derby wiſely miſtruſted ſaied yt lorde haſtinges muche miſiyked theſe two ſeueral coūſelles ꝙ talke one matter yt one place lytle wot wherof talke place well ꝙ lorde haſtynges lyfe neuer doubte whyle one man whiche neuer thence neither bee thing mynded ſhoulde ſounde amiſſe towarde ſhoulde bee mine eares well oute mouthes ment cateſby whiche nere ſecret councell whome familyerly vſed mooſt weightye matter putting manne ſo ſpeciall truſt hym ſith wiſte well manne hym ſo muche beholdyng cateſbye whiche manne well learned lawes lande ſpeciall fauoure lorde haſtynges good authorytee muche rule bare countrees leiceſtre northampton yt lorde haſtinges power laye ſurely greate pitie either trueth leſſe wit diſſimulacyon onely kepte myſchiefe vp whome yf lorde haſtinges put ſo ſpecial truſt yt lord stanley wt diuers lordes departed coūtrees broken al ye daunce many euel ſignes yt ſawe conſtrued al beſt ſo ſurely thought coulde harme towarde hym counſayle entended cateſbye truth protectour duke buckyngham made good ſembleaunce vnto lorde haſtynges kepte hym muche theyre compaignie vndoubtedlie protectour loued hym well lothe haue loſte hym ſauynge feare leaſt hys lyfe ſhoulde haue quayled theyr purpoſe whyche cauſe moued cateſby proue wyth ſome wordes caſte oute farre whether coulde thyncke poſſible wynne lorde haſtynges theyr part cateſby whether aſſayed hym aſſayed hym reported vnto hym founde ſo faſt heard ſpeake ſo terrible wordes durſt farther breake truth lorde haſtinges truſte ſhewed vnto cateſby myſtruſt began haue matter therfor fearyng leaſt theyr mocyons myght wt lorde haſtynges haue myniſhed credence wherunto al matter leaned procured protectour haſtly ryd hym muche rather truſted hys death obtayne much yt rule whyche lorde haſtynges bare hys coū tree onelye deſyre whereof thynge enduced hym procurer one ſpecialleſt contriuers al thys treaſon wherupon lorde protectoure cauſed counſayle ſet towre frydaye xiii daye iune much commonyng honourable ſolempnytee coronation whyche tyme appoynted aproched ſo nere pageaū te making day nyght weſtminſter vytayle kylled afterwarde caſt awaye theſe lordes thus ſittyng commoning matter protectoure came emong thē ix clocke ſalutynge theim curteouſly excuſynge hym ſelfe bene frome theim ſo longe ſaiynge merely bene ſſeper yt daye lytle talkynge wyth theym ſayd biſhop ely lorde haue good ſtrawberies garden holborne requyre let v haue meſſe theim gladly lorde ꝙ would ſome better thyng redy youre pleaſure wyth ſente ſeruaunte al haſte dyſh ſtrawberyes protectoure ſet lordes faſte commonynge thereupon prayed theim ſpare hym lytle ſo departed came agayn betwene x xi clocke chā ber al chaunged ſowre angry countenaūce knyttynge browes frownynge frettynge gnawynge hys lyppes ſo ſet downe hys place lordes dyſmayed ſore marueyled thys maner ſodayne chaunge thynge ſhould hym ayle ſytten whyle thus beganne woorthy haue compaſſe ymagyne dyſtruccyon beynge ſo neare bloodde kynge protectoure hys royal realme whyche queſtyon lordes ſat ſore aſtonned muſynge muche thys queſtyon ſhoulde ment whych euery man knewe hymſelfe clere lord haſtynges familiaritee betwene thoughte myght boldeſt wyth hym anſwered ſayd worthye bee punyſhed heyneous traytours ſo euer affyrmed ſame ꝙ yonder ſorceces brother wyfe wyth meanynge quene theſe wordes manie lordes ſore abaſhed whyche fauoured lorde haſtynges better contente hys mynde moued anye loued better albeit hys hearte grudged afore made councel matter well takynge kynred theyr puttynge deathe whyche hys aſſente deuiſed behedded pomfrete thys ſelfe ſame daye whyche ware ye deuyſed hym ſelfe ſhoulde ſame daye behedded london ſayde protectoure wyſe ye ſorcereſſe hys counſayle shore wyfe wyth affynitee haue theyr ſorcerye wychcrafte thys waſted bodye therewyth plucked vp hys doublet cleane hys elbowe hys lyfte arme ſhewed weryſhe wythered arme ſmall neuer thereupon euery mannes mynd myſgaue theim well perceauynge thys matter quarell well wyſte quene boothe wyſe goo aboute anye ſuche foly yf ſhe woulde yet woulde ſhe al folke make shore wyfe leaſte councel womenne ſhe moſt hated concubin • kyng huſband moſt loued alſo manne knewe hys arme euer ſuch ſyth day hys byrth neuertheleſſe lorde haſtynges whyche death kyng edward kept shore wyfe ſomewhat doted kynges lyfe ſauynge ſayd forbare reuerence towarde hys kynge elles certayne kynd fydelitee towarde hys frende yet nowe heart ſomwhat grudged haue loued ſo hyghly accuſed knewe wel vntrulye therefore aunſwered ſayde certaynlye lord yf haue ſo doone worthie heynous ponyſhemente ꝙ protectoure thou ſerueſt wene wyth yf wyth tell haue doone wyll make good thy bodye traytoure therewith greate anger clapped fyſte boorde great rappe whych token geuen one cryed treaſon withoute chamber therewyth doore claped came ruſhing men harneyes many chamber coulde holde anone yt protectoure ſayd lorde haſtynges arreſt traytoure lord ꝙ yea traitour ꝙ protectour one let flye lord stā ley whyche ſhroncke ſtroake fell vnder table elles hed bene cleft teth ſhortly ſhrancke yet ranne blood aboute hys eares archebyſhoppe yorke doctoure morton byſhoppe ely lorde stanleye taken dyuers whyche beſtowed dyuers chamber ſaue lorde haſtynges whome protectoure commaunded ſpede ſhryue hym apace ſaint poull ꝙ dyne till ſe thy hed booted hym aſke heuilie tooke preeſte auenture made ſhorte ſhrift lenger would bee ſuffred protectoure made ſo muche haſte dyner whiche might goo till murther dooen ſauing vngracious othe brought foorth grene beſide chapell within towre hed layde dowe logge tymber laye buyldyng ye chapell tyrannouſly ſtryken bodye hed enterred wyndeſore mayſter kyng edward fourth whoſe ſoules ieſu pardon amen merueleous caſe either warnynges ſhould haue voyded token could voyde next nyght deathe lorde stanley ſent hym truſty meſſenger mydnight haſt requiryng hym ryſe ryde awaye hym diſpoſed vtterlye lenger abyde fearfull dreame whiche thought bore tuſkes ſo raſed theim bothe heddes bloodde ranne aboute bothe ſhoulders aſmuche protectour gaue bore cogniſaunce ymagened ſhould bee dreme made ſuche fearfull impreſſiō hearte yt throughly determined lēger tarye horſſo readie lord haſtynges would goo hym thei would ryde ſo ferre night thei ſhould bee oute daungere next daye good lord ꝙ lord haſtynges meſſenger leaneth lord thy maſter ſo muche ſuche trifle hath ſuche faith dreames whiche either awne feare fāteſieth doo riſe yt nightes reſt reaſon dayes thought tell hym plaine witchcraft beleue ſuche dreames whiche thei token thynges come thynketh yt might likely make theim true goyng caught brought backe frendes fayle flyer bore cauſe lykely race v tuſkes folkes fled ſome falſhed wherfore either perell none deede bee rather goyng abydyng ſhould nedes fall perell one waye yet leuer menne ſhould ſe mennes falſhed thynke either awne faute faynte feble heart therfore goo thy maſter commende hym praye hym bee mery haue feare aſſure hym aſſured yt māne wotteth myne owne hande god ſende grace ꝙ meſſenger ſo departed certen alſo rydyng toward towre theſame mornyng whiche behedded horſſe accuſtomed ryde ſtombled hym twiſe thriſe almoſt fallyng whiche thyng although happeneth theim daylye myſchaunce towarde yet hath olde eiuill token obſerued gooyng toward myſchief nowe yt foloweth warnyng enuyous ſcorne theſame mornyng ere vp bed shore wife laye wt hym night came hym ſir thomas hawarde ſoonne lorde hawarde whiche ſturryng mornyng earlye courteſie accompaignie hym counſaill foraſmuche lorde haſtynges readye taried awhile hym haſted hym awaye ſir thomas lorde haſtynges ſtayed awhile commonyng preeſt met towre ſtrete brake lordes tale ſaiyng hym merely lord praye come wherfore talke ſo long preeſt haue nede preeſt yet laughed vpon hym though would ſaie ſhall haue nede one ſone lytle wiſt meant night theſe woordes well remembred theim heard theim ſo true lorde haſtynges litle miſtruſted neuer merier ner thought life ſuretye dayes whiche thyng often ſygne chaunge ſhall rather lette thyng paſſe vayne ſuretye mannes mynde ſo nere deathe vpon towre wharffe ſo nere place hedde ſo ſone manne might well caſt balle purſyuan̄t awne called haſtynges mette wt hym metyng ye place put remembraūce another tyme whiche happened theim mete together ye ſame place whiche tyme ye lord haſtynges beē accuſed kyng edward yt lord ryuers quenes brother ſomuche yt awhile laſted long highly yt kynges indignacion ſtode great feare hymſelf foraſmuch nowe met theſame purſyuaunt theſame place ieopardy ſo well paſſed gaue hym greate pleaſure talke hym therof wt whō talked theſame place matter therfore ſaied ah haſtynges arte thou remembred met heuy herte ye lord ꝙ remembre well thanked bee god thei gatte good ner harme therby thou woldeſt ſaie ſo ꝙ thou kneweſt ſo muche dooe whiche fewe knowe yet mo ſhall ſhortly meant erle ryuers yt lord richard ſir thomas vaughm̄ ſhould yt daye bee behedded pomfrette thei deede whiche acte wyſt well ſhould bee dooen nothyng ware yt axe honge ſo nere owne hed feith manne ꝙ neuer ſo ſorye ner neuer ſtoode ſo greate daungier life thou mette loe worlde turned nowe nowe ſtande myne enemy daungier thou mayſt happe heare hereafter neuer life meryer neuer ſo greate ſuertie praye god proue ſo ꝙ haſtynges proue ꝙ dowteſt thou naye naye warraunt ſo maner dyſpleaſed entered towre long lyue haue hearde lord god blyndeneſſe mortall nature mooſte feared mooſt ſuretie reconed hym ſelf mooſt ſureſt loſte life yt within ii houres thus ended honorable manne good knight gentle great autorite wt prīce liuyng ſomewhat diſſolute plain open enemie ſure ſecrete frende eaſye beguyle good herte courage foreſawe perelles louyng manne paſſyng welbeloued verye faythfull truſtie ynough truſtyng much deſtruccion maye perceaue nowe flewe fame lordes death thorough cytie farther like wynde euery mannes eare protectoure immediatly dynner entendynge ſet ſome coloure vpon matter ſent haſt many ſubſtanciall menne cytie towre commynge hym ſelfe wyth duke buckyngham ſtoode harneſſed olde euell fauoured bryganders▪ ſuche manne woulde wene would haue voucheſalued haue putte backes excepte ſome ſodeyne neceſſitee conſtreigned theim lorde protectoure ſhewed theim lorde haſtynges conſpyracye hadde contryued haue ſodenly deſtroyed hym duke buckyngham theſame daye councell entended farther yet wel knowen whiche treaſon neuer knowledge ten clocke theſame fornoone whiche ſodeyne feare draue theim put ſuche harneſſe came nexte theyr hādes defence ſo god holpe theim miſchiefe turned vpon theim would haue done thus required theim reporte euerye manne aunſwered fayre thoughe manne myſtruſted matter whiche truthe manne beleued yet farther appeaſyng people myndes ſent immedyatlye dynner heralde armes proclamacion citee london whiche proclamed kynges name lord haſtynges dyuerſe treyterous purpoſe cōſpired theſame daye haue ſlain protectoure duke buckyngham ſittyng counſaill haue takē vpon theim rule kyng realme pleaſure therby pill ſpoyle thei liſt vncomtrolled muche matter deuiſed theſame proclamacion ſclaunder lord haſtynges eiuill counſaillour kynges father entiſyng hym many thynges highly redoundyng miniſſhyng honoure vniuerſall hurt realme eiuill compaignie ſyniſter procuryng vngracious exſample aſwell many thynges vycious lyuyng inordynate abuſyon bodye bothe many eſpeciall shore wife whiche one ſecrete counſaill heynous treaſon laye nyghtlye namely nyght paſſed next deathe ſo leſſe maruell yf vngracyous lyuyng brought hym vnhappie ende whiche nowe putte commaundement kyng highnes honourable faithfull coū ſaill bothe demerytes beyng ſo openly taken falſe contriued treaſon alſo leaſt delaiyng execucion myght haue encoraged myſcheuous perſones parteners conſpiracye whoſoeuer woulde ſaye kyng richarde lawfullye kyng woulde fight hym vtteraunce threwe downe gauntlet thē hall cried kyng richard ſo thre partes halle one broughte hym cup wyne couered dronke caſte oute drinke departed cuppe herauldes cryed alargeſſe thryſe halle ſo went vp ſtaige ende diner mayre london ſerued kyng quene ſwete wyne eche theim cuppe golde couer gold tyme done darkenight ſo kyng retourned chaumbre euery man lodging feaſte thus fyneſhed kyng ſente home lordes countrees woulde departe excepte lorde stanley whome reteyned tyll hearde ſoonne lorde ſtraunge wente aboute ſuche wente home gaue ſtreyghte charge cōmaundement ſee countryes well ordred yt wronge extorcion ſhould bee done ſubiectes thus taught execute iuſtice equite contrary wherof daylye exercyſed alſo greate rewardes geuen northrenmenne whyche ſent hys coronation ſente theim home theyre country wyth greate thanckes whereof dyuerſe theim nature verye gredye authoryte ſpecyally whē thynke haue conforte fauoure tooke ſo hyghly wroughte ſuch maſtreis ye kyng fayne ryde thether hys fyrſte yere put ſome execution ſtaye countrye elles ſmall myſchechefe enſued nowe thys tryumphante coronation fell myſchiefes thycke thicke thing euell gotten neuer well kepte ſo al tyme hys vſurped reygne neuer ceaſed theyre quel murder death ſlaughter tyll owne deſtruccion ended fyniſhed wt beſt deathe mooſte ryghtwyſe ſaye hys owne ſo beganne wyth mooſt pyteous wycked meane lamentable murther innocente nephewes yonge kynge hys tender brother whoſe death fortune hath neuertheleſſe ſo farre come queſtyon ſome remayned long doubte whether dayes deſtroyed yt parkin warbek many folkes malyce mo folkes folye ſo long ſpace abuſynge worlde aſwell wt prnceis wt poore people reputed taken younger theſe two alſo thynges ſo couertly demeaned one thynge pretē ted another mente nothynge ſo playne openly proued yet common cuſtome cloſe couert dealyng mē euer inwardly ſuſpect many well countrefet iewelles make true miſtruſted howbeit concernyng opinion menne maye ſee conueighaunce therof lyfe noble prynce kyng henry ſeuēth proceſſe parkyn meane ceaſon preſent matter ſhall reherſe dolorous ende theſe two babe euery way haue heard waye haue ſo heard ſuche menne ſuche meanes thynketh heard ſhould true kyng rychard coranacion takynge howe maner two ſōnes king edward deſtroyed waye glouceſtre viſyte newe honoure toune whiche bare name olde deuyſed roade fulfyll thynge intended foraſmuche mynde gaue hym nephewes lyuyng men woulde recon coulde haue right realme thought therfore without delaye ryd theim though kyllyng kynſmen might ende cauſe make hym kyndely kyng wherupon ſent iohn grene whome ſpecially truſted ſyr roberte brakenburye conſtable towre lettre credence alſo ſame syr robert wiſe ſhould put two chyldren death iohn grene dyd errand syr robert brakenbury knelyng ladye towre playnelye aūſwered would neuer put theim death dye therfore whiche aunſwer grene returned recountyng ſame kynge rycharde warwike yet iourneye wherewith toke ſuche diſpleaſure thought yt ſame night ſayed ſecrete page ah whome ſhall manne truſte haue broughte vp ſelfe went would haue moſte ſurely ſerued euen thoſe fayle cōmaundement wyll doo nothing syr ꝙ page lyeth one ye palet chaumbre without dare well ſaye dooe youre grace pleaſure thing ryght heard would refuſe meaning iames tirell whiche manne goodly perſonage gyftes nature worthie haue ſerued muche better prince well ſerued god grace obteyned haue aſmuche treweth good wyll ſtrengthe wyll manne hyghe hearte ſore longed vpwarde riſyng yet ſo faſte hoped beynge hyndred kepte vnder ſyr rycharde ratcliffe ſir willyam cateſbye longing nō parteners prince fauoure namely whoſe pride knew woulde beare pere kept hym ſecrete driftes oute ſecrete truſt thing page well marked knowen wherfore occaſion offred verye ſpeciall frendſhippe ſe tyme ſet hym forwarde ſuche wyſe dooe hym good enemy excepte deuell coulde neuer haue dooen hym ſo muche hurte ſhame vpon page woordes kynge rycharde arooſe communicacyon ſytting drafte conuenyente carpet ſuche counſaile came oute palette chaumbre dyd fynde bedde ſayd iames tyrell ſyr thomas tyrell perſone like brother blood nothyng kynne condicions ſayde ye kyng merely theim ſyrs bed ſo ſone called vp iames tyrrell brake hym ſecretely mynde myſcheuous matter ye foūde hym nothyng ſtraunge wherfore morowe ſent hym brakenburye lettre whiche commaunded delyuer ſayde iames keyes towre night thende might accomplyſhe kynges pleaſure ſuche thynges geuen hym commaundement lettre delyuered keyes receaued iames appoynted nexte nyght enſuynge deſtroye theim deuyſyng preparyng meanes prince aſſone protectoure tooke vpō hym bee kyng left name protectoure therof aduertiſed ſhewed ſhould reygne vncle ſhould haue croune whiche woorde prynce ſore abaſhed beganne ſighe ſayed ala woulde myne vncle woulde lette haue lyfe althoughe leſe kyngdome tolde hym tale vſed hym good woordes put hym beſt conforte coulde foorthwith brother ſhut vp remoued theim one called blacke wyll wyllyam ſlaughter excepte whiche ſette ſerue theim iiii ſee theim ſure whiche tyme prince neuer tyed poyntes thyng rought hym ſelfe young babe brother lyngered thought heueuyſſe till theſe trayterous death deliuered theim wretchedneſſe iames tirrell deuiſed thei ſhould murthered beddes bloode ſhed thexecuciō wherof apoincted myles foreſt one foure kepte theim feloe fleſhe bred murther tyme ioyned one ihon dighton awne horſkeper bygge broade ſquare ſtrong knaue beyng remoued theim myles foreſt ihon dighton aboute mydnight child beyng beddes came chaumbre murtherynge kynge edward chyldren ſodenly lapped theim vp emongeſt clothes ſo bewrapped theim entangled theim kepyng downe force fetherbed pyllowes heard vnto mouthes yt within awhile thei ſmored ſtyfled theim brethes faylyng thei gaue vp god innocent ſoules ye ioyes heauen leauyng tourmētoures bodyes dedde bed whiche ye wretch perceaued firſt yt ſtrugglyng ye panges dea long liyng ſtill throughly dedde thei laied bodyes vpon ye bed fetched iames tirrell ſe theim whiche ſawe theim perfightly ded cauſed murtherers burie theim ſtayre foote metely depe grounde vnder greate heape ſtones thē rode iames tirrell great haſt kyng rychard ſhewed hym maner ye murther gaue hym greate thankes mēne ſaye made hym knight alowed buriall ſo vyle corner ſaiyng yt would haue theim buryed better place becauſe thei kynges ſoonnes lo honourable courage kyng would recompence deteſtable murther ſolempne obſequy wherupō preeſt ſir robert brakenburyes tooke theim vp buried theim ſuche place ſecretly occaſion death whiche verie ſhortlye whiche onely knewe truthe could neuer yet bee well perfighly knowen ſome ſaie kyng rychard cauſed yt preeſt take theim vp cloſe theim lead put theim coffine full hole hoked ye endes ii hokes yron ſo caſte place called ye blacke depes ye thamis mouth ſo yt thei ſhuld neuer riſe vp bee ſeen ye truth vnknowē reaſon ye ſaid preſte dyed ſo ſhortly diſcloſed neuer perſone ye would vtter truthe ſir iames tirrell towre treaſon committed kyng hēry ſeuenth bothe dighton examined together poynte bothe thei confeſſed murther bee dooen theſame maner haue hearde whether ye body remoued thei bothe affirmed thei neuer knewe thus haue learned theim yt muche knewe litle cauſe lye wer theſe ii noble prince theſe innocēt tēdre childrē borne ye moſte royall blood brought vp ī great welth likely lōge liue reigne rule yt realme treyterous tirāny taken depriued eſtate ſhortly ſhut vp priſon priuely ſlain murderd ye cruell ambicion vnnaturall vncle diſpiteous tourmētours whiche thynges euery part well pōdered god gaue worlde neuer notable exſample either ī vnſurety ſtādeth worldes weale miſchief worketh ye proud entrepriſe high hearte finally wretched ende enſueth ſuche diſpiteous crueltie firſt begynne wt ye miniſtres mile foreſt ſ martines le graūd peace meale miſerablye rotted awaye ihon dightō liued caleys long leſſe diſdeined hated poynted dyed great miſery ſir iames tirrell behedded towre hill treaſon kyng richard hymſelf ſlain ye feelde hacked hewed enemy handes haried horſbacke naked beyng ded heare diſpite torne tugged like curre dogge miſcheif yt toke wt leſſe thre yeres miſchief yt thre monethes comperable yet ye meane tyme ſpēt much trouble pein outward much feare dread anguiſh wt haue heard credible perſons ſuche ſecret wt chaūberers yt abhominable dede dooē neuer quiet minde neuer thought hymſelf ſure wēt abrode bodie preuely feinted eyen wherled hand euer dagger countenaunce maner like alwayes ſtryke toke eiuill reſt nightes laye long wakyng muſyng forweried care watche rather ſlōbred thē ſlept troubled wt fearfull dreames ſodeinly ſome tyme ſtert vp leapt bed looked aboute chambres ſo reſtleſſe hearte contynually toſſed tou 〈…〉 bled tedious inpreſſion ſtormy remēbraūce abhomynable murther exreable tirannie ſhortely vnquieted conſpiracie rather confederacie betwene duke buckynghm̄ many gentleman againſt hym ye ſhall next yere occaſiō duke kyng fell oute dyuerſe folke dyuerſe wyſe pretended duke haue hearde aſſone duke glouceſter death kyng edward come yorke ſolempne funerall ſeruice dooen kyng edward ſent hym ſecrete ſeruaunt called perſall ſuche meſſages haue hearde ye duke buckyngham came thre hundred horſſe northampton ſtill continued hym partener chief organe deuices till coronacion thei departed ſemyng verye frendes glouceſtre whence aſſone duke came home ſo highly turned hym ſo highly conſpired againſt hym māne would meruell wherof ye chaūge grewe ſo ſhorte ſpace ſaie occaſyon yt litle yt coronacion ye duke required kyng emōgeſt thrnges bee reſtored erle herffordes lāoes foraſmuche title whiche claymed inherytaunce ſomewhat interlaced title lancaſter whiche houſe made title croune enioyed theſame three dyſcentes menne knewe till houſe yorke depryued third kyng whiche henry ſixte kyng rychard ſomewhat miſtruſted conceaued ſuche indignacion reiected duke requeſt many ſpitefull minotary woordes whiche ſo wounded duke hearte wt hatred miſtruſt could neuer endure looke ryght kyng rychard euer feared owne lyfe ſo farrefoorth protectoure ſhould ryde coronacion feigned hymſelfe ſycke becauſe would dooe hym honoure takyng euell parte ſente hym woorde ryſe ryde would make hym caryed wherupō gorgeouſly apparelled ſumpteouſly trapped burnyng carte naues golde embrodered roade kyng london euell wyll woorſſe heart yt notwithſtandyng roaſe ye daye coronacion feaſte feignyng hym ſelfe ſycke whiche kyng richarde ſayde dooē hate ſpight hym therfore men ſayd eche theim euer lyued cōtynually ſuche hatred dyſtruſt duke looked verelye haue bene murthered glouceſtre frō whiche fayre maner departed ſurely ſuche right ſecrete bothe affyrme vntrue wyſe mēne thynke vnlykely depe dyſſymulyng nature bothe theſe menne well conſydered nede grene world protectoure hadde duke perell duke ſtoode yf fell ſuſpycion tyraunte ye protectoure would geue duke occaſyon dyſpleaſure duke protectoure occaſyon myſtruſt ſurely menne thynke kyng rychard hadde ſuche opynyon conceaued hym would neuer haue ſuffred hym aduoyd handes eſcape power verye true duke buckyngham high mynded man euell could beare glorye another ſo haue hearde ſome ſawe yt ſuche tyme croune ſet vpon protectoures hedde yie could neuer abyde ſight therof wryed hed another waye men ſayde well eaſe kyng richard well knowen well takē demaunde duke requeſt vncurteouſly reiected gentelye deferred bothe greate giftes high beheſtes moſte louyng truſtie maner departed kyng glouceſter ſone commyng home brecknocke hauyng kyng richardes commaundemēt doctour moorton byſhop ely haue hearde taken councell towre waxed hym famylyer whoſe onlye wyſedome abuſed pryde owne delyueraunce duke dyſtruccion byſhop man great natural wyt verye well learned honourable behaueoure lackyng wyſe wayes wynne fauour fyrſt vpon parte kyng henry whyle yt parte wealth neyther left forſoke woo fled realme quene prince kyng edward kyng henry pryſon neuer retourned felde barner whiche felde loſte vtterly ſubdued al parte takynges extynguiſhed kyng edward faſt faythe wyſedome onelye cōtent receaue hym alſo wooed hym come hym frō thenſforth ſecrete truſt ſpecyall fauoure nothyng deceaued beyng kyng edwardes death fyrſt taken tyraunt truthe kynge founde meane ſette duke toppe ioyned gentleman together ayde erle richemounde whiche named kyng henrye ſeuenth fyrſt deuyſyng maryage betwene ladye elizabeth daughter kynge edwarde fourthe whiche faythfull true ſeruyce declared maſters wt infinite benefite ye realme coniunccion bloddes lancaſtre yorke whoſe funerall tytles longe inquyeted realme manne afterwarde eſcaped duke 〈…〉 realme went rome neuer myndyng medle worlde tyl kyng henry ſeuenth ſent hym made hym archebyſhop cauntorbury chauncelour englande made cardinall lyued well mennes iudgementes dyed well retourne ye former purpoſe long often alternate proffe aſwel proſperytee aduerſe fortune gotten great experience verey mother maſtreſſe wyſedome depe inſight pollytike worldlye driftes whereby perceauynge nowe ye duke cōmen hym fed hym wt fayre woordes many pleaſaunt prayſes perceauyng grefe communicacions duke pryde nowe balke oute lytle brayde enuye towarde glorye kynge thereby feelynge hym eaſye fall oute yf matter well handled craftely ſoughte wayes prycke hym forwarde takynge alwayes occaſyon hys commynge alſo keepynge hymſelfe clooſe wythin hys bandes rather ſemed folowe hym leade hym duke beganne fyrſte prayſe boaſte kyng ſhewe muche profite realme ſhould take reigne byſhoppe morton aunſwered ſurely lorde folye lye ſure yf woulde ſwere contrarye ye would beleue yf worlde would haue begone would haue wyſhed kyng henryes ſoonne croune kynge edwarde woulde haue bene true faythfull ſubiecte god ordeyned hym loſe kyng edwarde reigne neuer ſo madde dead manne ſtryue agaynſt quycke ſo euer kynge edwarde faythfull true chapeleyn gladde would haue bene chyldren ſhoulde haue ſucceded hym howbeit yf ſecrete iudgemente god haue otherwyſe prouyded purpoſe ſpurne agaynſte prycke laboure ſet vp god pulleth downe late protectoure nowe kyng woorde left ſauynge ſaide hadde alreadye medled muche worlde would daye medle booke bede ferther longed duke ſore heare woulde haue ſayde becauſe ended kynge ſo ſodeynlye ſtopped exhorted hym famylyerly betwene theim bothe bee bolde ſaye whatſoeuer thought whereof faythfullye promyſed ſhoulde neuer come hurte paraduenture good woulde hym ſelfe entended vſe hys faythfull ſecrete aduyce counſayle ſayed onlye cauſe whyche procured kynge haue hym hys cuſtodye myghte recon hym ſelfe home elles hadde bene putte handes theim wyth whome ſhoulde haue founde lyke fauoure biſhoppe right humblye thanked hym ſayed good faythe lorde loue muche talke prynces thynge oute perell althoughe woorde bee without faute pleaſeth prince conſtrue euer thynke iſopes tale lyon proclaymed payne deathe ſhoulde horned beaſtes come wood one beaſte bonche fleſhe growing oute hedde fledde greate pace ye foxe ſawe hym flye haſte aſked hym whether fledde fayth ꝙ neither wote ne recke ſo hence becauſe proclamacyon made agaynſte horned beaſtes foole ꝙ foxe lyon neuer ment whiche thou haſte horne thy hedde mary ꝙ wote well ynoughe yf ſaye horne duke laughed merely tale ſaied lorde warraunte neither lyon bore ſhall pycke matter thyng ſpoken ſhall neuer come nere care good faythe ſyr ſaied byſhoppe yf dyd thyng aboute ſaye taken aſwell god mente coulde deſerue thanke yet taken wene would myghte happen turne lytle good leſſe longed duke muche wherupon byſhop ſaied good faith lord late protectoure • ith kyng poſſeſſyon purpoſe diſpute title welthe realme whereof grace hathe nowe gouernaunce wherof ſelfe poore membre aboute wyſh thoſe good habilitees wherof hath already righte many litle nedyng prayſe yet mighte haue pleaſed god better ſtore haue geuen hym ſome ſuche excellent vertues mete rule realme oure lord hath planted perſone grace lefte againe whiche woordes duke perceauyng byſhop bare vnto hym good hearte fauoure myſtruſted entre plaine cōmunicacion hym ſo farre ye laſte byſhoppe declared hym ſelfe bee one theim would gladly helpe richard vſurped croune mighte bee depoſed knowen howe myghte conuenientely bee broughte paſſe ye ſuche perſone true title inheritaunce vnto ſame might bee reſtored therunto vpon ſaied duke knowing biſhoppe bee manne prudence fidelitee opened hym whole hart entent ſaying lorde haue elder doughter edward fourth byſhop ely ryghte well alowed bothe deuyce purpoſe duke alſo maner waye howe matter ſhoulde bee broughte effecte founde meanes reynold breye ſeruaūr margarete mother realme alſo aduauncemente bloodde debated nowe came ſo paſſe duke buckyngham ladye margaret mother ſaied henrye bene communicacyon ſame matter ſaied lady margarete deuiſed ſame meane waye depoſycion myghte bee broken vnto quene elizabeth wyfe kyng edwade fourthe beynge sanctuarye hereupon ſhe cauſed one lewes phyſicyan owne name thoughe came hym ſelfe breake matter vnto quene ſaying yf ſhe would
