henry earle richemounte whiche blood henry ſixte whome yf ſhe woulde content yt marye elizabeth eldeſt doughter ſhoulde ſyde bee made righte many frendes ſhe parte myghte helpe lyke maner wherby doubte ſhoulde come paſſe ſhoulde poſſeſſe croune mooſt rightfull inheritaunce whiche matter ſhe heard liked excedingly well ſo much ſhe counceled ſaied phiſicyan breake ye ſame vnto maiſtreſſe ladye margaret knowe mynde therein promiſyng vpon woorde ſhe would make frendes kyng edwarde take parte ſayed henrye yf woulde ſworne came poſſeſſyon croune woulde immediately take maryage elyzabeth eldeſt doughter elles yf ſhe lyued tyme would take cicile yongeſt doughter whereupon ſayde lewes retourned vnto ladye margarete hys mayſtreſſe declarynge vnto whole mynd entent quene thē ſhortly agreed betwene theſe two wemen wyth al ſpede thys matter ſhold ſet forwarde ſo much lady margarete brake thys matter vnto reynolde bray wyllynge hym moue ſet forwarde ſame wt ſuche ſhoulde perceaue eyther hable doo good wyllynge thereunto quene deuyſed one chryſtopher whome foreſayde lewes phyſicyan promoted ſeruyce ſhoulde bee ſente brytayne henrye geue hym knowledge theyr myndes ſhoulde prepare apoynt hym ſelfe redye come wale ſhoulde fynde ayde helpe ynonghe readye receaue hym ſhortly yt came vnto knowledge duke buckingham himſelfe afore entended ſame matter whereupon ſhe thoughte yt ſhould mete ſende ſome meſſenger reputacyon credyte thys chryſtopher ſo kepte hym home ſente hughe conewaye wyth greate ſome monye wyllynge hym declare vnto henrye thynges ſhould haſt hym come lande wale aforeſayde hym one rycharde guilforde oute kente ſente one thomas ramey wyth ſame meſſage whyche two meſſengers came maner bothe one tyme brytayn earle henrye declared vnto hym theyr commyſſiōs whiche meſſage henry perceaued throughly heard reioyſed harte gaue thankes vnto god fully purpoſyng al conuenyente ſpede take iourney towardes england deſiryng aide helpe duke brytayne promiſe thanckfull recompence god ſhould ſende hym come ryghte duke britayne notwithſtanding longe required thomas hutton purpoſely ſent hym kyng richard meſſage monye efte ſones impriſone ſaied henry erle richemoūt continually kepe holde ſame frome cō minge englande yet gladneſſe fauoure inclined deſyre henry aided hym might menne monye ſhypes neceſſaryes henry whyle might accordynglye appoynte furnyſhe hym ſelfe remayned brytayne ſendyng afore foreſayde hughe coneway thomas ramney whiche two hym trewe faithful beare tidynges englande vnto frendes commynge ende myghte prouydentlye ordre thynges aſwell commodyous receauynge hym comminge alſo foreſeynge ſuche daungers myghte befalle aduoydinge ſuche trappes ſnares rycharde thyrde hys complyces myght bee ſette hym company ſhould bryng hym meane tyme frendes henrye care ſtudye dilygence wroughte thynges vnto purpoſe belongynge thoughe ſecretlye wrought conueyed emonge ſo greate nombre poſſible yet pryuye knowledge therof came eares kyng rychard althoughe firſte hearynge muche abaſſhed yet thought beſt dyſſemble matter thoughe knowledge therof whyle myghte ſecretly gather vnto hym power ſtrengthe ſecrete ſpyall emonge people get perfyght knowledge whole matter chiefe autoures contryuers ſame becauſe knewe chiefe princypal theim vnto whō owne conſcience knewe hadde geuen moſte iuſt cauſes enemytee thought neceſſary firſt dyſpatche ſame duke oute waye wherfore vnto duke addreſſed letter enfarced replenyſhed humanytee frendſhippe famylyaritee ſweteneſſe woordes wyllyng deſyryng ſame come vnto hym conuenyent ſpede ferther gaue commaundemente meſſenger caryed letter ſhoulde behalfe make many high gaye promyſes vnto ye duke gentle meanes perſuade ſame come vnto hym ye duke myſtruſtyng ye fayre woordes promyſes ſo ſodenly offred hym whoſe wylye craftes meanes knewe ſondrye exſamples afore practiſed deſyred ye kynges perdon excuſyng ſelf deſeaſed ſicke might aſſerteined ye poſſyble wer hym come would abſent hym ſelf frō grace thys excuſe kyng would admitte eftſones directed vnto ye duke letter roughe ſorte wythoute manacynge threatenynge onleſſe woulde accordynge hys dutye repayer vnto hym hys callynge whereunto duke plainely made aunſwer woulde come vnto knewe hys enemye immedyatelye duke prepared hym ſelfe make warre agaynſt hym perſwaded hys complyces partaker hys intente wyth poſſyble expedycion ſome one place ſome another ſturre agaynſte kynge rycharde thys meanes maner one tyme houre thomas marque dorceſter reyſed armye wythin country yorke beyng hym ſelfe late come forthe ſāctuarye meanes helpe thomas rowell preſerued ſaued frome perel death alſo deuonſhyre edwarde courtenay wyth hys brother peter byſhoppe excetter reyſed lyke maner armye kent rychard guyl ford accompanied wyth certayn gentylmen cayſed vp people foreſayde thys done maner one moment king ye meane tyme gathered together gret power ſtrēgth thynkyng yt beſt purſuyng euery one hys enemyes dyſparkle hys cōpaygnie ſmal flokes determyned let paſſe others withal whole puiſaunce ſet vpon chiefe heade ſaye duke buckynghm̄ ſo takyng iourneye londō went towardes saliſbury thentent might ſette vpon ye ſaid duke caſe might haue perfight knowledge ye ſame laye felde embatailed nowe kyng within twoo dayes iourney saliſbury ye duke attempted mete hym beyng accompaignied great ſtrength welſhmen therunto en forced coherted lordly commaundement lyberall wage hyre whiche thyng deede ye cauſe thei fell hym forſooke hym wherfore beyng ſodenly forſaken menne neceſſite conſtrained flee whiche dooyng manne caſt ſodeine therfore greate feare ſodeine chaunge fortune reaſon theſame feare knowyng become hyde hed ſuche caſe beſt dooe ſecretly conueighed hym ſelf hous homffraye banaſtar conceaued ſure hope confidence finde faithfull truſtie vnto hym becauſe theſame thē ſeruaunt entendyng remayne ſecrete vntill might either reiſe newe armie el ſome meanes cōueigh hym ſelf brytein henry erle rychemount aſſone theothers whiche attempted theſame entrepryſe againſt ye kyng knowledge duke forſaken compaignie fled could bee foūde thei beyng ſtryken ſodein feare made euery māne hym ſelf ſuche ſhift might beyng vtter deſpayre health life either gotte theim ſāctuaryes deſerte place el aſſaied eſcape ouer ſea many theim deede arryued ſauely britain emong theſe whoſe name enſue peter curteney biſhop exceter brother edward erle deuonſhire thomas marque dorceſtre ſoonne thomas beyng verye yoūg chylde ihō bourſhere ihon welſhe edward wooduyle ſtoute manne armes brother elizabeth quene robert willoughby gyles dawbeneye thomas harondell ihon cheiny twoo brother wyllyam berkeley wyllyam brandō thomas brother rychard edgecome theſe moſte parte knightes alſo ihon halwell edwarde poyntz excellēt good capitain chriſtopher vrſwicke ihon moorton biſhop ely theſelf ſame tyme together ſondrye noble gentleman ſailed flaundres richard kyng nowe come saliſbury gotten perfight knowledge theſe party ſought ſlie realme dyligence haſt might bee ſent ye porte tounes theraboute make ſure ſteye none theim might paſſe vntaken made proclamacion yt whoſoeuer would bryng hym knowledge duke buckynghm bee ſhould haue rewarde bō deman frebome fre pardon beſydes thouſand pounde moneye furthermore becauſe vnderſtode thomas hutton newely retourned oute britein afore mencioned fraunces duke brytain would onelye holde henry erle rychmount priſone ſake alſo readie helpe theſame henry menne money ſhippes might againſt hym ſette dyuerſe ſondry ſhippes place conuenyent ſeacoſtes brytain ward henry ſhould come waye might either bee taken arriuall el might bee kept frō landyng coaſte england furthermore euerie coaſte corner ye realme laied wondrefull wayte watche take partely enemy ſpecially theſaid duke buckynghm̄ wherupon theſaid homffrey banaſter mede loſyng life goodes diſcloſed hym vnto kynges inquyſy • ymediatly tooke hym foorthwith brought hym saliſbury kyng rychard duke beyng dylygently examined vttred without maner refuſall ſtyckyng ſuche thynges knewe truſtyng plain confeſſion ſhould haue lybertee ſpeake kyng whiche made moſte inſtaūt humble peticion might dooe aſſone cōfeſſed offence towardes kyng rychard oute hande behedded death ye duke receaued handes kyng rychard holpen affayrs purpoſes beyonde god forbode whyle theſe thynges wer hand england henry erle richmount made readye hoſte ſtrength nombre fiue thouſand brytones fiftene ſhippes ye daye apoynted departure beyng nowe come whiche ye twelfe daye moneth octobre yere lorde god thouſand foure hundred lxxxiiii ſeconde yere ye reigne kyng richard hauyng fayre wynde hoyſed vp ſayles ſetforwarde towarde night came ſuche tempeſt thei diſperſed one another ſome britain ſome normandy ſhip whiche henry one ſhip toſſed night waues ſea tempeſt mornyng came waxed ſomewhat calme faire weder thei come toward south parte england hauen porte called poole theſaid henry ſawe ſhores bankes ſette full harneſſedmen whiche ſouldyours apoynted wayte kyng rychard haue ſaied comyng landyng erle henry abode gaue commaundement manne ſhould land yt comyng ſhippes meane tyme wayted theim ſent litle bote fewe lād knowe thei ſtoode ſhore frēdes enemy thoſe ſouldyours beeyng taught thei ſhould ſaie aunſwered thei frendes henry appoynted ye duke buckynghm̄ abide commyng conducte hym thoſe caſtelles holdes tentes pauylyons ar •• llary warre laie remayned hym greate power entended nowe ſpede ſet vpon kyng rychard nowe ſle • feare cleane without prouiſion therfore beſought hym come alande henry ſuſpectyng bee fraude ſaw none ſhippes apered hoyſed vp ſatles hauyng meruelous good wynde euen apoynted hym god delyuer hym great ieopardy ſayled backe agayn mandy landyng compaignie laboures areſted theim ſpace iii dayes determynyng go thence afoote brytayne meane ſent meſſengers vnto charles frenche kynge ſonne lewes lytle departed ſechyng hym lybertee lycence paſſe thorough normādy brytayn young kyng charles beeyng ſory fortune onlye ready well pleaſed graunt paſſage alſo ſent hym moneye helpe hym foorthe iourneye henry knewe kynges mynde doubtyng great humanytee gentlenes ſent awaye ſhippes towardes britayne ſet hym ſelfe forwardes iourneye made greate haſte tyll meſſengers retourned whiche greate gentlenes receaued kyng reioyſed hearte luſtye ſtomacke good hope ſet forwarde brytayne take ferther counſayle affayres brytayn receaued frō frendes englande knowledge duke buckyngham behedded marque dorceſtre greate nombre ye noble men englande bene lytle ſeke hym wer veneti cytie brytayne whiche thynges beynge knowen erle one parte greately lament death euel chaunce chiefe princypall frende yet parte greatlye reioyſed ſo many noble menne take parte battayll therfore conceauynge good hope opinion purpoſe ſhoulde well frame come paſſe determyned hym ſelfe expedycion ſet foorth warde therupon wente place brytayn called rhedon thence ſent marque noble men ſhould come vnto hym hearde henrye ſafe returned brytayne reioyſed lytle thei thought landed englande ſo fallen handes kyng richarde made lytle haſte tyll wer come vnto hym whiche met greatloye gladneſſe aſwell parte began talke prepenſed matter nowe chriſtmaſſe come whiche daye altogether aſſembled churche ſware fayth truthe one another henry ſware firſt promyſyng aſſone ſhould poſſeſſe ye croune england woulde marye elyzabeth doughter edward iiii warde ſware feaultie homage vnto hym euē though already bene kyng ſo tyme foorthe dyd take hym promyſyng hym thei would ſpende bothe lyfes goodes hym richard ſhould lēger reigne ouer theim dooen henry declared theſe thynges duke britayne praiynge deſyryng hym nowe helpe woulde ayde hym greater nombre menne alſo lende hym frendly honeſt ſomme moneye might nowe recouer right enheritaunce croune england vnto yt called deſyred al lordes nobilitee realme whiche god wyllyng moſte aſſured poſſeſſe poſſeſſiō would moſte faythfully reſtore ſame duke promyſed hym ayde vpon truſte wherof beganne make redye ſhippes might expedicion bee redy ſayle tyme ſhould loſte whiche tyme kyng richard agayn retourned london taken dyuerſe theim yt wer conſpyracy yt ſay george browne roger clyfforde thomas selenger knyghtes alſo thomas ramme robert clyfford dyuerſe cauſed put death called parliament wherin deereed thoſe fled oute lande ſhould reputed taken enemyes realme landes goodes bee forfayte confiſcate content preade ſmal thyng cauſed alſo great taxe ſome monye leuyed people ye large giftes lyberalytee firſt vſed buye fauoures frendſhippes many brought nede nothing like yt thomas stanley ſhoulde haue bene reputed takē one thoſe enemy becauſe woorkyng margarete wife mother vnto henry erle richemoūt noted ye chiefe hed worker cōſpyracy aſmuch thought ſmall purpoſe wemen coulde dooe thomas beynge nothyng fauty dely • ed cōmaūded ſhould ſuffre margarete wyfe haue ſeruaūtes neither yt ſhe ſhould go abroad ſhut vp yt thence foorth ſhe ſhould ſende meſſage neyther ſoonne frendes wherby hurte mighte wrought agaynſt kyng whiche commaundemēt accomplyſhed authoryte ſame perliament peace concluded scottes whiche lytle ſkyrmyſhed borderer thyng brought paſſe ye kyng ſuppoſed conſpiracye bee clene auoyded aſmuche duke compaignie put death alſo certen bannyſhed yet kyng richard daylye vexed troubled partelye myſtruſtynge owne ſtrength partely fearyng commyng henrye compaignye ſo lyued myſerable caſe becauſe would ſo continue lenger determyned hym ſelfe put awaye cauſe feare buſyneſſe either pollecye elles ſtrength hadde thus purpoſed hym ſelfe thought nothyng better tempte duke britayn yet eyther money prayer ſome ſpeciall rewarde becauſe yt kepyng erle henry moſte chiefly becauſe knewe yt yt might delyuer hym trouble delyueryng impriſoning ſayed henry wherfore incontmentlye ſente vnto duke certein ambaſſadoures whiche ſhould promeſſe vnto hym beſyde greate rewardes broughte theim geue hym yerely reuenues landes henry lordes beyng hym yf woulde receyte ambaſſadoures put theim pryſone ambaſſadoures beynge departed come duke laye could haue communicacion hym aſmuch extreme ſickneſſe wyttes feble weake wherfore one peter landoſe treaſourer manne bothe pregnaunte wytte greate authoritee tooke matter hand whiche cauſe afterwarde hated lordes britain peter engliſhe ambaſſadoures communicacion declaring hym kynges meſſage deſyred hym inſtantlye aſmuche knewe might bring theyr purpoſe paſſe woulde graunt vnto kyng richardes requeſt ſhoulde haue yerely reuenues landes ſayed lordes peter conſidering greatly hated ye lordes owne nacion thoughte yf myght bring paſſe thoroughe kyng richarde haue theſe greate poſſeſſyons yerely reuenues ſhould bee hable matche theim well ynough care ruſhe theim whereupon aunſwered ambaſſadoures would doo richard dyd deſire yf brake promeſſe hym hatred bare vnto henry hated hym longe ſaued lyfe earle henry greate • eoperdye ſuche good fortune englande craftye compacte tooke place whyle letter meſſengers ranne betwene peter kyng kichard iohn biſhoppe ely beinge flaundres certifyed preeſt whiche came oute england whoſe name chriſtopher vrſwicke whole circumſtaunce deuyce purpoſe wherupon ſpede ſayed byſhop cauſed ſaied preeſt ſame daye cary know ledge therof britayn henry erle richemounte willing hym noble men dyſpatche theim ſelues wt poſſible haſte fraunce henry veneti whē heard fraud without tariaunce ſent chriſtopher vnto charles frenche kyng deſiring lycence henry noble men myght ſafely come fraunce thing ſone obteigned meſſenger retourned ſpede lorde prince earle henry ſetting buſineſſe good ſtaye ordre mighte talked lytle made fewe counſail herof expedicyon hereof cauſed therle penbrucke ſecretly cauſe noble men take horſes diſſembling ride vnto duke bretain came vttermoſt partes therof ſhould forſake waye led theim toward duke make fraunce euer might dooing euery thing biddē loſte tyme ſo ſped theim ſhortely obteygned gate coūtie angeou henry within ii dayes folowyng ſtyll veneti tooke iiii fyue ſeruauntes hym feigned thoughe woulde haue ryden therby viſyte frende foraſmuche many engliſhmenne lefte toune manne ſuſpected thynge kepte ryghte waye ſpace fyue myles forſooke turned ſtreyghte woode thereby tooke vpon hym ſeruauntes apparell putte apparell vpon hys ſeruaunte ſo tooke one theym hym whome waited thoughe bene ſeruaunte maiſter conuenyente ſpedy haſte ſo ſette forthe theyr iourney tyme loſte made tariaunce way onelye baitynge theyr horſes ſo ſhortly recouered coaſtes angeou companye within foure dayes earle thus eſcaped peter receaued kyng richard confirmacion graunte promiſes made betreiyng henry noble wherfore ſaide peter ſente oute hym horſes menne ſuche expedicion ſpede haue taken hym ſcacely erle entred fraunce one houre heles englyſhe menne beyng aboue noumbre thre hundreth veneti hearing earle noble fled ſo ſodeinly withoute knowledge aſtonyed maner deſpaired theyr lyues happened contrary theyr exſpectacyon duke britaine taking matter ſo vnkyndely henry ſhould bee ſo vſed hym feare ſhoulde bee compelled flee lande lytle vexed peter althoughe ignoraunte fraude crafte wrought hym yet layed whole faute hym therfore called vnto hym edward poyninges edward wood vile deliuering vnto theim foreſayde monye ye henrye deſyred duke lende hym towarde charge iourney commaunded theim conuey conducte engliſh menne ſeruauntes vnto hym paying theyr expenſes deliuer ſayde ſome monye vn earle earle ſawe menne come hearde comfortable newes lytle reioyſed deſiring meſſengers returned ſhewe vnto duke truſted ere long time ſhewe ſelfe bee vnthankeful greate kyndneſſe nowe ſhewed vnto hym within fewe dayes earle went vnto charles french kyng whome rendred thankes great benefites kind neſſe receaued hym cauſe comming fyrſte declared beſought helpe ayde whiche ſhoulde bee immor tall benefite hym lordes whome generallye called vnto kyngdome foraſmuch ſo abhorred tiranny kyng rychard charles promiſed hym helpe bade good chere take care would gladly declare vnto hym beneuolence ſame tyme charles remoued tooke hym henry noble menne whyle henry remained iohn earle oxenford whome ſpoken put priſone edward fourth caſtell hammes alſo iames blounte capteine caſtell iohn forſkewe knyghte porter towne caleies came vnto hym iames capitain becauſe lefte wife ye caſtell dyd furnyſhe ſame good gariſon men departure henry ſawe therle meaſure glad ye ſo noble man greate experience battayl ſo valiaunt hardie knight thought bee moſte feithfull ſure ſomuche time edward ye fourth continuall battail hym defending henry ſyxte thought nowe ſo well apointed coulde deſire bee better therfore cōmunicated vnto hym whole affaire bee ordred ruled hym longe charles frenche kyng remoued paris whome henry folowed againe moued beſoughte kyng moſte fauourably kindely entreteigned hym time wordes alſo dedes yt would lykewiſe pleaſe hym yet ſo much extend fauoure beneuolence vnto hym nowe woulde ayde helpe hym forwarde iourney yt onely alſo lordes nobilytee englande myghte iuſtely haue cauſe knowlage confeſſe meane fauoure goodneſſe reſtored againe poſſeſſyon enherytaunces whiche withoute hym coulde well bryng paſſe meane fortune ſuche ye many englyſhe menne came ouerdaylye oute englande vnto many whiche paris amonge whome diuerfe ſtudentēs fell vnto parte bothe leſſe ſpecially one whoſe name richard foxe preeſt beyng manne ſynguler good wytte learning whome henry ſtreyght waye reteigned cōmitted ſecretes vnto hym whome alſo afterward promoted many hyghe promocyons laſte made hym biſhop wincheſter richarde hearyng conſpiracye greate ayde dayly wente ouer vnto henry thought yet might bring paſſe henry ſhould couple maryage blood king edwarde ſhoulde dooe well ynoughe hym kept hym poſſeſſyon croune deuyſed hym ſelfe wayes meanes myghte bee howe bryng paſſe fyrſte thoughte bee beſte fayre woordes large promeſſes attempte quene whoſe fauoure obteygned doubted ſhortelye fynde meanes haue bothe doughters oute handes owne reſted nothynge yf hym ſelfe myghte fynde meanes warde marye one ſame doughters whereby thought ſhoulde make ſure ſafe vtter diſapoyntinge henrye wherupon ſente vnto quene beynge sanctuarye dyuerſe ſondrye meſſengers ſhoulde excuſe pourge hym facte afore dooen towardes ſettynge forthe matter pleſaunte woordes hye promyſes bothe alſo ſonne thomas lorde marque dorſet thynges coulde deſyred theſe meſſengers beyng men grauitee handled quene ſo e •• ftly anone ſhe beganne bee alured herken vnto theim fauourably ſo concluſion ſhe promyſed obedient kyng requeſt forgettyng iniuries dooen parte remembryng ye promeſſe ſhe made maigarete henryes mother firſt ſhe delyuered doughters handes kyng rychard ſhe ſent preuely lorde marque ſonne beyng parys wt henry ye haue heard wyllyng hym forſake henrye whome ſpedely returne englande thynges perdoned forgeuen ſhe fauoure frendſhip ye kyng ſhould highly aduauncement honoure kyng richard whē quene elizabeth thus brought fooles paradyce receaued al brother doughters ſanctuary palayce thought nowe remayned nothyng dooen caſtyng awaye deſtroiyng owne wife whiche thynge wholy purpoſed decreed within hym ſelfe nothyng feared hym ſo much mooſte cruell deteſtable murder loſyng good opynion ye thought people conceyued hym ye haue heard faigned hym ſelfe good mā thought people eſtemed hym euen ſo notwithſtandyng ſhortly foreſaide vngracious purpoſe ouercame al honeſt feare firſt abſteyned beddyng lyyng alſo found ſelf greued barrēneſſe wife ſhe vnfruteful brought hym forth chyldren complamyng therof greuouſly vnto ye noble realme chieflye aboue vnto thomas rotherame archebiſhoppe yorke whome delyuered lytle afore oute pryſon whiche byſhop gather quene ſhould rid waye ere long ſuche experience kyng richardes complexciō practiſed many lyke thynges longe theſame tyme alſo made dyuerſe ſecrete frendes preuy theſame coniecture cauſed rumoure ronne amōg commen people woulde haue ye autoure knowen yt quene dead thentent yt ſhe hearyng meruelous rumour ſhould take ſo greueous conceyt anone ſhe ſhould fall ſome great diſeaſe ſo would aſſay waye caſe ſhould chaunce afterward ſicke dead otherwyſe murdred ye people might impute death vnto ye thought ſhe tooke el ye ſickeneſſe whē quene heard ſo horryble rumour death ſprōge abroade among commen people ſhe ſuſpected matter ſuppoſed worlde ende incontinently ſhe wente kyng lamentable countenaunce wepyng teares aſked hym whether ſhe dooen thyng whereby might iudge worthy ſuffer death kyng made aunſwere ſmilyng diſſimulyng countenaūce flatteryng woordes byddyng bee good comforte plucke vp heart ſuche thyng toward knewe howe ſo euer fortuned either ſorowe el poyſonyng within fewe day quene dedde afterwarde buryed abbay weſtminſter ſame anne one rychard earle warwikes doughters whiche cōtracted prince edwarde kyng hē ry ſixt ſoonne kyng beyng thus delyuered wife fantaſied pace ladye elizabeth nice deſiryng wiſe mary becauſe menne yee mayden ſelf abhorred vnlawfull deſire thyng mooſte deteſtable determined hym ſelf make greate haſt matter chiefly pecke trouble fearyng leaſt yt noble menne ſome would forſake hym runne vnto henry part leſte would fauoure ſecrete conſpiracy made hym ſo ende almooſt doubte alſo parte commen people ſo greate diſpeare many theim rather bee accompted noumbre enemy put theim ſelfes ieopardy bothe loſſe body goodes takyng parte emongeſt thoſe noble menne feared firſt thomas standley wyllyam brother gylbert talbote greate noūbre whoſe purpoſe▪ though kyng rychard ignoraunt neuertheleſſe truſted one theim leſt thomas standley becauſe maryed henryesanother maye well appeare fol oweth ſayd thomas woulde haue departed courte vnto owne manſion recreacion ſaide ye truthe becauſe woulde bee readyneſſe receaue henry ayde hym commyng realme kyng let hym would ſuffer hym departe vntyll ſuche tyme left courte behynde hym george strange ſoonne heyre pledge whyle kynge richarde thus wrapped feare care ye tumulte come lo euen tydynges came henrye entred lande caſtell hammes prepared receiue henry meanes erle oxenforde whiche fled iames blunte keper caſtell vnto henry kyng rychard thynkyng begynnyng ſtey matter ſent forth haſt • greater parte calyce recouer ſaid caſtell thoſe caſtell thei ſawe aduerſaries make towardes theim ſpedely thei armed theim ſelfes defence al haſt ſent meſſengers hēry deſyryng hym ayde henry forthwith ſent erle oxenforde choſen ſorte menne aſſiſt theim firſt commyng laid ſiege farre caſtell whyle kyng rychardes menne turned backe hauyng yie towardes theim thomas brandon thirty valeaunt menne otherſide gate ouer water caſtell ſtrength theim within thei within laid heard charge without ye otherſide erle oxenford ſo valiantly aſſayled backeſide thei glad make proclamaciō theim within thei would content geue ouer caſtell thei ſhould haue free liberte departe euer thei erle oxenforde hearyng whiche came onely ſaue frendes hurte namely iames bluntes wife contented condicion departed ſaufgarde frendes returning backe henry whiche paris kyng rychard informed yt frenche kyng wery henry compaignie would doo nothyng hym wherby henry nowe hable maner helpe ſelf ſo poſſible yt ſhuld preuaile goo forwarde thenterpriſe thoughte haue taken hande agaynſt kynge rycharde kynge rycharde beeyng brought thus falſe paradice thought hym ſelfe bee feare cauſe ſhould beynge ſo ſure one wake oute hys ſlepe trouble hym ſelfe furder therefore called backe hys nauye ſhyppes redy vpon ſea whyche fullye furnyſhed haue ſcoured ſeas yet ſuretie leaſt ſhould bee ſodenly oppreſſed gaue commaundemente greatte men dwellynge ſea ſyde ſpecyally welſhemen watche nyghte daye leaſte aduerſaries ſhuld haue eny oportunitee entre lande faſhyon time warre thoſe dwell ſees ſide ſhould make bekyns higheſt place whiche might bee ſene afarre ſo ſhould chaunce enemyes aryue towarde lande ſhould fyre theyr bekyns rayſe countreye thentent quickely place place might aſcerteyned whole matter alſo arme theim ſelfes ſpedelye agaynſte theyr enemy ſo come purpoſe agayn kyng richard thorough aforeſaide tydynges beganne bee careleſſe recheleſſe ſaye power withſtand deſteny honge ouer hedde suche prouydent iuſtyce god manne dooeth leſte knowe prouyde beware vengeaunce god euen hande offence go forth ye tyme henry earle richemounte remayned fraunce entretyng ſuyng ayde helpe frenche men many chiefe noble men realme gouernaunce becauſe young age charles kyng fel ſomewhat diſſencion whiche variaunce lewes prynce orlyaunce chiefe hedde whiche becauſe maryed iohanne kynges ſyſter looked haue bene chiefe gouernoure realme meanes came paſſe one man princypall gouernaunce realme therefore henry erle conſtraigned ſue vnto noble ſeuerallye one another deſyrynge praiynge theim aide helpe purpoſe thus matter prolonged meane tyme thomas marque dorcet whome ſpake afore preuely ſent come home mother partely myſtruſtynge henrye ſhould preuayle partly greate large promeſſes kyng richard made hym whiche letter ſayd marque receaued beleuyng thynges mother wrote vnto hym alſo thynkyng henry ſhould neuer preuayle frenchemen mocke daylye hym ſodeynly night tyme conueyed hym ſelfe parys great ſpede made towardes flaūders whiche thyng ye erle engliſhe lordes heard thei wer ſore aſtonned amaſed ſpede purchaſed charles kyng lycence commaundement marque might ſteyed wherſoeuer wer found wt dominion fraūce chiefly ſecrete councel knewe purpoſe cōmaundemēt quickly obteyned poſtes made forth euery waye emōgeſt one humfrey cheyncy plaiyng ye parte good blooddehounde ſo truely ſmelled folowed trace found toke marque ſo handled perſuaded hym gentle good woordes ſhortely content retourne henry beyng delyuered chaunce thought beſt prolonge matter farther leaſt ſhould looſe preſent oportunytee alſo wery frendes looked hym englande wherfore made haſte ſet forewarde ſmall army obteyned frenche kyng alſo borowed ſome money ſome frendes whiche left marque ihon burchere behynde pledge ſo ſetting forward came roan whyle taryed prepared ſhippyng ye hauen seyne tydynges cam hym ye kyng richardes wyfe deade purpoſed mary lady elyſabeth kyng edwardes eldeſt doughter nice maried cycile ſyſter mannes ſonne lāde far vnderneth degre whiche thyng henry ſore amaſed troubled thynkyng meanes al purpoſe daſhed waye hym come kyngdome maryage one kyng edwardes doughters menes alſo feared leaſt frendes englande would ſhrynke frō hym lacke honeſt title thei conſulted vpon matter thei thought beſt cary lytle proue might gette helpe make mo frendes among thought beſt adioyne lord harbarte vnto theim whiche mā great power wale yt ſhould brought paſſe meanes lorde harbarte ſyſter maryable whō henry would content mary would take part brīg al matter paſſe meſſengers ſent henry erle northhumberlande whiche maryed ſyſter ſo ſhould bryng matter wayes ſo beſet meſſengers could come hym meane ſeaſon came veray good tydynges ihon ap morgan temporall lawyer whiche ſignified vnto theim ſyr ryce ap thomas noble valiaunt man ihon sauage fauoured parte earneſtlye alſo ſyr reynolde braye prepared greate ſumme mony wage battayl parte helpe hym therfore woulde ſhould make haſt euer could make towarde wale henry ſpedely prepared hym ſelfe becauſe would lynger frendes lenger made prayer vnto almightye god might haue good ſucceſſe iourney two thouſande menne fewe ſhyppes calendes auguſt ſayled hauen seyne ſeuēth daye whiche xxii daye auguſt aryued wale aboute ſonne ſet lāded wilforde hauen ye parte whiche called dale hearde yt dyuerſe layde wayte hym kepe hym backe thence mornyng betymes remoued towarde towne called harford tēne myle dale ioyfully receyued contrarye tydynges brought hearde normādy afore ſyr ryce ap thomas ihon sauage wythal euer coulde make kyng richardes parte notwithſtandynge ſuche tydynges ſent theim frō menne pembruche valiaūt gentlemā whoſe name arnold butteler reioyſed heartes whiche yf former offence might bee remitted woold bee redyneſſe ſticke vnto owne geſpare erle henryes company meanes beeyng encreaſed departed frō harforde fyue myle towarde cardygane refreſhed menne ſodenly came rumoure vnto hym lorde harbarte whiche dwelled carmerdyne nye hande greate armye menne whiche rumoure greate ſturre amongeſte theim euerye manne tooke hym ſelfe weapon made theim ſelfes redye nede fight lytle afrayed tyl ſuch tyme henrye ſent horſemen trye ye truthe whiche thei came agayn declared thynges quiet ther ſuche thyng moſte maſter gryffythes verye noble man conforte theim gladden heartes whiche although ioyned hym ſelf lorde harberte tyme cleued henry ſuche companye although fewe theſame tyme came ihon ap morgā vnto hym henry went ſtyll forward caried almoſte place becauſe would make ſuer woorke better ſpede inuaded ſuche place afore thei armed againſt hym ye whiche place bette downe wt litle ſtrēgth afterward hauyng knowlage ſpyes ye lorde harbert ſyr ryce redynes geue hym battail determyned ſet vpō theim either put theim flight orels make theim ſweare homage feaultee vnto hym take theim wt hym hoſte againſt kyng richard becauſe woulde aſcertayne frendes englande howe matter went forwad hym ſent mooſt truſtye frendes ladye margarete mother standely talbot moſt eſpecial frendes certain commaundementes effecte commaundementes intended helpe hys frendes paſſe ouer seuerne shreweſbury make toward london ther fore deſyred theim thoſe councell tyme place conuenient mete hym meſſaungers going forth theſe commiſſyons henry went forward toward shreweſbury waye mette ſyr rice ap thomas great noumber menne came vnto hym parte two dayes afore henry promyſed hym bee chiefe ruler wale ſoone came croune yf would come vnto hym afterward gaue hym dede meane time meſſengers executing meſſage diligētly returned back agayne large rewardes theim whome ſent came henry ſame day entred shreweſburye ſhewed howe frendes redyneſſe dooe vttermoſte laye theim tidynges put henry ſuche greate hope went forth courage came towne newporte ſet vp tentes vpon lytle hyll laye night night came hym ſyr gylberte talbot aboue two hundreth menne went forthe stafforde whyle willyam standley came hym fewe hym talked litle retourned backe hoſte whiche prepared thence went lichfelde nyght laye without toune ye morning betime entred ye citee receiued honourably daye ii afore thomas standley fyue men armed whiche knewe henry cōming forthwith went afore village called aderſtone tarye tyll henrye came dyd auoide ſuſpicion beyng afraid leaſt kyng richard knowing intent would haue put ſoonne deathe whiche telled lefte wt hym pledge father kynge rychard meane tyme nottingham hearing henry fewe baniſhed men entred wale ſo lightly regarded matter thoughte muche bee paſte vpon came ſo fewe noumbre lorde harbart ſir rice wer ruler wale would kyll hym elles take hym bring hym aliue afterward remembred ſelf oftentimes ſmal matter batel bee looked vnto betymes would make laſte great ſturre thought beſt remedy matter betimes commaunded henrye earle northumberlande noble realme whome thoughte ſet hym owne goodes rayſe vp army come hym ſpeede alſo ſente dyuers meſſengers letter robert brakenburye keper towre london commaundynge hym come vnto hym haſte brynge hym felowes battell thomas burſchere walter hungerforde dyuerſe knyghtes whome dyd litell ſuſpecte tyme ſhewed henrye come shrewiſburye without hurte tidinges ye kyng beganne rage made exclamacion againſte theim contrary faithes vtterly deceiued hym beganne miſtruſt menne wiſte whome mighte truſte ſo thoughte beſt ſette forthe hym ſelfe ageinſt aduerſaryes forthwith ſent ſpies knowe waye henry take dooen diligence retourned backe ſhewed hym howe henry come lichfeld thing knew becauſe greate noumbre ſouldyours come together menne ſet araye commaunded theim forwarde gooe foure foure together waye kept hearde ſaye enemy commynge ſuſpecte perſones putte myddes hym ſelfe thoſe truſted came behind winges horſemen running euery ſyde thus keping order aboute ſonne ſette came vnto leiceſtre henrye meane ſeaſon remoued lichefelde vnto nexte village called tamworth mydwaye mette walter hungerforde thomas burſchier many promiſed aide hym afore forbecauſe perceyued ſuſſpected richard leaſt ſhould brought violentlye vnto hym beyng enemye forſooke robert brakenbury capitaine nyghte tyme ſtale priuely awaye wente henry vnto whome chaunced waye worthy bee marked whiche henry althoughe manne noble courage alſo companye dyd dailye encreaſe yet ſtoode great feare becauſe vncertayne thomas standly whiche telled feare puttynge ſoonne deathe inclyned yet vnto parte matter ſo ſlēder kyng richard reporte made hym frendes wherfore afrayde withoute cauſe tooke onely twenty menne ſteyed iourney manne diſpaire halfe muſynge hym ſelfe beſte bee dooen aggrauate matter tidinges broughte hym kyng richard comming nere mete hym great houge hoſte menne thus lyngered feare behinde hoſte came afore toune tham worth becauſe darke night loſt bothe company alſo waye wandryng frome place place laſte came lytle village iii myle hoſte full feare leſte ſhould fall daunger ſcoute watche durſte aſke queſtyon man partly feare preſente partely come laye nyght tooke ſygne pronoſticacyon ſome greate plage come parte hoſte leſſe abaſhed ſeyng abſence tyme morning henry came theim light daye excuſed ye matter abſent becauſe loſt waye rather purpoſe becauſe would commen wt preuy frendes would ſene daye yt went priuely aderſtone thomas standley willyam brother dyd dwell henry thomas willyam mette tooke hande louing ſalutacions glad one counceled together metyng kyng richard whome perceyued bee farre theim day drewe toward night euening ihon sauage brytanne sanforde simon digby many forſaken kyng richarde came henry wt great power men whiche thyng power ſtrengthe ſate henry alofte meane ſeaſon kyng richard purpoſed go • thorow thicke thinne mater came boſworthe alitell beyond leiceſtre place batell ſhould bee manne would ſaye hye iuſtice god whiche coulde bee auoided hanging ouer hed called hym place ſhould ſuffer worthy punyſhemente deteſtable offenees ſette vp tentes reſted night afore went bed made oration companye greate vehemence perſwading exhorting manfully fight afterward ſaied terrible dreame ſlepe ſeming ſawe horrible deuilles appere vnto hym pulling haling hym coulde take reſt viſyon fylled hym full feare alſo heuy care waked ſore greued minde prognoſticate dreame euill luke heuy chaunce came hym came ſo cherful countenaunce vnto company wonte dooe leeſt ſhould thinke heauineſſe feare enemy ſtoode vp reherſed vnto theim dreame thinke dreame rather conſcience pricked ſharpe ſtynge miſcheuous offence although dooe pricke alwaye yet moſt cōmenly wil byte moſte towarde latter daye repreſentyng vnto v onely ſelfe alſo terryble punyſhement ordeined ſame ſyghte deuill tearyng haling v ſo therby haue grace may take occaſyon bee penitēt elles lacke ſame dye deſperacyon nowe come purpoſe nexte daye kyng richard hauing thynges redyneſſe went army oute tentes beganne ſette men araye fyrſt forward ſet forth meruelous lengthe bothe horſemen alſo footemen veray terrible companye theim yt ſhould ſee theim farre formoſt parte ordered bowman ſtronge fortreſſe theim came ouer iohn ye duke norffolke hedde capitaine hym folowed kyng mightye ſorte menne henry beyng departed ye communicacion frendes without tariyng pytched tentes nere enemy laye nighte cōmaunded men bee redineſſe morninge ſente alſo thomas standley middes betwixt bothe hoſtes ſhould come nere armye ſent hym woorde ſhould ſet menne ordre tyll came anſwer otherwiſe thought mater dyd require alitel abaſhed ſtoode doubte yet yt taryed ſpede ſet menne ordre ye forward ſlender becauſe noūber fewe archer ſet formoſt parte ouer theim iohn earle oxford hedde capitain ryght wing ſette gilbert talbot ye lefte put iohn sauage ſelfe ye helpe thomas standley folowed one companye horſemen fewe footemen whole company ſcāt fyue beſides ye bothe stanley company willyam standley thre kinges army double ſo bothe armyes redineſſe beganne come within ſight bragged forth theim ſelfes bothe party looking onely ſygne token ſtriking together betwyxte bothe hoſtes marreſſe whiche henrye lefte ryghte hande purpoſelye defence menne found meanes alſo haue bryght ſunne backe myght daſyll eye enemyes kyng ſawe henry paſſe ouer marras cōmaunded men violence ſet vpon theim ſodein clamour lette arrowes flee theim ſyde paied theim home manfully ſame came nere together laied valeauntly ſwerdes earle oxforde fearing leaſt meane time kyng richardes multytude ſhould haue compaſſed menne whiche wer fewe cōmaunded theim fyues ſhould moue forwarde paſte ten fote whiche cōmaundement knowen knitte theim ſelfes together ſeaſed fyghting aduerſaries beyng afrayed ſuſpected ſom crafte guyle began breake many ſame parte wer much greued therwith becauſe wer glad ye king ſhould loſte ſaued therfore fought leſſe courage erle oxford menne thicke together ſtroke freſhlyer parte dyd likwyſe ſame firſte wardes batell fought ſo manfully richard perceiued ſpies henry farre fewe companye armed menne afterward cōming nere richard knewe hym ſygnes token inflamed anger furiouſlye ſtroke horſe ſpurres ranne one ſyde hoſte like lyon ranne hym ſyde henry perceiuing hym commyng deſyrouſe mete hym richard fyrſte ſetting forth kylled diuers ſtode threwe doune henry banner willyam brandon bearer alſo ranne cheyny manne great mighte whiche came mete hym greate violēce ouerthrewe hym grounde made hymſelf awaie theim come henry henry kept better tacke hym thē men would haue thought whiche thē allmoſte deſpayre victory euē ye tyme lo came wyllyam stanley aide theim wt iii mēne euen verie ſame tyme reſidue kyng richardes men put flight thē richard fightyng alone middeſt enemy ouerthrowne ſlain ye meane tyme therle oxēford ye foreward fought māfully litle put ye reſidue flight whō ſlewe greate nōbre agreate nombre whiche folowed richard feare loue helde handes fightyng went awaie without hurte thei loked ſafegard rather deſtruccion ſlain conflicte many one thouſand whiche theſe noble menne ihon duke norffolke walter feris robert brachyngbury richard radcliffe many within twoo day wyllyam catiſby lawyer certain felowes put death leiceſtre emonges thoſe ye ranne awaie fraunces louell humfray stafford thomas brother ranne ſanctuary colcheſtre eſſex captiues greate nombre becauſe richard ſlain euery manne caſt doune wepon yeld hymſelf henry ye whiche ye parte would haue dooen ſo begynnyng feare kyng richardes ſpies whiche thē wā dered euery place emongeſt theſe noble erle northumberlande erle surrey whiche therle surrey put priſone frend receiued fauour henry felde loſte aboue hū dred menne emongeſt chief wyllyam brādone whiche bare henryes bāner battaill fought xxii day moneth auguſte inthe yere oure lorde thouſand cccc lxxxvi ye conflict indured ii howres richard might fame went aſaued hymſelf would afled awaie thoſe hym thei ſawe menne begynnyng fight faintly ſome ronne awaie vnto parte ſuſpected treaſon willed hym flie mater manifeſt hope victory paſt thei brought hym ſwi • te horſe puttyng ſied hope truſt fleiyng made ſaied aunſwere daie would haue ether ende battaill orels life ſuche greate audacite manfulnes whiche becauſe ſe certainly daie ſhould ob 〈◊〉 kyngdome quietely day life •• loſe bothe euer entred emōgeſt theim declared intendyng vtterly ether loſe orels wynne ſo wretehe dyed hauyng ende ſuche wont haue whiche ſtede lawe honeſtie godlynes folowe owne appetite vyllanye wyckednes plainly example whiche cannot expreſſed feare theim whiche ſuffer one howre bee otherwyſe ſpēt cruelte miſchief deuilliſhe faſſhiōs henry thus obtained victorye fell downe knee many praiers thankes referred goodnes god thē ſtode vp beyng wounderfully repleniſhed ioye went vp vpō alitle hill gaue two greate comendacions ſouldyours commaundyng theim hurte heled dede bee buryed afterward gaue immortall thankes noble capitains promiſyng theim would neuer forgette benifite multitude ye meane tyme one voyce one mynd proclaimed hym kyng whē thomas stanley ſawe ye toke kyng richardes croune whiche founde emongeſt ſpoyle putte vpon head though created kyng eleccion people wonte bee olde tyme firſt token felicite kyng hēry compaignie carriage went leceſtre toward night bed whether refreſſhed compaignie well ſpace twoo day thei might better goo toward london kyng richardes bodye brought naked ouer horſe backe hed armes hāgyng one ſide legges ye caried grey freres leceſter ſurely myſerable ſight loke vpō yet good inough cōſideryng wretched leuyng without ſolempnite buryed twoo dayes raygned twoo yeres twoo monethes one daie ſmall ſtature hauyng deformed bodie ye one ſhoulder higher ſhorte face cruell looke whiche betoken malice guyle deceite muſe vpō thing ſtāding would byte vnder lippe continually whereby māne might perceiue cruell nature within wreched bodie ſtriued chaffed alwaie hym ſelf alſo dagger whiche bare aboute hym would alwaies bee choppyng ſharpe pregnaunt witt ſubtill deſſimule fayne verie mete alſo proude cruell mynde whiche neuer went houre death whiche rather ſuffer ye cruell ſworde reigned throughout england wherof alſo enſued plague token ye people iudged plaine argument kyng henrye ſhoulde neuer bee oute feare dreade ſome miſchaunce ſeing ſuche great vexacyon ſedicyous tumulte ryſen al claimynge crowne whē thynges wer apeaced london ordered owne mynd rode northward progreſſe pacifie realme eſpecially thoſe partes firſte commocion alſo wer priuie cloked frendes aduerſaries becauſe nigh eaſter tooke waye lincolne tariyng certified lorde louell humfre stafforde gone ſanctuary colcheſter place whether mā could tell whiche meſſage kyng litle regardyng wēt foorth apointed yorke came cōmocion made lord louell lorde stafforde ſhewed hym lorde louell hand ſtrong power menne woulde inuade cytie alſo ſaid lorde stafforde brother wer gloceſtre made inſurreccion ſet menne euery parte defende gate walles citie firſt hearyng kyng litle moued certified letter frendes true greate feare neyther armye prepared harnyes theim becauſe mattier required haſte leaſt long taryeng aduerſaries power might bee encreaſed multiplyed commaunded duke bedforde mete theim three thouſande mēne whiche harnyſed barely theyr breſte plate moſte parte lether hym ſelfe yt meane tyme would gather vp hoſte might euery place duke hauyng mē nigh ye tētes enemyes cōſulted wt certain cōpaignie waye mighte traine theim peace withoute bloodde ſhedyng whiche deliberation aduiſement decreed certaine ſhoulde proclaime openly yt thei ſhould haue pardonne woulde leaue battaile whiche proclamation auayled muche lorde louell eyther ſome feare myſtruſt people feryng hym ſelfe owne behalfe fledde pryuely night compaignie lankeſhire ther remained ſpace ſyr thomas broghton knight hys army knowledge therof thei alſo ſubmittyng theim ſelfes duke aſked pardonne heinous offence lorde counſaill perſwaſion brother buſineſſe aſſwaged yorke ſhyre ſet peace quietnes kyng went london ſhortelye wyncheſter quene wyfe deliuered prynce called arthure wyncheſter retourned agayne london sone chaunſed one ſyr richard symond preeſt borne nature traytour ſedicious perſonne yet well learned chyld called lambert symenel bee hys ſcholar whome inuented crafte diſceat woulde make chyld kyng england hym ſelfe archebyſhoppe ſome hygh poteſtate realme knewe verely many menne ſuppoſed kyng edwardes chyldren bee fled ſome ſtraunge place edwarde erle warwyke ſonne duke clarence ether ſhould bee put death ſhortly ende myght ye better bryng hys purpoſe taught chyld bothe learnyng good maners alſo order hym ſelfe one linially deſcendyng hygh progenie sone rumoure younge earle warwyke dead pryſonne preeſt heard intendyng therby bring matter aboute chaunged chyldes name called hym edwarde younge earle warwyke whiche boothe one age ſayled irelande opening mynde certain nobilitee whome knew beare lytle fauoure kyng henry promyſed ayde lorde gerardine chauncellour countree coulde dooe whyche lorde fyrſt callyng hys frendes louers together deſyred helpe reſtoryng yong earle herytage dyd ſende certain englande deſire theym kynge rychardes frendes continue loue faythfulnes towardes hym helpe hys nephiewes chylde ryghte hys power myghte bee ſtronger ouercome hys enemyes deſyred lady margarete ſyſter kynge edwarde wyfe duke burgondy hys purpoſe helpe whyche lady beyng flaunders promiſed meſſaungers ſhe would onely maintaine entente large mony ſubſtaunce laboure peynes ſhe myght occaſion ye ſame conſpiracie kynge henrye certified thys ſore greued meanes ſuche myſcreaunte perſonne ſo great ſedicion ſhould bee neuertheleſſe kynge conſideringe ſhoulde bee deſtruccion manye menne yf ſhoulde fyghte enemy open feelde called hys counſayle together charter houſe beſyde rychemounde conſulted pacifie thys matter wythoute anye dyſturbaunce fyrſte decreed thei ſhoulde bee pardoned offence treaſons latelye commytted whiche hath frome tyme borne theim ſelfes vpryght towardes kinge leaſte ſyr thomas broghton whyche kepte lord louell king great tyme wyth deſpeyring theyr pardon ſhoulde haue made ſome ſodaine inſurrection agaynſt hym men ſhoulde thyncke duke clarence englande appoynted ſhoulde ſhowe hym ſelfe abrode wherby opynion ireland myghte bee fruſtrate accompted lye alſo determyned ladye elyſabeth wyfe kyng edward iiii ſhoulde loſe al landes becauſe ſhe ſubmitted ſelfe doughters wholye handes kynge rychard contrary promyſe made lordes noble whyche deſyre lefte al englande fledde kynge henrye brytayne dyd ſweare hym marye eldeſte daughter ſhe wylled theim dooe purpoſe frame god would thys quene buylded collage cambrydge gaue landes maynteyning ſame whiche thys houre called ye quenes collage thys order determynacion kynge ended wente london nexte sondaye folowynge cauſed young earle bee broughte tower ſtreetes poules ſhewe hym ſelfe euerye bodye taſke chiefe noble menne thoughte haue conſpyred agaynſte kynge henrye thys cauſe myghte perceaue iryſhe menne moue battayle vnaduyſedly cauſe ſtryfe vppon iuſte occaſion howebeit thys nothyng auayled earle lyncolne duke suffolkes ſoonne nephewe kynge edwarde coulde ſuffer kynge henrye thus reygne traytoure ſayled flaūders ladye margarete takynge wyth hym syr thomas broghton certayne alſo lorde louell landed twoo three dayes beynge together determyned earle lyncolne lorde louell ſhoulde goo irelande attend vpon counterfeyte earle brynge hym englande power myghte agaynſte kynge henrye yf dooynges good ſucceſſe foreſayde lambarte miſnamed earle ſhoulde conſente counſayle depoſed true earle bee delyuered oute pryſon enherite right iuſte tytle dominion kyng miſtruſting man bee ſo foolyſh hardy fyght ſuch cauſe anye ſo vndyſcrete eſpeciallye hys realme beleue dyd onelye mynde ſuppreſſynge iryſhe menne theyr enterpryſe ſubdue yet hearynge earle lyncolne fledde gooen hys aduerſaries cauſed border bee dilygentlye kepte none myghte eſcape geue theym ſocoure commynge abbaye sayncte edmundes burye certified lorde thomas marque come excuſe pourge hym ſelfe hym certayne thynges ſuſpected whome kynge dyd ſende earle oxford take commynge conueyghe hym towre london thys cauſe yf frende dede ſhould bee myſcontented ſuffer lytle impryſonmente ſafetie hys kynge yf hys frende tarye myghte haue damage hurte hym ſo kynge wente forthe norwyche tariynge chriſtemas daye went walſingham thence cambridge ſo ſtreyght london tyme erle lincolne lord louell got two thouſande germaynes wyth martyn swarte theyr captayne ſo ſaylynge ireland came made fornamed lambarte kyng englande deuelynge ſo wyth greate multitude iryſhe menne aſwell naked vnarmed perſonnes lorde gerardyne vnder hym ſayled englande landed purpoſe wythin lytle lancaſtre truſtynge bee ayded syr thomas broghton chiefe authoure thys conſpiracie kynge ſlepynge hys mattiers myſtruſtynge ſuch thynges ſhoulde chaunce ſente certayne knyghtes throughe eaſte party attende commynge hys enemyes gatherynge hys hooſte together went hym ſelfe couentree beynge certified hym earle lyncolne landed lancaſtre wyth newe kynge whome kynge appoynted meete conſente agremente hys counſayle goo vppon theym wythoute anye farther delaye leaſt theyr power long ſufferaunce ſhould bee augmented multiplyed ſo ſuche aduiſemente taken went notingham lytle woodde called boures pytched hys tentes whome ſhortelye came lorde talbote earle shroweſburye lorde straunge lorde cheiney wyth greate armye menne manye noble menne whoſe name enſue latemere wyllyam bulmere ihon langforde wyllyam norrys ihon neuill thortinbridge ihon wyllyams erle lyncolne meane ſeaſon went forth ſoftely compaignie yorkeſhire without hurte diſcommoditie māne dwelt therabout truſtyng partely therby ꝑtely alſo bycauſe well knowen acquainted emong theim ſhould get greate ayde ſocour perceiued none folowe hym could ſeyng enemy ſo nigh hand alſo ſo far entred ſafegard hoſte returne bacward yet thought beſt abyde taſte chaunce battaill ſo muche yt rather becauſe ſawe henry within twoo yeres accompaign • ed fewe ſmall ſorte ſouldiers ouercome kyng richard whiche brought hym greate hoſte well armed menne wherfore beeyng greate hope victory toke iorney then towarde newarke ſette ſouldyours araye mete kyng knew well though bee paſte ii dayes iorney hym could come thither kyng hēry whiche ſurely certified thynges yt wēt came newarke alitle euen thei ſhould fight yt morowe wyſe erle loked tariyng long went forth three myles ferther ſette tentes taryed night whoſe commyng although therle knewe yet went foorth luſtely tourney came night village nigh enemy called stooke pitched tentes next daie kyng ſo ſone ſette ſouldyours due ordre araye went forwarde wt ſpede place erle laye whiche place come appointed felde moſte mete battaill bee fought gaue place enemy come foorth prouoked theim battaill ready prouoke ſo readie wer thei owne courage come foorth ſo bothe party thei ranne battaill fought moſte egerly whiche tō flicte euidently appere germaines whiche ſette forewarde whoſe capitain martine swarte nothyng woorſe manlyneſſe cheualry thei gotte chiefly daily long exerciſe engliſhemen ireſhmen although thei fought verie luſtely yet reaſon thei ware harnes accordyng faſſhiō cuſtome diſcomfcited beate downe bothe nōbre ſoner yet battaill ſo earneſtlie boldly fought whyle bothe party could bee wel diſcerned whiche ſyde victorie would incline laſt kynges forewarde abode ieoperdie ſo luſtely couragiouſly ranne vpon enemy yt none hable reſiſt abyde power ſo yt aſwell germaines iriſh men ſlain orels made flie ye whiche none could eſcape awaie whiche battaill whē thus dooen mēne might ſe boldnes audacitie theſe rebelliōs capitaines ihon erle lincolne frācis louell thomas broghtō martine swart thomas gerardine neuer gaue backe one foote ſlaine ſame place thei began firſt fight kylled vattaill fiue capitaines ſpoken euen partie foure thouſand kynges part halfe theim whiche fought ye forewarde ſlain thē lambert child whiche falſly reported bee duke ſoonne clarēce maiſter ſir richard simond preeſt taken neither theim putte death becauſe lambert yet child ſeme dooe compulſion maiſter thē owne preeſt whiche defaulte caſt perpetuall priſone lambert taken kynges kechin made one kynges faukeners yet lyue thus yt margarete went tyme turned naught none effecte whiche thyng whē ſhe heard tell flaūders ſhe verie lory hearte made greate mone yet could ſhe bee contēt immediately inuēted thyng vexe trouble kyng henry ſhalbe ſhewed kyng henry thynges brought thus paſſe vtterly vanquiſſhed theſe enemy thought hymſelf one tyme deliuered twoo eiuils together ſaie bothe feare preſent alſo come bee thought yt thei whiche ſo fewe nombre durſte bee ſo bold entre realme make battaile againſt ye kyng knewe wel ynough would bryng hym great well armed hooſte felowes ſame coniuracion whiche would mete ayde theim could tyme place conuenient therefore kyng ſawe hoſte enemy manifeſtly eye commaunded mā ſhoulde kyll earle lincolne ſhould bee brought hym alyue entent might ſhewe bewraye whiche ye conſpiracie ſowdyers would leaſt ſauyng hym ſhould bee deſtrucciō ſhould haue dede many battayle fought yeare oure lorde thouſande foure hundreth foure ſcore ſecōde yere hēryes reigne ye whiche yere alſo thomas burſcher archebyſhop cā terburye died whoſe roume ſucceded iohn morton late biſhop ely whome alexander name ſixte biſhop rome made cardinall retourne purpoſe kyng gathered al prayes ſpoyles together buryed theim wer ſlain went forth lincolne taryed three dayes euerye daie one proceſſion thanke god almightie ouerhande enemy incontynently ſent banner walſyngham conſecrate lady bee kepte perpetuall mo • ument victorie execuciō ſuche rebellion taken ſhortely tooke iorneye foorth yorke likewyſe ſuche founde gyltye dyd punyſhe ſtrayghtlye dooen wente vnto newcaſtle frome thence ſente scotlande richarde foxe whiche longe made biſhop exeter richarde edgecombe knight ambaſſadoures kynge iames league peace henrye thought great pleaſure cōmoditee bee peace concorde kinges gouernours whiche laye aboute realme ſpecially kyng iames becauſe yt rebellion might truſt whiche otherwiſe perchaunce woulde haue truſted haue ayde ſuccoure hande ſo thereby durſte none againe take weapon againſt hym ambaſſadoures wer come scotland kyng hym gently moſte louing faſhion receiued heard dyd plainlye declare open theim yt hym ſelfe loued kyng henrye man 〈◊〉 yt moſte parte scottes ſubiectes could caſe agree engliſh menne wherfore excepte ſhould offend 〈…〉 ſe theim deſired ye legate bee contēt truce vii yeres promeſſe dede ſayed peace betwene theim parte ſhoulde neuer bee broken euer thoſe ſeuen yeres ſhould bee paſſed would geue truce ſeuen yeres lenger ſo kyng henry would euer bee peace moſte aſſured amytie kyng iames becauſe knewe facte people ſhoulde bee alowed ambaſſadoures hearde tooke yeres offered theim concernynge peace retourned home kyng hē ry againe ſhewed hym mattier ordre whiche tydynges veraye well contented shortely kyng departed thence towarde london waye leicetre mette hym abaſſadoures frenche kyng ſhewed hym kyng charles recouered many tounes cyties whiche poſſeſſed kyng maximilian kepte battayle nowe fraunces duke brytayne becauſe kepte ſocoured dominion certaine traytours rebellion againſt hym whiche chief lewes duke orlyance therfore deſyred hym frendſhip familiaritie either would helpe hym orelles medle neyther partie kynge henrye althoughe founde muche frendſhip frenche kynges hande yet muche ſpyed whereof ſtryfe beganne meſſage well contente cauſe frenchemenne tooke battayle becauſe ſawe duke olde manne neuer chylde thereby myghte brynge dukedome ſubieccion kyng henrye perceiued alſo howe louyng brytaynes euer englande finally remembred tendre loue betwene duke hym thought beſt nede wer helpe britaynes yet muche founde frenche kyng veray kynde tymes paſt partely helpe recouered kyngdome veraye lothe medle ſo muche coulde well tell beſt mattier bee dooen laſte fully purpoſed neceſſitie ſhoulde require helpe duke might yet leaſt ſhould make highe frende hys extreme enemie aunſwere ambaſſadoures intende make kyng duke frendes wherfore aſſone frenche kynges ambaſſadoures dimiſſed ſent meſſage chriſtopher vrſwycke charles kynge fraunce firſte certifye hym veraye glad victorye vpon maximilian ſecondarely tumulte inſurreccion made englād thyrdly eſpecially deſyre hym bee one againe duke brytayne commaunded vrſwycke kyng fraunce ſhoulde bee ſo contente go foorthe immediatlye duke deſyre hym lykewyſe ſame kyng come againe london ioye myrthe victorye ye euery ſyde onely kyng alſo euerye one cytezyns reioyſed veraye muche wherfore kyng ſhewed hym ſelfe beraye humane courteous toward menne alſo rewarded theim tooke paynes battaile moſte bountefully long delyuered lord thomas marque • oure loued hym veraye well meane ſeaſon chriſtofer vrſwicke come frenche kyng hym moſt louing faſſion yt coulde bee receiued ſone ſhewed meſſage ye kyng ſhewed ſelfe bee wt veray well pleaſed went ye ambaſſadour ſtreight thence cōmaunded hym britain ſhewed duke kyng henry would haue dooen duke becauſe hym ſelf ſicke great therby memory wit •• aied called hym heare meſſage bothe lewes duke orleaunce councell whiche lewes wyſe woulde haue peace bee made ſaied mete kyng henrye ſeing founde ſuche kyndneſſe duke hande britaine ſuche good defence england helpe kepe battayle yt might againſt frenchman retourned chriſtofer againe fraunce declared king charles aunſwer made ye britain ſhortely came englande againe ſtill meane time ye frenche kyng went aboute buſely ouercome brytains nigh purpoſe ſo much ye exhorte deſire kyng henry make peace betwene theim wherfore ſēt bernarde daubeney knighte haſte kyng henrye deſire hym wiſe make ſome ende cō trauerſy therupon kyng deſirous ſame choſe thre oratours ye abbot abindon iohn lilie biſhop rome collectoure richard tonſhal knight veray wiſe man gooe firſte frenche kyng duke make amitee frendſhyp againe betwene theim euer theſe ambaſſadoures proceded iourney iohn lilye fell ſicke goute therfore hym choſen chriſtofer vrſwycke together wente cōmaunded firſte fraunce kyng thence withoute delaye britain fraunces duke caſe would take ſuche condicyons wer offered wherfore came back againe fraunce without purpoſe tarieng ſignified kyng henry letter dooen letter came kynges handes edward woodilile bold champion came hym deſired veraye earneſtly myght haue hoſt men helpe britain leaſire ſhould cauſe diſſencion betwene frenche kyng hym ſaied would gooe priuely without paſporte thentent might bee thought ſtole land kyng much truſted peace ſhoulde bee made woulde wyſe graunt peticion wherfore edward wēt ſtreight yſle veches dominacion ſo ſone gathered menne together foure c ſayled ouer britaines ioyned hym ſelfe theim againſt frenchmē whiche thing knowen fraunce made ye ambaſſadours greatly afraid liues while feare frēchemen thought dooen maliciouſly kyng henry came ambaſſadours frome hym frenche kyng certifieng hym declaring moſt euident tokēs nothing dede thought haue meſſage albeit ye kyng lytle credēce yet made thoughe bene angry ye ambaſſadours renewed peace betwene king hym xii monethes retourned home ſhewed kyng ſuch thinges yt either hearde ſene wherof gathered ye frenchman nothing leſſe entend haue peace made wherfore without delay called parliament conſulted aidyng brytains exſpence ſhould bee therin made mattiers aſſone parliament broken vp cauſed muſters bee taken euery toune thorowoute realme yet leaſte peraduenture might ſeme willingly breake amitee whiche betwene frenche kyng hym ſent ambaſſadours fraunce certifye kyng late kepte parliament yt pleaſed noble ſhould ſende helpe ye britain becauſe time dooen benefites englande naciōs therfore ſhould either leaue battail orelles ſhoulde bee greued dyd obey ye mindes lordes prelate yet woulde promiſe hym one thing yt ſhould medle wt hym lēger britain kepte battaile vpon theim theſe commaundementes ye ambaſſadours went foorth declared ye french kyng minde wyll kyng thyng litle cared thought came paſſe dede engliſhemen coulde lytle auayle meane ſeaſon britain fought one felde place called ſainte albanes ſped beray euel theim lewes duke orleaūce many mo taken edwarde wooduile iames galeot italian veray good warryer diuers noble menne ſlaine whiche thing kyng henry heard tell thinking tyme make haſte ſente ſpedely roberte brooke lorde iohn cheinye iohn midelton raufe helton richarde corbet thomas leightō richard lacon edmond cornewell luſtye capitaines viii thouſand wel armed men ye brytains helpe theim theyr nede whiche reaſon ye wind ſerued theim came thither ſo ſone could deſire frenche menne knewe comming whome knewe ſo longe freſhe luſty bee maner inuincible ye firſte wer blanke durſte ſcarſely looke oute tentes afterwarde truſting yt might wery theim went many theim together diuers place kepte many bikeringes engliſh menne theim ſelfes euer bare worſte away howſoeuer engliſhmen ſped ſped naught while kynde warre exerciſe duke fraunces died daſſhed chyefe ruler brytains ſome theim corrupted money ſome ſturred vp ambicyon fell deuiſyon amonge theim ſelues ſemed nomore endeuoure defende commune weale rather deſtroy vtterly extinguiſhe thing engliſhe menne perceiuing alſo ſuffering muche colde compelled neceſſitee within fyue moonethes wente thyther come backe agayne englande charles french kyng maried anne duke doughter gat al britayn meanes hys hādes ſhalbe ſpoken decreed englande ſouldyours ſent brytayne expence warre euery man ſhould paye thei hable tribute whyche mooſte parte theim dwelte byſhopryke durhā yorke ſhyre dyd vtterly refuſe pay complayned matter lorde earle northumberland immediately ſignified kyng letter people dyd greatly lament ſory ſaiyng thei neuer put ſo muche coaſt thei late dayes nowe ther ſo much requyred theim neither thei hable pay ſo great ſumme would pay yet al kyng cōmaunded erle get thē make theim pay whether thei would leaſt peraduenture myght cauſe yf time tribute agayne ſhould bee required thē make inſurreccion thyng people hearde ranne vnto earle authoure tribute paiyng themurde ryng erle northūberland kylled hym hande thei ſo done thei chaſe ihon egremonknight verey dicious perſonne bee captayne ſo arraied ſelfes went agaynſt kyng makyng cry euery towne thei came fight nother cauſe defēde yt cōmon libertie mattier ſhoulde come blowes thei waxed colde ſorte theim euerye one wiſhed tumulte wer retracted nowe alredy begonne ſo cōcluſiō one ſcacely ſcaped without great diſcommodite kynge aſſone hearde inſurreccion went downe hooſt yorke wherof theſe ſlaues traitours beyng greatly afraied fledde ſome hether ſome thether durſt abide ſuſtaine power ye kynges army wherfore thei wer ſone taken puniſhed greuouſely accordyng deſeruyng euery one theim ihon egremont whiche captain fledde flanders margarete whome ſpake kyng ſo ſone buſines quē ched tooke iourny back vnto london committed tribute whiche yorke yorke bee taken vp holy richard touſtal ye yere lord thouſand foure hundred xc fourth yere reigne kyng henry thys yere alſo kynge scottes 〈…〉 ſore vexed ſubiectes roaſe agaynſt hym made ſonne iames whiche yet chylde capitain wherfore ſent kynge englande frenche kyng byſhoppe roome innocentius deſire theim make ſome end thys ciuile battayle contencion whiche betwene hys people hym whiche afterwarde ſente theyr ambaſſadours deſired vayne ye rude ſort would nedes fight onleſſe kyng scottes ſlain ſubiectes would reſygne crowne wherfore ſhortely thei fought battayle kylled kyng gaue ſonne iames whiche fourth name crowne byſhoppe rome legate hadrian came late whyles englande wt kyng henry worde came kyng scottes ſlayne battayle hys ſoonne made kyng therfore taried england ſpace veray muche made hyghly commended kyng ihon mortō archbyſhop canterburie whereby came ſo high fauour kyng henry made biſhoppe herforde ſhortly leaſt gaue hym biſhopprike boothe welles bathe longe retourned wt theſe honour roome alexander made cardinall beganne alſo freſhe certayne buſineſſe concernynge brytaine geare appeaſed whiche maximilian beyng tyme without wyfe would haue maried duke briteines doughter one wowed hym lady promiſyng hym fayth trueth entent ſhe might go word vſed way wt ſhe went bed night bedde wedlocke wower hired putte one fete ye bed knee ye ſight cōpany many noble matrōs lady token teſtimony yt mariage conſūmate thei ii mā wife nothing auaile char frenche kyng deſireous marye hearyng maximiliā ſure dyd buſely ſet vpon britaynes thentent might haue ladye countree alſo wyll eſtemed mariage bee ſtrength force neuertheleſſe feared kyng henry muche leaſt would ſtoppe purpoſe whiche kyng made league ferdinande alſo kyng spayne made ye ſame britaynes aſſiſt theim ieoperdies perilles ſhould chaunce theim foren countrees wherfore ſent al poſt haſt franceſe lucemburgenſe charles marignane roberte gaguine kyng henry peace bee confirmed hadde deſyrynge hym kyng might ordre mariage ladye anne wer thought beſt without let hynderaunce hym kyng henry would agree theim lady ſhould bee maried hym conſyderyng ſhe made ſure kyng maximilian againſt right lawe bothe god manne albeit kynge would gladly make peace betwene theim bothe ſo demiſſyng ye kynges ambaſſadoures large ample rewarde ſent thomas goldeſtone abbot cantorbury lord thomas ormondye ambaſſadours ſtreight theim meane ſpace alexander b rome ſixt name innocētius ſent biſhop cōcordienſe legate frenche kyng certayne mattiers emong peace vnitee bee confederate betwyxt hym kyng henry whiche eaſely obteyned came englande beyng entretained moſte roially kyng purpoſe deſire hym engliſhe ambaſſadours beyng frenche kyng purpoſed haue peace concluded whiche firſt demaunded certain thynges kyng ere ſhould bee made albeit kyng would graūt theim nothyng ſore moued requeſt aſkyng ye ſhortly frenche kyng ſent noble menne britain greate giftes rewardes entent thei might moue ladie anne giue troweth hym alſo ſent herſelf many princely giftes token ye ſhe would beare loue hym yt ſhe might feare ſhe might lawfully marie hym certified ye promiſe none effecte yt ſhe gyuē maximiliā yt geuē made wtout cōſent whiche ye gouernaunce dominion ouer ye countre cauſe concorde peace could bee kept betwixt theim kyng taken maximilians doughter ladie margaret bee wife ſaied might bee lawfully diſſolued becauſe ye ladie vnder age ripe bee maried ladie anne britain perſuaſion many noble menne countree contented bee wife ladie kyng certified haſtened mariage expedicion celeritee could engliſhe ambaſſadours returned countree nothyng dooen agreed vpon matter kyng certified ambaſſadours purpoſed make battaill againſt hym reuenge naughtie entent ſwerde aſſemblyng counſaill together ſhowed theim matter iuſte cauſe fight deſteryng theim maintenaunce theſame warres helpe hym money neuertheleſſe menne ſhould thynke bee extorte theim willed euery māne gyue muche litle would theim bee eſtemed taken moſte beſte aſſured frendes gaue ye moſt money ſomme gatheryng preparaunce made battaill maximilian kyng warred ſore frenchemen whiche kyng taken litle certain brunt ſkirmiſhe made caſt priſone whiche tyme kyng henry ſent hym giles dabeney capitain calais aide hym three thouſād harniſſed mēne ye length maximilian hauyng better hand frenchemen entēded reuenge hymſelf frēche kyng repudiate doughter ladie margarete taken hym wife quene anne becauſe fully hable hymſelf ſuſtein battaill ſent iames conti • alde ambaſſadour kyng henry helpe whiche iames dooen meſſage kyng promiſed would dooe hym could mainteinyng warres tyme charles frenche kyng maried ladye anne chalengyng mariage dominion gouernaunce ye brytaines maximilian kyng beyng certified greately moued onely forſake repudiate doughter ladye magarete alſo receiued mariage ye ladye quene anne wife furie ſent kyng hēry deſieryng hym prepare armie would goo vpon frenche menne kepe open battaill theim whiche kyng henry gathered hoſte menne proclaimed battaill realme whiche proclamacion came london houge armie menne capitaines whiche herafter enſewe folowe rycharde thomas greate compaignie welſhe menne erle thomas derbie george erle shroweſburie thomas erle harundell edmunde duke suffolke edwarde erle deuenſhire wt noble young ſoone thomas erle ormō dye george erle kent lorde thomas dorcet marque ihon cheyney gyles dabeney richard gylforde ihon raynſforth iames terell ihon sauage thomas baro heltō wyllyam bulmerey edwarde stanley armie araied kyng ſent ſir chriſtopher vrſwycke ſir ihon ryſeley knyghtes kyng maximilian certifye hym thei redyneſſe kepe battaile would haue theim dooen meſſage thei returned backe kyng certifiyng hym maximiliā ſo poore nedye monye menne could hable ſuſteyne battaile neuertheleſſe mynde good power habilitee correſpondent kyng receipte theſe letter diſpleaſed muche hym albeit conſyderyng gooen ſo farre ſuche furnyture thynges prepared leaſt menne ſhoulde impute hym cowardneſſe faynt frō battaile proceded forth towarde fraunce ye vi daye septēbre landed caliſe reſted armye wher worde brought hoſte thei knowe maximilian could make preparaunce lacke mony ye whiche thei maruailed greatly conſideryng ſuche vilanye ſhewed hym longe kynge fraunce hand yet thei wer neuer diſcoumfeyted like ſtoute valiaunt warryars great confidence owne power ſtrengthe wyth whō kyng fraunce yt perceaued beſt profite eaſe would gladly haue reconciled although ready hoſte fight againſt theim withſtāde power eſpecially deſyred peace cauſe yt might haue loue neighboures entent realme might bee better ſauegarde quietnes whē ſhould warre againſt ferdinād kyng napels ye deſyre ludouike sfortia duke millayn whiche preſent tyme inuite hym wherfore ſende philip deſquerd chief annonye deſyre kyng henrye peace whiche philip ſend ye letter hym came countre hymſelf wherin ſignified would take ſuche paine bryngyng purpoſe would ſhould ſo pleaſe grace reconcile bothe hym kyng loue eche thei haue dooen heretofore ſaied ſhould bee honour take theſame condicion whiche condicion would ſend certain capitains mete hym parte fraunce determine ſhould haue promiſed hereafter duely bee performed kyng red theſe letter ſend biſhop exceter giles dabeney forenamed philip peace agreed vpon concluded whiche ſpace determyned vpon certain condicions whiche ſhalbee ſhewed peace ſhould bee bothe party thei thus conſultyng ye kyng hauyng hoſte caleis remoued place bononye pitchyng tētes beſeeged toune power might whiche toune becauſe ſtrongely defended furniſhed thynges neceſſarye warre could bee ouercome without greate labour yt either could ouercome parte woord brought peace cōcluded made whiche heard pleaſure frenchemen ſo ſorowe engliſhe men thei cried kyng ſaied honour ſo dooe kyng wiſe manne moſte prudent prince ſaied ſhould death many noble puiſaunt capitaines ſhould continue theſame battaill therefore might ſore reproche wer power tendre aſ well health cōmons owne whiche ſaiyng ſomewhat coule pacifye grief dooen kyng returned backe caliſe becauſe enformed hym yt one richard ye named hym ſelf ye ſonne kyng edwarde made inſurreccion flaūders ye counſaill lady margarete ye quene fight againſt hym thyng kyng henry conſyderyng ſpedely haſten conclude peace condicion peace bee made yt frenche kyng ſhould paye kyng henry certain ſumme meny whiche leauyed ambaſſadours coſt charge kyng put battayll alſo ſhould yerely certain ſpace paye cauſe bee payde kyng englād full recompence x • v thouſand crounes whiche frenche kyng beyng warre
