perceauyng yt erle cōpaignie could haue ſuche ſucceſſe buſineſſe ſhe would haue wiſhed theim ſhe inuēted new way worke treaſon againſt certain yoūg mā tornace beautiful faire coūtenaunce pregnaunt witte whiche yoūg mā called peter ſurnamed warbecke cowardnes nycknamed engliſhe men called perkyn perkyn warbeck yoūg mā trauaylyng many countrees could ſpeake many lāguages baſenes ſtocke birth knowen none almoſt therfore ye quene thynkyng yoūg man bee mete whō ſhe might feigne duke yorke ſōne brother kyng edward kept hym certain tyme wt priuely tellyng hym ſhould yt might rather perſuade mē kynges ſonne ſend hym irelāde time ſhe knewe kyng henry apointed fight againſt frenche kyng honorably receaued taken euery manne prynce whoſe right promyſed fight helpe hym yt could came ye frēche kynges eare yt ſuch one ireland whō kyng ſend ſee cauſed hym brought came p̄ſence ye kyng accepted hym gladly princely faſhiō intreteined hym ye came loue wt kyng england ſayd charles dimiſſe ye yoūg mā would lōger kepe hym leaſt ſome inconueniencie cauſe ſtrife ſhould chaunce thorough wherfore ye young manne went flaunders agayne quene magarete whiche quene receaue hym ſuche gladneſſe ſhe coulde well rule ſelfe cauſe onely ſhe dyd ſhewe ſelfe ſo ioyfull merye menne mighte perſwade theim ſelfe richard kynges ſoonne vpon cauſe truely men ye reuerence younge manne yt firmely beleue hym bee righte heire ſonne kyng edwarde alſo rumour blaſed abrode aſwel england fraunce flaundres beganne great ſedicion ſpryng firſte long ſanctuary greate offence commytted wer caſt pouertie gathered compaignie mē ſayled ouer flaunders counterfaicte edwarde otherwiſe named peter alſo many noble men conſpired together entent might bryng purpoſe wel ſend certain quene margarete knowe theſame edwarde might come conueniently englande ye thei beyng certified theſame might ye eaſely receaue bryng hym ye realme yt conſent agrement theim ſyr robert clyfforde knight wyllyam barley wer ſent ſhewe myndes aduyce concernyng newe founde duke quene margarete whome quene accepte gladlye perſuaded theim true publyſhed rycharde duke ſtreight vpon ſhewed theim theſame peter whiche muche lyke richarde prayſyng vertues qualitees wonderfullye ſaid robert whē ſeen theſame yoūg manne beleued ſurely kynges bloode wrote englande coumpaignye felowes conſpiracie knewe hym bee kynges ſoonne face euery proporcion body theſe letter came vnto englande chief capitaynes buſineſſe openly diuulgate publyſhe trewe ſpoken ſaied abroad duke dooen ſuche crafte manne coulde tell authoure rumoure kyng perceiued many men geue credence vaine fable thought beſte owne ſafegard prouide remedy alſo myſtruſting ſome conſpiracye bene made bicauſe ſir robert clifford fled priuely flaundres commaunded certain knightes choſen piked menne warre wt bonde menne kepe border ſurely ye manne might eſcape ſayle ouer ſea without paſporte licence geuen hym alſo men myghte contynue falſe perſwaſion belefe conceyued duke cauſed certain ſpies ſearch citees belgike knowe progenie myſnamed richarde geue theim highe rewardes would ſhewe verite truth ſame matter ſailynge fraunce euerye manne dyd gooe contraye quarter enquired diligently hym ye length certain theim came towne called tornace certifyed teſtymonye many honeſt menne came lowe courſe parentage named peter war becke whiche thing alſo kynges frendes certified hym letter writynges hym plaine euidentelye therfore kyng knowen matter wholy aſwel frendes ſpies ſent foorth purpoſelye ſame cauſed bee proclaimed openly aſwell region countrees england diſceate deueliſh crafte might appere euident euery manne firſte ſent ambaſſadours philyp chiefe capitaine flaundres councell becauſe younge age whiche ſir edward poninges knight ſir william varame preeſt lawyer might ſhewe euidently howe falſely younge manne hath vſurped name richarde duke yorke whiche kylled brother edward towre london cōmaundement kyng richard vncle euery man coulde teſtifye affirme moſt ſurely alſo borne poore ſtocke obſcure famulie tornace named perkin warbecke therfore woulde pleaſe hym councel ſuffer theim ſelfes bee blynded ſeduced ſuche mere impoſtures craftie illuſions yet aide hym hande cauſe ſedicion ſtrife conſideryng iuſte title enheritynge ſame would rather bee frendes nowe becauſe yt helped maximilian theyr kyng yere againſte power violencye frenche menne hym ſelfe hable refyſte theyr myghte ſtronge power ambaſſadours dooen meſſage gentely entretayned hym requeſt woulde loue oughte vnto kynge counſaile helpe theſame perkin thinge neuertheleſſe yf quene margaret would perſiſte continewe malice towardes kyng whome ambaſſadour ſir william varame reproued checked ſore bringing vp ſuche monſters commune plague publike weale oration made vnto philippe counſayle power withſtande becauſe ſhe might doo owne herytage thinges owne wyll pleaſure whiche quene entended fully arme perkin ſtronge compaignye menne againſt kyng henry kynge henrye dyd heare purpoſed pacyfye buſyneſſe like chaunce wytte policye ſtreight dyd ſende foorthe certaine ſpies whiche ſhoulde fayne theim ſelfes haue fledde vnto duke meanes ſearche foorthe knowe whole entente theyr coniuracion waye framed theyr matter alſo ſhoulde promyſe pardon remyſſyon vnto ſyr roberte clyfforde willyam barley offence cōmitted kyng ſo dooen many theim returned englande broughte name certayne chief ſame conſpiracye taried vntyll ſuche tyme ſir robert clifforde came englande agayne kyng knowen chief capitaines tumulte ſpyes theim cauſed bee attached brought london preſēce whoſe name wer ſir iohn ratclyffe ſyr simon monforde ſyr thomas thwarte knightes william dabeney roberte ratcliffe richard leſey wt many alſo certaine preeſtes religious menne ſir william richeford thomas poynes bothe monkes ſainct dominikes order ſir william sutton ſir william vrſeley deane poules robert layborne giltie ſame crime hearing many compaignie wer taken fledde take ſanctuarye taken wer condempned treaſon ye whiche heded ſir simon monford ſir robert ratcliffe william dabeney authours chiefe capitaines buſines pardoned preeſtes alſo order taken alſo ſir iohn ratcliffe pardoned lyfe came caliſſe caſte priſone behedded becauſe corrupted kepers wt many promiſes haue eſcaped ſame shortly ſir robert clifford truſting find fauour grace kynges hande came england whoſe cōming ye kyng certified went ſtreight ye towre london taryed tyll ſuche tyme ye ſyr robert clyfford came whiche thyng vſed vnder pretence yf ſir robert clifford accuſed man hym ye treaſon euerie ſuche perſon mighte bee called thether withoute anye ſuſpectiō anie euel ſtreight bee caſt holde goo furder wyll ſhewe opinion many men conceaued knightes goynge flaunders men helde opinion kyng henrye dyd ſende hym ſpye flaunders therfore came ſoner fauoure neuertheleſſe lyke bee true diuerſe reaſōs fyrſt tourned ye great infamye hurt hym ſelfe frendes secondarly ſo greate fauoure kyng ben tymes paſt becauſe giltie part therfore ſaied ſir robert comming king retourne england kneled mekelye downe foot deſired pardō grace beyng enquired coniuration examined wer authours miſchiefe pronounced ſaied william stā ly whome kynge made earle one chief ſo ſaied kyng greatly diſmayed greued ſhould offend whō made chief priuie chamber conſidering alſo founde great kindenes hertofore hande dyd ouercome kyng rychard chiefly helpe meanes kyng coulde bee perſwaded ſuche offender bene ſhewed manifeſt token apparēt argumentes ye true ſaied king thē cauſed taken examined matter examinacion proued offender kynge doubtynge dooe dyd conſult breath lytle ſelfe feared brother lord thomas ſhewed great kyndneſſe woulde take greuouſly alſo yf ſhoulde remitte faulte would abuſe lemtee treſpace highly albe laſte wylled ſhoulde ſuffer offence ſo cauſed hym bee behedded cauſe loue mē reporte dyd chaunge hatred lorde wylliā conſideryng ſaued kyng brought hym realme gouernour thought could neuer bee recompenſed hys ſo doyng wher kyng alſo remembring benefyte dyd make hym chiefe chamberlayn gaue hym hygheſt promocions lytle regarded loked ſome greater rewarde wherfore king perceauynge ſore greued hym ſo thei bothe dyd fall debate hatred eche wyth alſo time king thought beſt vſe ſome aſperite correcting offēces ſubiectes becauſe ye ſome taken ſuche heart audacitee ye thei feared ſpeake euel maieſtie moſt ſpiteful contumeleous wordes truſting euer ye fayned rychard duke york lately ryſen death lyfe god name ſhould claime crowne enheret counterfeted father poſſeſſions ſuch perſōs ſuffered due poniſhment offence learning neighbour miſchaunce beware dyd frome ye tyme beare theim ſelfes true faithfull ſubiectes aſſyſted al power time required help thē death william stanley giles dabeney choſen made chiefe chā berlain ye kyng good ſtaye realme ſauyng yt ireland wel weded pernicious ſede ye ſowed young mā perkin warbeck ſecte wherfore ſent ſir henry deny late abbot lanktō abbey thither made chauncellour ouer al ile edward ponyng ſerch place forenamed perken puniſh thē extremely example ye giltie yt crime thei heard thei fled moſt part woddes maryſh place defence ſafgard ſelfes conſultyng kepe open warre agaynſt hym whiche edwarde perſued theim many time coulde neuer try wyth becauſe thei wer ſo diſparſed foren wilde people returned backe ſuſpectinge earle kyldare occaſion attached counſayl erle euel willers brought priſoner england wher arained certain matter treaſon laied charge aduoided thē clerly quite ſelfe whome kynge dimiſſed ſente hym irelande bee gouernour captayne ouer theim kyng beeyng oute feare battayle dyd take hys progreſſe ſhyre recreate ſpirites ſolace ſelfe mother lady margarete wyfe counteſſe earle darby yet ye king thus delityng hym ſelfe perken warbecke could moderate rule hym ſelfe although ſo manye ſuffered put execucion miſchife proue chaunce battel gathered great armye men aſwell priſoners ſlaues ſānctuary men came kent becauſe wind ſo ſerued ther cauſed certayne land enquire yf ye kentiſh men would bear whō kentiſh mē working guile promiſed ye thei would aſſiſt yf cō panie would land ther albeit ſame perkē fearing ye thei meaned falſhode craft would deſcende ſelfe cauſed certain ſouldiours lande whiche perſones beynge pretye way ſhippes wer ſore beatē put flight many theim taken priſoners wer condempned dye wherfore perkē failing purpoſe fled backe flaunders conſulted frendes vntyll ſuche time better prepared bothe men counſayle kynge herynge hys enemyes made ētraūce realme left progreſſe purpoſed go london beynge certified next day wel thei ſped continued went forth progreſſe ſendyng theim richard gilford geue thankes promiſe good turne herafter ye good ſeruice thei done thoſe tumultes aſſaultes enemy alſo thei might haue acceſſe herafter thoſe party king commaū ded ye lordes bee defēded ſtrōgely wt bulwarkes ſure munimētes fortreſſes whiche ſame perken beyng certified haſtened ye renue battaill againſt kyng yt might haue longer ſpace delaye dooe theſe thynges defence realme ſo came irelande armie tariyng ſpace ſailed scotlande ayde ſuccour kyng iames truſtyng finde grace hand ſpake maner thinke vnknowē moſte noble kyng ruine ſtocke edwarde fourth name late whiche dooe know pleaſe grace ſo take ſoonne power god preſerued liue houre mightie hand tiranne father died apointed brother richard duke glouceſtre bee gouernour ꝓtectour albeit rather deſtroyer progenie mainteiner wyllyng kyng hymſelf depriue v right title commaunded ſhould bothe bee ſlain diſpatched worlde therfore hauyng full power ordre v cauſe brother bee deſtroyed becauſe yt might bee without ſome parte offenſe ſhewe hymſelf tirāne cauſed bee conueighed ſome ſtraunge foren countree bee deſolate comforte helpe ſo kyng richard hold croūe diſpatchyng away v two ſo could tell reaſon tendre age vntill late myne aunte ladie margarete beyng flaūders ſhewe ſhe ſeen entent might recouer father poſſeſſions ſhe hath geuen power bonde mēne wyllyng ye ſhould deſire helpe externe nacions countrees ſo come ſuccoure whō reported helpe tymes euery manne right caſe bee ſhall finde fauorable ſhall binde myne neuer thynke ourſelfes hable make amendes thus ſaied kyng promiſed hym ſhould neuer repente hym commyng hym bad take good hearte kyng aſſemblyng counſaill together aſked thei thought beſt matter whether deliberacion ſhould bee takē ſome theim w • ſeſt aunſwered foliſhenes go fur 〈…〉 ſuche matter conſideryng painted feigned duke right england alſo ſaied diuerſe cauſes moſte profitable cōmen wealth partely parkyn matter goo well forwarde would rewarde theim thei would deſire enriche realme moſte plentefully liberalite partely alſo henry kyng perceiuyng kyng aſſiſt hym would gladly paie tribute hym peace concord bee counſaill gyuen kyng gladly folowe loue might bee apparent people cauſed ladie katherine doughter therle hūtley nigh kinſemā maried hym dooen kyng willyng yt perkyn ſhould reigne englāde haſtened iourney towarde border cōmyng proclamed openly ye ſhould bee pardoned ye would beare duke yorke fight quarell mēne might feare ſubmitte theim ſelfes thei burned ſpoyled killed wt mercie ferre thei go kyng perceiuyng yt engliſhemen came aide young duke ſouldiours wer ſo loden wt praies ſpoiles yt thei would gladly go returned backe scotlād cariyng wt hym infinite goodes rich duke came scotlande conſideryng greate diſtruccion loſſe engliſhmen none came aide hym entēt iuglyng countrefeict dignite might perceiued ſaied verie craftely loude voice oh wretch ſtonie hearte moued loſſe death ſo many engliſhemen myne woorde deſired kyng yt would moleſtate realme herafter ſuche cruel tormentyng fieryng kyng ſhaped hym aunſwere right ſhortely truely ſir thynke take charge thought mannes realme owne becauſe coulde ſe manne woulde take parte helpe power whē laſt emong theim cauſe ye kyng litle eſteme hym tyme countyng hym incōſtant vnſtable ſpeakyng woordes agreyng promiſe ye engliſh lordes captaines hearde buſines thei wer greate feare fled ſafegade life euery manne caſtell holde gatheryng axmie withſtand enemy certified kyng poſt haſte scottes enterpriſe whiche hearyng prepared armie haſt fight againſt theim scottes beyng lodē praies ſpoiles thei gone backe countre ere engliſhe menne could bee readie firſt commocion buſines scottes againſt engliſhemen scottes thus gone kyng certified thought ſuffer theim lenger leſte long tariyng deferryng ye matter thei ſhould take heart ſo fearſenes inuade realme aſſemblyng counſaill together ſhewed theim proffite publique weale warre againſt enemy thei agreed right gladly mainteinyng battaill leuyed certain ſumme tribute paid euery mannes hed whiche paiment although eaſie ſmall yet many commen people grudged paie parliament alſo conuocacion certain lawes actes ſtatutes confirmed made thought moſte expediēt publique weale dooen kyng prepared fight haſte gatheryng armie made giles dabeney graund capitain ouer theim goyng scotlande beganne ſodenly ciuile battaill realme whiche paiment money ye corniſhemen whiche made inſurreccion beeyng poore could well paie tribute ſo gatheryng together one michael ioſeph smyth thomas flāmoke take blacke smyth vpon theim gouernaunce compainie ſeyng theim greued ſore ſhould paye ſo muche incenſe theyr myndes againſte prynce albeit layde faulte cauſe exaction ihon mortō biſhoppe cātorbury ruigenald braye becauſe chief kynges houſe thus preparyng theim ſelues warre whē aſwell ſufficiente viandrye thynges ready tooke theyr iourney welles thence entended go london kyng ſhewed auditours wer vp lorde twychet lorde audely nobylitee taken partes thought fyrſte ſcoure realme ſuche rebelles traytours ere would fight againſt scottes therfore cauſed giles dabeney returne backe agayn goyng vpon scottes whoſe armye encreaſed multiplyed many pycked freſhe warryers might better leſſe laboure ouercome theſe rebelles alſo leaſt scottes might nowe hauyng good oportunite inuade realme time ciuile battyle cauſed lorde thomas erle surrey puiſſaunt moſt redoubted warryer whome iames cromer ihon peche iohn darel henry wyat rychard haulte ihon fogge ready withſtande theyr power cauſe people beare trewe heartes theyr kynge whiche many cornyſhe men faynted leſſe mynde fight feare fled priuely nyght compaignie captaynes perceauyng coulde haue helpe theyr handes truſted theyr owne power brought theim blackeheath feld nigh london pytched theyr tentes playn byd battail kyng would mete theim el inuade cytie whome kynge perceauyng readye fight cauſed henry burſchere erle eſſex edmunde polam erle suffolke richard thomas three noble warryers beſiege theim ſydes wyth two wynges ſo came hym ſelf myddeſt ſendyng giles dabeney greate power commyng thus felde bothe erles richard thomas ſette vpon theim violently firſt brunt put theim flight killed aboute two thouſande reſ • ſied tooke priſoners could bee told emonges theim ye captaynes ſhortely wer put death michael ioſeph mā ſuche ſtoute courage valiaūtneſſe yt neuer fainted gaue backe vntyll ſuch tyme ſtryken downe kylled openly battaile ended kynge loſte thre hundreth compaignye wer kylled preſente alſo pryſoners taken pardoned ſauyng captaynes firſt autours miſchief whoſe quarter would haue bee put ſtakes ſet dyuerſe place cornewell theyr naughtie dooynges fooliſhe entrepryſes might bee document hereafter beware becauſe many coūtree would gladly haue renewed battaile yf might haue ſome capitayn yt wer nothyng abaſhed ye ouerthrowe theyr late inſurreccion turned mynd ſo yt thei wer thither quarter ſet vpō ſtakes whē buſines hād ye kyng scottes certified certain ſpies thought beſt inuade englande againe burned waye leſt kyng ſhould prouoke hym force becauſe dooen ſo muche hurte thus came durham burned aboute entending alſo wynne norham caſtle whiche biſhoppe furniſhed litle menne vitaile ſufficiently ſo coulde haue none acceſſe caſtell biſhop foxe biſhop exeter godlines verteouſe liuing made biſhoppe welles bathe whiche biſhop nowe buſineſſe certified kyng haſte alſo therle surrey yorke ſhyre greate army menne whome erle came ſhortly compaignye hym folowed noble menne quarter euery one bringīg habilitee many could aide biſhop fight defence quarell theyr kyng compaygnie many greate power beſeging forenamed caſtell whiche coulde meanes ouercome fledde ſtreighte backe scotlande whome earle folowed longe vyttailles ſerued returned backe durham theyr abiding vntyll ſuch time knewe furder kynges pleaſure meane ſpace one henrye hailes ſente ambaſſadoure frome ferdinand vnto kyng scottes generall peace bee hym kyng englande loued hym well kyng henrye alſo whoſe ſoonne younge prynce arthure woulde haue geuen doughter ladye katheryne mariage affinytee kyndered blood loue might continue euer henrye entreated hartelye king scottes peace ſome hope wrote vnto kyng englande would pleaſe hym ſende one noble helpe conclude matter hym scottes kyng becauſe greate trouble veraye deſierous peace ſent byſhoppe durham hym haſte henrye biſhop reaſoned scottyſhe ambaſſadours concernyng peace albeit thei could agree becauſe kyng henrye deſiered haue perkyn warbecke cauſe buſynes ſo greatly diſquieted realme whome kyng woulde delyuer although might ryghte conſideryng falſehode deceyte vſed hym therfore reaſoned much matter could bring ende yet truce taken certain yeres condicion ſame perkin warbecke ſhould bee conueyghed oute scotland tary longer whyle dooinge kyng henry cauſed ambaſſadours ye frenche kyng bee brought hym ſhewed wer ſtopped douer iourney vntill ſuche tyme yt inſurreccion eorniſh men ceaſſed hearing yt came peace league bee made graūted theim right gladly yt nowe beīg reconciled wt ii kynges theſame neighbour thanked fernand wife elizabeth ye cauſed peace bee made betwixte hym scottes rewarded ambaſſadoure moſte worthely princely maner tyme vnitee concorde made yere oure lorde thouſande foure hundreth foure ſcore eighten ye xii yere kyng henry reigne kynge scottes kepte promeſſe xii pere hē ry vii well ynoughe perceiued manifeſtly deluded called vnto hym perkin warbeck firſt declared benefites pleaſures dooen vnto hym counſailed hym gette hym vnto ſome place mighte byde ſafegarde come againe another time ſhoulde haue oportunitee neuer looke helpe hād partely becauſe made peace kyng englande partely becauſe ſawe engliſhemen came take parte wherfore deſired hym bee miſgreued thus leaue hym alſo counſailed hym goo ſome place regyon wherfore perkin veraye ſorye kyng counſailed hym departed thence wife went ireland determining hym ſelfe might haue helpe menne cornewale retourne thence faſte myghte bee home greate mailres aunte margaret flaundres ſoner come thither heard diuers meſſengers yt cornewale ready fyght againſt kyng henry euer wer hoope whiche went ſtreyght cornewall dyd ſturre vp heartes gyftes promyſes immediatelye called capitain ſaied thei woulde folow hym thinges obey promptly hys commaundementes thē perkē good hoope euer becauſe would nothynge raſhelye withoute aduiſemente purpoſed fyrſte ouercome citees wel defēded place lay way ſo get many coulde folowe hym take part incontinently buckle ye kynges hoſt whē thus deliberate wēt ſtreight exeter next citee coulde come vnto beſieged becauſe gunnes breake downe walles laboured myght bee breake gate ſaw thei could eaſely betten downe thyng ſtreight ſet fyre theim whereof citezins veray ſore afraied priuely night let downe diuerſe ouer ye walles rope go certifie kyng trouble meane tyme whē thei ſaw enemy almoſt brēt vp gate one ſide tooke great blockes ſet fyre ſide none cauſe aſwell enemyes therby might excluded thei ſelfes included thei truſting made alſo wtin great ditch thī ge defend thē inuaſiō rebelles perkē ſaw got ladder would meanes haue come citee came ſo ſone vp thei beate downe meanes many ſlayne þet would thence depart truſted ſurely laſte thei ſhould glad yelde theim ſelfes al wer within lack viandrie ſone kyng hearde haſted hooſt toward exeter faſte poſſible ſente dyuerſe ſouldiours beefore certifie menne commyng preparaunce tyme ſet forth helpe theym exeter thomas trencherd william corteney walter cortney edmond carre ihon halemel peter eggecomb thomas fulford ihō crook william saintmaur great hoſt whoſe capitain edward corteny erle denſhire ſonne william whiche young man mooſte noble courage whiche thyng peter heard tell left beſiegyng exeter went ye nexte towne whiche called taūtun vieued hooſt ſet aray redye fyght howbeit lytle affiaunce ſame becauſe many ſouldiours ſo ſlenderly harneiſſed better ſkylled warre kyng ſawe gone taūtun haſted thither ſpede thether came alſo edward ye duke buckingham young mā veray valiaunt luſtie courage hym folowed greate compaignye noble men giles brigge alexander brayhā moryſhe barkeley robert tame ihon sapcot ihon wadhā hugh lutrel nycholas hys ſonne william • orton thomas lynde ihon semar wylliam norris thomas blunt ihon guyſe roberte poynte harry vernon ihon mortimer ihon speke rychard beaucāp fraunces chenie roger tokete roger wenburg henry roger edwarde darell ihon langforde richard lacon thomas tremaile edwarde sutton amis paulet ihon byknell wyllyam sayntemaur thomas longe nycholas latimer ihon turbaruyll wylliam martyne walter hungorforde moryſhe baron rycharde corbet thomas cornuall many beſydes theſe king came nygh towne ſente begynne battayle roberte broke lorde rycharde thomas giles dabeney great ſtronge hooſt entent hym ſelfe ſouldiours myght ſet vpon behynd deuiſe purpoſe kyng al ſuperfluous perkin ſo ſone eſpyed kyng redie fight fledde priuely nyght ſanctuary bellylo abbey lurked whether perkē ſo dyd feare leaſt men ſhould forſake hym timeditie hym ſelfe much vncertayne probable ſure kyng tooke hys flyght greate commoditee corneſhe menne ſurelye purpoſed eyther wynne ouercome theyr enemy elles one theim haue lyued anye daye lenger kynge henrye knewe perkin gone ſente hym many horſe menne yf myghte bee ſhoulde ouertake hym hys iourney brynge hym backe perkyn warbecke made ſuche ſpede ſeene came sanctuarie petie capitaines coulde ſcape ſo clene theim mooſt part ta ken brought backe againe kyng reſidue ſouldiours thei vnderſtode ye perkyn chief capitain fled ye taken gaue vp theim ſelfes king without buſines hym moſt gently wer forgeuen dooen kynge went ereter gaue great thankes ſuch wer worthy puniſhed authoures ſturrers vp inſurrection mooſt ſtraitlye ye meane tyme many ſouldiours road ſ mighels mounte chaunce found katherin perking wife brought ſtreight like bond woman captiue kyng kyng ſent accompanied goodly ſort matron becauſe ſhe ſo goodly young woman london quene true ſure token vyctorie while taried exeter ſuppoſyng ſelfe could haue perfect victory vntyl gottē perkin ſelf beginner ſedicion ſtrife ſent forth two company menne beſiege ſanctuarye wher perkin meanes myght ſcape away ſent worde alſo certain truſtie meſſengers yf would humblie ſubmit ſelfe ſhould forgeuen committed wherfore perkin ſeynge ponderynge ſtate miſerie wēt voluntarily ſanctuary commytted hym ſelfe kynges pleaſure kyng weray glad toke iourney immediatly towarde london without great metyng people whych came euery quarter ſe feloe monſtre becauſe beyng aliente durſt bee ſo bold come ſo noble realme make battaill delude noble menne ſuche faſſion whē kyng come london appointed certain menne kepe hym bothe night daie verie vigilantly thentent might neither conueigh hymſelf lande ner goo whether within realme make like perturbacion diſquietnes kyng perceiuyng ye many well somerſet deuēſhire whiche helper rebelles greatly bothe goyng foorth commyng homeward thought good puniſhe theim alſo leaſt peraduenture thei might ye bold dooe like thyng therfore committed buſines amis paulet knight robert sherburne deane poules dooen ſerchyng ſuche thoroweout bothe ſhires wer verie exacte diligent thei wer fauorable al ſuch feare compulſion yet thei none ſo fauorable thei thought defaultes indifferently puniſhed equitie therin verie well executed ſame yere ſmall matter befell greate ſtrife betwene kyng henry iames kyng scotlande whiche ſtrife beganne faſſion certain younge menne ye scottes came armed vnto dureſme caſtell beheld wonderous circumſpectly though thei deſierous know dooen whē kepers caſtle could perceaue yt thei went aboute hurte diſpleaſure ſeing theim go awaie owne accorde thei made woordes let theim alone thei came nexte daie vieued likewiſe kepers ye ſaid caſtel demaunded theim intent thei aūſwered theim like rude vnmanerlie ientlemenne frowardly could bee thought ſo muche yt laſte muche altercacion bothe party thei fell together eares ſome scottes ſlain reſidue put flight whē thei came home certified kyng theſame wherwith beyng ſore moued angre ſēt woorde kyng henry would wtout doubt reuenge querell wherfore kyng hēry verie ſorie ſo much forfeare liue quietnes peace age made aūſwere yt doē default coūſaill rather raſheneſſe ſubiectes whiche thei could bee ꝓued guiltie ſhould accordyng faulte puniſhed wherfore deſired moſte louingly cōtēted hable mitigate ſwage scottes angre outrageouſneſſe whiche cauſe richard biſhop dureſme whiche heuie becauſe ſeruūates ye beginner diſcord wrote many letter kyng iames deſire hym kepe peace bee quiet whiche letter kynges rage ſo quenched yt bothe ſent verie kynd letter hym deſired hym hartely come ouer talke hym ye whiche tydynges biſhop verie glad went ſtreight kyng henry ſhewe hym matter leaue hym incontinenly go ouer hym came scotlāde receiued louyngly coulde bee thought kyng hymſelf abbey called melroſe complained muche crueltie vſed toward menne englāde beganne commen ſecretly matter eſpecially amitie betwene kyng henry hym whiche bee euer ſtabliſhed confirmed deſired yt kinges doughter margaret mariage whiche thyng albeit biſhop glad heart yet would make perfect aunſwere ſheweforth ſure hope ye ſame ſaied came home would dooe beſt matter laie hym wherfore kyng ſhortly dimiſſed hym deſired hym erneſtly breake ye ſame matter kyng hēry whē come home ſo ye proffer pleaſed ye kyng verie well becauſe manne whiche alwaies delited wt peace quietnes wt troubleſomneſſe battaill approch ye death perkin warbeck edwarde erle warwicke whiche ſo long lyen readie tower perkē thought would ſaue hymſelf therfore tyme tooke leggues ranne awaie ſo ſone kyng harde tell therof made menne hym ſpede ye might bee wt whoſe clamour ſhoutes perkyn ſo feared yt neceſſitie compelled go abbaie called bethelē ther intreacted ye abbot place deſire kyng pardon might dye whiche thyng abbot hym obteined wherfore perken brought bounde feitered weſtminſter ſtoode whole daie ſight menne great ſhame reproche hym ſelf partely becauſe kyng promiſed hym life partely becauſe ſhould renne awaie cōmitted ye towre wickednes boylong ſo hote within breit would ſuffre hym eſcape vēgeaūce puniſhemēt god ſhortly moſte iuſtly worthely put deathe herafter ſhalbe ſhewed chaunſed ye monke whoſe name patricke ſcholer whome promiſed would folowe counſaill ſhould eaſely come kyngdome englande whiche ſcholer one heard maiſters mynd verie inſtaunte matter deſired maiſter forget purpoſe rather begynne ſone poſſible wherfore thei twene theim ſelfes taken deliberacion counſailled thyng ſhould brought paſſe thei went bothe together kent beganne young feloe tell priuely many erle warwicke gotte tower helpe monke whiche perceiued credence geuen declared openly deſyred al men helpe euer ſedicion beganne goo foreward heddes principalles theſame wer taken caſle pryſone whiche one condempned death condēpned perpetuall pryſon darkeneſſe tyme englande ſo muche attrybuted preſtes al religious mē though committed felonie murder yea treaſon ſhould haue bene therfore condempned death moreouer whoſoeuer could reade though wer neuer ſo lytle crime ſoeuer committed ſaue treaſon ſhould booke bee ſaued therfore inuented default wer ſo great another manne ſhoulde ſuffer death theſame ſhould onely burnt hande wherfore ye committed thefte ſhould bee marked hand letter committed murdre yf deprehended lyke cryme ſhould fauour menne bee ſhewed whiche acte made confyrmed kyng henry ſecond yere reigne takē frenchemen whiche wonte thei take ſuche cutte one care let hym go whiche priuiledges bookes made thefes bolde plentie thorowe coaſtes party realme englande nowe matier perkyn ſpake muche whyles ye towre corrupted many kepers partly giftes partely fayre promyſes ſo agreed ſaue leuetenaunt whome fully determined kyll erle warwike ſhould gooe theyr waye toure afterwarde make beſt ſhyfte could theim ſelfes purpoſe came full effecte knowne within ſhorte tyme whiche felowes ſame counſayle hanged neckes earle warwike becauſe foundegyltie theſame defaulte behedded whiche dooen yeare oure lorde thouſand foure hundreth xcix xiii yeare kyng henry reigne nexte yere englande 〈…〉 〈◊〉 greate plague wherof menne died many place vereye ſore eſpeciallye mooſte london died yere aboue thyrtye thouſande wherfore kynge ſayled ouer caleis taryed greate beyng came ouer hym philippe erle flaunders receaued hym louyngly could bee thought alſo euer departed league whiche made betwene theim two longe renewed sone plague ſlaked kyng returned agayne englande ſoner come thyther met one gaſper pons ſente alexander byſhoppe roome brought hym indulgence perdo • e whereby made kyng beleue ſhould flye ſtreight heauen thoſe could bee graunted withoute greate ſomme money whiche rather might obteyne promyſed parte kyng hymſelfe ſo deceauyng ye kyng ye people ſame yere burnt place ye kynges whiche buylded vp againe named richemount aboute tyme died three biſhoppes england ihon morton biſhop cantourbury thomas langton biſhop wyncheſter thomas rotherham biſhoppe yorke alſo yere greate maryages made kyng henry geuen doughter ladye margarete kyng scottes ſonne prince arthur ladie katherine doughter ferdinande kyng spayne whiche mariages made ſpecially cauſe might liue peace thoſe kynges olde age prynce arthure came londō purpoſely bee maryed went wale agayne lady wife ouerſee thynges well entente might miſcarye go waie rulyng domimon hym many noble mē firſt richard poole nighe kynſman paſſeporte licēce kyng quene margarete aunte returned ſo excuſed hymſelfe kynge founde fautles thyng yt obiected vnto hym alſo mariage kepte london great pompe ſolēnitee edmunde fled flaunders wt brother richard either yt great charge theſame mariage ſo farre caſt debte hable paye either becauſe ye quene margarete aunte allured hym orels eiuill enuie kyng ſhould proſper ſo well whē knowen yt gooen kyng certified feared yt ſome buſynes ſhould ryſe meanes ſory yt pardoned hym offēce lately cōmitted ſone yt erle came flaunders ſyr robert curſone knight capitaine hāmes caſtel feignyng hym ſelfe bee one conſpiracye wente purpoſely eſpye quene entended againſt kyng henrye whyche afterwarde ſo doynge greate fauoure wyth hym kynge ſo vigylaunte circumſpecte matter dyd knowe theim namelye either bare hym eiuill woorked theyr mynde cauſed bee attached caſte holde emong theim wyllyam erle deuonſhyres ſonne whiche maried ladie catheryne daughter kyng edward taken another wyllyam brother edmonde earle souffolke iames tyrell ihon wyndham theſe two wylliams taken rather ſuſpection offence gyltines wherefore wylliam earles ſonne deuonſhyre death kynge henrye deliuered great fauour wyth kinges ſonne henrye eyght ſhortly whan beganne exercyſe hym ſelfe agayne marciall feates warre ſickened dyſeaſe called plureſes died therewith whyche becauſe ſtraunge vnknowen phiſiciās incurable lefte one ſonne behynde hym alyue vphold name auncetree wyllyam brother edmunde earle suffolke alſo greater fauoure ſhowed hym pryſon iames terel ihō wyndham becauſe traytours manifeſtly accuſed ſame wer put death behedded earle suffolke heard thys great deſpayre wyth hym ſelfe ſhould neuer frame hys matter wel ſo wente aboute germanye fraunce ayde ſocour prouyng yf coulde fynde helpe handes yt would oppreſſe thē wrong people hated oppreſſours therfore deuiſed hym ſelfe honeſte meane might thus deuiſing called minde yt engliſh mē dyd litle paſſe vpō obſeruaciō lawes yt made ſo much ye yf ſuch thynge ſhould called accompte thoughte manye men well lordes lay fee would bee founde fautie ſo ſearchyng ouer ſtatutes made puniſhed lytle purſſe tranſgreſſed theim appoynted two commyſſioners receaue forfeictes one richarde hempſon edmunde dudley booth lawers temporaltee whiche perſonnes deſire pleaſe king reſpect thei got monye ſo thei myght haue ether ryght wrong albeit ye yere lord ccccc fyue thys earle hauyng nauye prepared ſayled flaunders wyfe spayne ſet forth longe ere wether beganne chaunge tempeſtes ryſe ſo laſt fearſenes wynde dyd dryue coaſtes border englande wher landed hauē porte called wynmouth ſore againſte mynd conſent companie knewe well ſame landyng ſhould bee occaſion long tariyng kno • n thus landed came agreate nomber harniſſed men proue yf kynges frende whiche thei perſeaued hym bee frende entended nothing loue frendeſhippe thomas trencharde chiefe compaignie went kyng deſyring hym yf would witeſalfe hym take lodging houſe whiche euen nigh hand truſting therby haue thāke ye kynges maſter certifyed al haſte commyng alſo iohn caroe deſired hym woulde gooe vntyll ſuche tyme ſpoken wt kyng louing feithfull frende conſideringe within two thre dayes iourney hym length although layde many excuſes haue gooen departed inſtance taried theim ye kyng enfourmed cōminge reioyced highly ſente certaine nobilitee bring hym wherfore erle ſeing remedy yt muſt nedes tary went ſtreight windeſore kyng dyd lye ſhortlye folowed wife quene iohan two cōmoned many thinges together laſte beganne treate league perpetuall amitee bee firſte kynge henrye deſired haue edmonde poole baniſhed man vnder captiuitee bondage whome earle aunſwered ſaied power reſtore hym yet muche entreating praiyng kyng graunted laſte ſhoulde hee ſente hym righte ſhortly thus prolonginge time yt might haue deſyre brought philyp earle london ſhewing hym citie retourned frome thence hym edmonde poole ſeyng hope bee foren prince truſting kyng henry would put hym libertee came englande willingly proue gentlenes yf vpon expectacyon hope deceiued yet might laſte dye buryed natiue countree weare receyued garment ſend baltheſar caſtillio mantuan borne vnto kyng
